# O3DESharp 1.2.0 Implementation Plan

> **For agentic workers:** REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development (recommended) or superpowers:executing-plans to implement this plan task-by-task. Steps use checkbox (`- [ ]`) syntax for tracking.

**Goal:** Ship O3DESharp v1.2.0 - a UX/UI and performance-focused release covering 19 approved audit findings (plus their supporting test/CI scaffolding), then bump the version, write release notes, and gate on maintainer confirmation before tagging/merging/pushing.

**Architecture:** No architectural changes. This is a punch-list release: 24 mostly-independent tasks across O3DE.Core's C# math/API layer, the native Coral host and reflection dispatch path, the Editor's C++/Python tooling, the ClangSharp binding generator, and documentation. Task 0 scaffolds a new xUnit test project (`O3DE.Core.Tests`) that several C# tasks depend on; Task 1 (the critical `LookRotation` fix) and Tasks 22-24 (release mechanics) bookend the work. Everything else is independent and can be executed in any order or in parallel by different engineers. Explicitly out of scope: any change to `GenericDispatcher`'s BehaviorContext dispatch internals (reserved for the maintainer's 1.3 refactor) and the FirstPersonController work on `feat/fpc-port-m1`.

**Tech Stack:** C++ (AZCore/O3DE conventions, CMake), C# (.NET 9.0 for O3DE.Core, .NET 8.0->9.0 for the binding generator, xUnit + FluentAssertions for tests), Python (PySide/Qt editor tooling, pytest for tests), TeamCity Kotlin DSL for CI.

Full audit findings and rationale: `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-01-1.2.0-ux-perf-audit-design.md`.

---

### Task 0: Scaffold O3DE.Core.Tests xUnit project

**Files:**
- Create: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj`
- Create: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/InternalCallsStub.cs`
- Modify: `O3DESharp.sln`
- Modify: `.teamcity/settings.kts`

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the test project directory and csproj**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj`:

```xml
<Project Sdk="Microsoft.NET.Sdk">

  <PropertyGroup>
    <TargetFramework>net9.0</TargetFramework>
    <ImplicitUsings>enable</ImplicitUsings>
    <Nullable>enable</Nullable>
    <AllowUnsafeBlocks>true</AllowUnsafeBlocks>
    <IsPackable>false</IsPackable>
    <IsTestProject>true</IsTestProject>
    <RootNamespace>O3DE.Core.Tests</RootNamespace>
  </PropertyGroup>

  <ItemGroup>
    <PackageReference Include="coverlet.collector" Version="6.0.0">
      <IncludeAssets>runtime; build; native; contentfiles; analyzers; buildtransitive</IncludeAssets>
      <PrivateAssets>all</PrivateAssets>
    </PackageReference>
    <PackageReference Include="FluentAssertions" Version="6.12.0" />
    <PackageReference Include="Microsoft.NET.Test.Sdk" Version="17.8.0" />
    <PackageReference Include="xunit" Version="2.6.2" />
    <PackageReference Include="xunit.runner.visualstudio" Version="2.5.4">
      <IncludeAssets>runtime; build; native; contentfiles; analyzers; buildtransitive</IncludeAssets>
      <PrivateAssets>all</PrivateAssets>
    </PackageReference>
  </ItemGroup>

  <!--
    O3DE.Core.dll can't be referenced directly: its csproj requires
    bin/Coral/Coral.Managed.dll (a native-build artifact not present on a
    bare CI checkout), and several of its types call through InternalCalls'
    unmanaged function pointers that Coral only populates at runtime. We
    compile the pure-managed math/logic files under test directly instead,
    matching the pattern BindingGenerator.Tests already uses for
    ExposedProperty.cs.
  -->
  <ItemGroup>
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Vector2.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Vector2.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Vector3.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Vector3.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Quaternion.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Quaternion.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Debug.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Debug.cs" />
  </ItemGroup>

  <ItemGroup>
    <Using Include="Xunit" />
    <Using Include="FluentAssertions" />
  </ItemGroup>

</Project>
```

Note: files physically created inside `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/` (like the stub below) are auto-included by the SDK-style project's default globbing — do not add explicit `<Compile Include>` entries for them, only for the linked files living outside this project's own directory tree (matching the existing comment in `O3DE.Core.csproj`: "Do NOT add explicit <Compile Include=...> - this causes NETSDK1022 duplicate errors").

- [ ] **Step 2: Add the InternalCalls stub**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/InternalCallsStub.cs`:

```csharp
using System.Collections.Generic;

namespace O3DE
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Test-only replacement for O3DE.Core's InternalCalls. The real
    /// InternalCalls is an internal static unsafe class holding
    /// delegate* unmanaged function pointers that Coral only populates
    /// when hosting a live .NET runtime inside the O3DE process -
    /// invoking one outside that host is a hard native crash, not a
    /// catchable exception. This stub defines a same-named type with
    /// ordinary managed methods instead, so Debug.cs / Debugger.cs bind
    /// to it when compiled into this test assembly (the real
    /// InternalCalls.cs from O3DE.Core is never linked in here).
    /// </summary>
    internal static class InternalCalls
    {
        public static readonly List<string> InfoLogs = new();
        public static readonly List<string> WarningLogs = new();
        public static readonly List<string> ErrorLogs = new();

        public static void Reset()
        {
            InfoLogs.Clear();
            WarningLogs.Clear();
            ErrorLogs.Clear();
        }

        public static void Log_Info(string message) => InfoLogs.Add(message);
        public static void Log_Warning(string message) => WarningLogs.Add(message);
        public static void Log_Error(string message) => ErrorLogs.Add(message);
    }
}
```

```
EndProject
```

In the `GlobalSection(ProjectConfigurationPlatforms)` block, after the O3DE.Core entries (after the line `{1F4FBB80-321E-1C5A-93DC-B45FE163C6C6}.Release|Any CPU.Build.0 = Release|Any CPU`), insert:

```
		{D4E5F6A7-8B9C-4D5E-9F0A-1B2C3D4E5F60}.Debug|Any CPU.ActiveCfg = Debug|Any CPU
		{D4E5F6A7-8B9C-4D5E-9F0A-1B2C3D4E5F60}.Debug|Any CPU.Build.0 = Debug|Any CPU
		{D4E5F6A7-8B9C-4D5E-9F0A-1B2C3D4E5F60}.Release|Any CPU.ActiveCfg = Release|Any CPU
		{D4E5F6A7-8B9C-4D5E-9F0A-1B2C3D4E5F60}.Release|Any CPU.Build.0 = Release|Any CPU
```

In the `GlobalSection(NestedProjects)` block, after the line `{1F4FBB80-321E-1C5A-93DC-B45FE163C6C6} = {FFA1169A-26DF-0A8A-0AC2-DBE3A54F0F65}`, insert (nests the new project under the same "Scripts" solution folder as O3DE.Core):

```
		{D4E5F6A7-8B9C-4D5E-9F0A-1B2C3D4E5F60} = {FFA1169A-26DF-0A8A-0AC2-DBE3A54F0F65}
```

Note: `BindingGenerator.Tests`, `SourceGenerators`, and `SourceGenerators.Tests` are NOT currently registered in this .sln either (CI calls `dotnet build`/`dotnet test` directly against csproj paths, not through the .sln) — this step is for IDE convenience/consistency, not a CI dependency.

### Task 1: Fix Quaternion.LookRotation conjugate-rotation bug

**Files:**
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs:286-330`
- Test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/QuaternionTests.cs` (new)

**Root cause (verified by hand, not just by the audit agent):** `LookRotation` builds a rotation matrix `M` with columns `(right, forward, up)` in `m00..m22` (this part is correct - matches `RotatePoint`'s row/column convention, and `column1 = M*e_y = forward`, which is what we want since local +Y is `Vector3.Forward`). But the Shepperd trace-based matrix-to-quaternion conversion that follows has every off-diagonal antisymmetric term's subtraction order flipped relative to the standard formula (verified by deriving the standard formula from `RotatePoint`'s own matrix layout and comparing term-by-term against all four branches). The net effect: the function returns the CONJUGATE of the correct quaternion in every branch (in the `trace > 0` branch this is literal - x/y/z are negated, w matches; in the other three branches, only the w-component's sign is flipped relative to standard, which - because a quaternion and its negation represent the same rotation - is equivalent to the conjugate up to an inconsequential global sign). Conjugate = inverse for a unit quaternion, so `RotatePoint` using the returned quaternion applies the INVERSE of the intended rotation. This confirms the audit's "returns backwards-facing rotations" finding is real, not a false positive.

- [ ] **Step 1: Write the failing test**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/QuaternionTests.cs`:

```csharp
namespace O3DE.Core.Tests.Math;

public class QuaternionTests
{
    [Theory]
    [InlineData(1f, 0f, 0f)]   // Right
    [InlineData(-1f, 0f, 0f)]  // Left
    [InlineData(0f, 0f, 1f)]   // Up
    [InlineData(0f, 0f, -1f)]  // Down
    [InlineData(1f, 1f, 0f)]   // diagonal, forward-right
    [InlineData(1f, 1f, 1f)]   // diagonal, forward-right-up
    [InlineData(-1f, 1f, 0.5f)] // arbitrary non-axis-aligned direction
    public void LookRotation_RotatesLocalForwardToTargetDirection(float x, float y, float z)
    {
        var dir = new Vector3(x, y, z).Normalized;

        var rotation = Quaternion.LookRotation(dir);
        var rotatedForward = rotation.RotatePoint(Vector3.Forward);

        rotatedForward.X.Should().BeApproximately(dir.X, 1e-4f);
        rotatedForward.Y.Should().BeApproximately(dir.Y, 1e-4f);
        rotatedForward.Z.Should().BeApproximately(dir.Z, 1e-4f);
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LookRotation_Forward_IsIdentity()
    {
        var rotation = Quaternion.LookRotation(Vector3.Forward);
        var rotatedForward = rotation.RotatePoint(Vector3.Forward);

        rotatedForward.X.Should().BeApproximately(Vector3.Forward.X, 1e-4f);
        rotatedForward.Y.Should().BeApproximately(Vector3.Forward.Y, 1e-4f);
        rotatedForward.Z.Should().BeApproximately(Vector3.Forward.Z, 1e-4f);
    }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Run test to verify it fails**

Run: `dotnet test Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo --filter "QuaternionTests"`
Expected: FAIL on every non-trivial direction (e.g. `(1,1,0)`, `(1,1,1)`, `(-1,1,0.5)`) - the rotated-forward vector will point roughly opposite/sideways to `dir`, not match it within tolerance. The axis-aligned `Up`/`Down`/`Right`/`Left` cases may also fail or coincidentally pass depending on symmetry; the diagonal cases are the reliable failure signal.

- [ ] **Step 3: Fix the Shepperd conversion**

In `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs`, replace the body from `float trace = m00 + m11 + m22;` through the closing `return q.Normalized;` of `LookRotation` (current lines ~286-330) with:

```csharp
            float trace = m00 + m11 + m22;
            Quaternion q;

            if (trace > 0f)
            {
                float s = MathF.Sqrt(trace + 1f) * 2f;
                q = new Quaternion(
                    (m21 - m12) / s,
                    (m02 - m20) / s,
                    (m10 - m01) / s,
                    0.25f * s
                );
            }
            else if (m00 > m11 && m00 > m22)
            {
                float s = MathF.Sqrt(1f + m00 - m11 - m22) * 2f;
                q = new Quaternion(
                    0.25f * s,
                    (m01 + m10) / s,
                    (m02 + m20) / s,
                    (m21 - m12) / s
                );
            }
            else if (m11 > m22)
            {
                float s = MathF.Sqrt(1f + m11 - m00 - m22) * 2f;
                q = new Quaternion(
                    (m01 + m10) / s,
                    0.25f * s,
                    (m12 + m21) / s,
                    (m02 - m20) / s
                );
            }
            else
            {
                float s = MathF.Sqrt(1f + m22 - m00 - m11) * 2f;
                q = new Quaternion(
                    (m02 + m20) / s,
                    (m12 + m21) / s,
                    0.25f * s,
                    (m10 - m01) / s
                );
            }

            return q.Normalized;
```

(Only the four antisymmetric-difference terms change: `(m12-m21)`→`(m21-m12)`, `(m20-m02)`→`(m02-m20)`, `(m01-m10)`→`(m10-m01)` in the trace>0 branch's x/y/z, and the `w` term in each of the other three branches gets its subtraction order flipped to match. The symmetric-sum terms like `(m01+m10)` are unchanged since they're unaffected by this sign issue.)

Update the doc comment above `LookRotation` (currently describes the right-handed-vs-Unity-convention fix from a prior pass) to also note the Shepperd-conversion sign fix, e.g. append: `/// Note: the trace-based matrix-to-quaternion conversion below must produce the quaternion consistent with RotatePoint's own (row, column) convention - the antisymmetric off-diagonal terms are intentionally (m_ba - m_ab), not (m_ab - m_ba); flipping this sign silently produces the conjugate (inverse) rotation, which was a real shipped bug fixed in 1.2.0.`

- [ ] **Step 4: Run test to verify it passes**

Run: `dotnet test Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo --filter "QuaternionTests"`
Expected: PASS, all cases.

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the full O3DE.Core.Tests suite to check for regressions**

Run: `dotnet test Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo`
Expected: PASS (no other tests exist yet at this point in the plan besides Task 0's empty scaffold, so this should just show the new QuaternionTests passing).

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/QuaternionTests.cs
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: Quaternion.LookRotation returned the conjugate (inverted) rotation

The Shepperd trace-based matrix-to-quaternion conversion had every
antisymmetric off-diagonal term's subtraction order flipped relative
to the convention RotatePoint itself uses, so LookRotation silently
returned the inverse of the intended rotation for any non-trivial
direction - turrets, cameras, and characters facing a target all
turned backwards. Only the trivial forward=Up case was unaffected,
which is why a prior manual check missed it. Added regression tests
asserting LookRotation(dir).RotatePoint(Vector3.Forward) == dir for
several non-axis-aligned directions.
EOF
)"
```

### Task 2: Vector3/Quaternion/Vector2 Equals/GetHashCode contract violation

**Files:**
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector3.cs:344-364`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs:480-501`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector2.cs:193-212`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj`
- Create: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/EqualityTests.cs`
- Test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/EqualityTests.cs`

- [ ] **Step 1: Fix `Vector3.Equals` to use exact equality**

Current code in `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector3.cs` lines 344-364:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        public bool Equals(Vector3 other)
        {
            const float epsilon = 1e-6f;
            return MathF.Abs(X - other.X) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(Y - other.Y) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(Z - other.Z) < epsilon;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Vector3 other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y, Z);
        }

        #endregion
```

Replace with:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        /// <summary>
        /// Returns true if this vector is exactly equal to <paramref name="other"/>
        /// (bit-for-bit component comparison via <c>==</c> on each float), matching
        /// the convention used by <see cref="System.Numerics.Vector3"/>.
        /// This is NOT tolerance-based: (1e-7f, 0, 0) is not equal to (0, 0, 0)
        /// even though the difference is tiny. Some game engines use an
        /// epsilon-tolerant Equals for vectors, but that breaks the contract
        /// that equal objects must always report equal hash codes, which in
        /// turn breaks Dictionary/HashSet lookups. Callers that want
        /// tolerance-based comparison should use
        /// <c>Vector3.Distance(a, b) &lt; epsilon</c> (or compare
        /// <see cref="SqrMagnitude"/> of the difference against
        /// <c>epsilon * epsilon</c> to avoid the square root) instead of
        /// relying on <see cref="Equals(Vector3)"/> or <c>==</c>.
        /// </summary>
        public bool Equals(Vector3 other)
        {
            return X == other.X &&
                   Y == other.Y &&
                   Z == other.Z;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Vector3 other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y, Z);
        }

        #endregion
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Fix `Quaternion.Equals` to use exact equality**

Current code in `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs` lines 480-501:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        public bool Equals(Quaternion other)
        {
            const float epsilon = 1e-6f;
            return MathF.Abs(X - other.X) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(Y - other.Y) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(Z - other.Z) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(W - other.W) < epsilon;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Quaternion other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y, Z, W);
        }

        #endregion
```

Replace with:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        /// <summary>
        /// Returns true if this quaternion is exactly equal to <paramref name="other"/>
        /// (bit-for-bit component comparison via <c>==</c> on each float), matching
        /// the convention used by <see cref="System.Numerics.Quaternion"/>.
        /// This is NOT tolerance-based: two quaternions that differ by 1e-7 in a
        /// single component are not equal, even though they represent visually
        /// identical rotations. Some game engines use an epsilon-tolerant Equals,
        /// but that breaks the contract that equal objects must always report
        /// equal hash codes, which in turn breaks Dictionary/HashSet lookups.
        /// Callers that want tolerance-based comparison should use
        /// <c>Quaternion.Angle(a, b) &lt; epsilonDegrees</c> instead of relying
        /// on <see cref="Equals(Quaternion)"/> or <c>==</c>.
        /// </summary>
        public bool Equals(Quaternion other)
        {
            return X == other.X &&
                   Y == other.Y &&
                   Z == other.Z &&
                   W == other.W;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Quaternion other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y, Z, W);
        }

        #endregion
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Fix `Vector2.Equals` to use exact equality**

Current code in `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector2.cs` lines 193-212:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        public bool Equals(Vector2 other)
        {
            const float epsilon = 1e-6f;
            return MathF.Abs(X - other.X) < epsilon &&
                   MathF.Abs(Y - other.Y) < epsilon;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Vector2 other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y);
        }

        #endregion
```

Replace with:

```csharp
        #region Equality

        /// <summary>
        /// Returns true if this vector is exactly equal to <paramref name="other"/>
        /// (bit-for-bit component comparison via <c>==</c> on each float), matching
        /// the convention used by <see cref="System.Numerics.Vector2"/>.
        /// This is NOT tolerance-based: (1e-7f, 0) is not equal to (0, 0) even
        /// though the difference is tiny. Some game engines use an
        /// epsilon-tolerant Equals for vectors, but that breaks the contract
        /// that equal objects must always report equal hash codes, which in
        /// turn breaks Dictionary/HashSet lookups. Callers that want
        /// tolerance-based comparison should use
        /// <c>Vector2.Distance(a, b) &lt; epsilon</c> instead of relying on
        /// <see cref="Equals(Vector2)"/> or <c>==</c>.
        /// </summary>
        public bool Equals(Vector2 other)
        {
            return X == other.X &&
                   Y == other.Y;
        }

        public override bool Equals(object? obj)
        {
            return obj is Vector2 other && Equals(other);
        }

        public override int GetHashCode()
        {
            return HashCode.Combine(X, Y);
        }

        #endregion
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Link the three Math source files into the test project (if not already present)**

Open `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj` and check the `<ItemGroup>` containing `<Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\...">` entries. Per the plan's Task 0, `Math/Vector2.cs`, `Math/Vector3.cs`, `Math/Quaternion.cs`, `Debug.cs`, and `Debugger.cs` are already linked in. Confirm the block looks like this (adjust only if it differs from what Task 0 actually produced):

```xml
  <ItemGroup>
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Vector2.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Vector2.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Vector3.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Vector3.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Math\Quaternion.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Math\Quaternion.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Debug.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Debug.cs" />
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" />
  </ItemGroup>
```

No `<Compile Include>` changes are needed for this task since all three Math types are already linked. If for any reason `Math/Vector2.cs`, `Math/Vector3.cs`, or `Math/Quaternion.cs` is missing from that ItemGroup, add the missing line(s) using the exact pattern above before proceeding to Step 5.

- [ ] **Step 5: Write the equality contract tests**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Math/EqualityTests.cs`:

```csharp
//
// Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
// For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
//
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
//

using System.Collections.Generic;
using O3DE;

namespace O3DE.Core.Tests.Math;

/// <summary>
/// Tests for the Equals/GetHashCode/operator== contract on Vector2, Vector3,
/// and Quaternion. Prior to this fix, Equals used an epsilon tolerance while
/// GetHashCode hashed exact float bits, which violates the .NET contract
/// that "if two objects compare as equal, they must have the same hash
/// code" and silently broke Dictionary/HashSet lookups for near-equal keys.
/// The fix drops epsilon tolerance from Equals entirely (exact float
/// equality, matching System.Numerics.Vector3's convention). These tests
/// pin that behavior so a future regression back to epsilon-tolerant
/// Equals is caught immediately.
/// </summary>
public class EqualityTests
{
    private const float NearEqualDelta = 1e-7f;

    // ---- Vector3 -------------------------------------------------------

    [Fact]
    public void Vector3_ExactlyEqualInstances_AreEqual_AndHaveEqualHashCodes()
    {
        var a = new Vector3(1.5f, -2.25f, 3.0f);
        var b = new Vector3(1.5f, -2.25f, 3.0f);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a == b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a != b).Should().BeFalse();
        a.GetHashCode().Should().Be(b.GetHashCode());
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Vector3_NearEqualButNotExact_AreNotEqual()
    {
        // This is the explicit behavior change: prior to this fix these two
        // instances (differing by 1e-7 in X) would have compared Equal under
        // the old 1e-6f epsilon tolerance.
        var a = new Vector3(1.0f, 2.0f, 3.0f);
        var b = new Vector3(1.0f + NearEqualDelta, 2.0f, 3.0f);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a == b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a != b).Should().BeTrue();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Vector3_EqualInstances_UseableAsDictionaryKey()
    {
        // The actual contract this fix restores: equal instances must
        // always hash the same, so Dictionary/HashSet lookups by value work.
        var dict = new Dictionary<Vector3, string>
        {
            [new Vector3(1f, 2f, 3f)] = "hello"
        };

        dict[new Vector3(1f, 2f, 3f)].Should().Be("hello");
        dict.ContainsKey(new Vector3(1f, 2f, 3f)).Should().BeTrue();
    }

    // ---- Vector2 -------------------------------------------------------

    [Fact]
    public void Vector2_ExactlyEqualInstances_AreEqual_AndHaveEqualHashCodes()
    {
        var a = new Vector2(4.5f, -1.25f);
        var b = new Vector2(4.5f, -1.25f);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a == b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a != b).Should().BeFalse();
        a.GetHashCode().Should().Be(b.GetHashCode());
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Vector2_NearEqualButNotExact_AreNotEqual()
    {
        var a = new Vector2(1.0f, 2.0f);
        var b = new Vector2(1.0f, 2.0f + NearEqualDelta);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a == b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a != b).Should().BeTrue();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Vector2_EqualInstances_UseableAsDictionaryKey()
    {
        var dict = new Dictionary<Vector2, string>
        {
            [new Vector2(1f, 2f)] = "world"
        };

        dict[new Vector2(1f, 2f)].Should().Be("world");
        dict.ContainsKey(new Vector2(1f, 2f)).Should().BeTrue();
    }

    // ---- Quaternion ------------------------------------------------------

    [Fact]
    public void Quaternion_ExactlyEqualInstances_AreEqual_AndHaveEqualHashCodes()
    {
        var a = new Quaternion(0.1f, 0.2f, 0.3f, 0.9f);
        var b = new Quaternion(0.1f, 0.2f, 0.3f, 0.9f);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a == b).Should().BeTrue();
        (a != b).Should().BeFalse();
        a.GetHashCode().Should().Be(b.GetHashCode());
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Quaternion_NearEqualButNotExact_AreNotEqual()
    {
        var a = new Quaternion(0f, 0f, 0f, 1.0f);
        var b = new Quaternion(0f, 0f, 0f, 1.0f + NearEqualDelta);

        a.Equals(b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a == b).Should().BeFalse();
        (a != b).Should().BeTrue();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Quaternion_EqualInstances_UseableAsDictionaryKey()
    {
        var dict = new Dictionary<Quaternion, string>
        {
            [Quaternion.Identity] = "identity"
        };

        dict[Quaternion.Identity].Should().Be("identity");
        dict.ContainsKey(new Quaternion(0f, 0f, 0f, 1f)).Should().BeTrue();
    }
}
```

Note: this test file uses `Should()` (FluentAssertions) and `[Fact]` (xUnit) unqualified, relying on the project-wide `<Using Include="Xunit" />` and `<Using Include="FluentAssertions" />` global usings already present in `O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj` (mirroring `BindingGenerator.Tests.csproj`'s convention).

Expected output ends with a line similar to:


All 9 facts (3 types x 3 facts each) must pass. If `Vector3_NearEqualButNotExact_AreNotEqual` (or the Vector2/Quaternion equivalents) fails, the `Equals` edit in Step 1/2/3 was not applied correctly — re-check that the `epsilon` tolerance was fully removed and not merely tightened.

```bash
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: use exact float equality in Vector2/Vector3/Quaternion Equals

Equals previously used an epsilon tolerance while GetHashCode hashed
exact float bits, violating the .NET contract that equal objects must
report equal hash codes. This silently broke Dictionary/HashSet lookups
for near-equal keys. Equals now compares components exactly, matching
System.Numerics.Vector3's convention; callers wanting tolerance-based
comparison should use Distance(a, b) < epsilon (or Quaternion.Angle for
rotations) instead. This is a minor behavior change: values that differ
by a tiny epsilon (e.g. 1e-7) are no longer treated as equal.
EOF
)"
```

**Files:**

- [ ] **Step 1: Add a private safe-format helper and use it in all four `(string format, params object[] args)` overloads**

Current code in `F:\O3DESharp\Assets\Scripts\O3DE.Core\Debug.cs`:

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Logs a formatted informational message to the O3DE console.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="format">The format string</param>
        /// <param name="args">The format arguments</param>
        public static void Log(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Logs a formatted warning message to the O3DE console.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="format">The format string</param>
        /// <param name="args">The format arguments</param>
        public static void LogWarning(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Warning(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Logs a formatted error message to the O3DE console.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="format">The format string</param>
        /// <param name="args">The format arguments</param>
        public static void LogError(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Error(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Logs a formatted message only in debug builds.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="format">The format string</param>
        /// <param name="args">The format arguments</param>
        [Conditional("DEBUG")]
        [Conditional("O3DE_DEBUG")]
        public static void LogDebug(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info($"[DEBUG] {string.Format(format, args)}"); }
        }
```

Replace all four overloads with the versions below, and add the new `SafeFormat` private helper right after the class's opening brace (immediately before the existing `Log(string message)` method at line 26). Use `Edit` with these exact replacements:

Replacement 1 — insert the helper before `public static void Log(string message)`:

Old:
```csharp
    public static class Debug
    {
        /// <summary>
        /// Logs an informational message to the O3DE console.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="message">The message to log</param>
        public static void Log(string message)
```

New:
```csharp
    public static class Debug
    {
        /// <summary>
        /// Formats <paramref name="format"/> with <paramref name="args"/>, falling back to a
        /// diagnostic-safe string if formatting itself throws (e.g. a mismatched placeholder
        /// count, or an args value whose ToString() throws). A logging API must never throw
        /// back into caller code just because the message it was asked to log was malformed.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="format">The format string</param>
        /// <param name="args">The format arguments</param>
        private static string SafeFormat(string format, object[] args)
        {
            try
            {
                return string.Format(format, args);
            }
            catch (Exception ex)
            {
                return $"{format} [format error: {ex.Message}]";
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Logs an informational message to the O3DE console.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="message">The message to log</param>
        public static void Log(string message)
```

Replacement 2 — `Log(string format, params object[] args)`:

Old:
```csharp
        public static void Log(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

New:
```csharp
        public static void Log(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info(SafeFormat(format, args)); }
        }
```

Replacement 3 — `LogWarning(string format, params object[] args)`:

Old:
```csharp
        public static void LogWarning(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Warning(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

New:
```csharp
        public static void LogWarning(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Warning(SafeFormat(format, args)); }
        }
```

Replacement 4 — `LogError(string format, params object[] args)`:

Old:
```csharp
        public static void LogError(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Error(string.Format(format, args)); }
        }
```

New:
```csharp
        public static void LogError(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Error(SafeFormat(format, args)); }
        }
```

Replacement 5 — `LogDebug(string format, params object[] args)`:

Old:
```csharp
        public static void LogDebug(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info($"[DEBUG] {string.Format(format, args)}"); }
        }
```

New:
```csharp
        public static void LogDebug(string format, params object[] args)
        {
            unsafe { InternalCalls.Log_Info($"[DEBUG] {SafeFormat(format, args)}"); }
        }
```

Apply all five replacements to `F:\O3DESharp\Assets\Scripts\O3DE.Core\Debug.cs` using the `Edit` tool (one `Edit` call per replacement, `old_string`/`new_string` exactly as shown above).

- [ ] **Step 3: Write DebugTests.cs**

Create `F:\O3DESharp\Assets\Scripts\O3DE.Core.Tests\DebugTests.cs`:

```csharp
//
// Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
// For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
//
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
//

using O3DE;

namespace O3DESharp.Core.Tests;

/// <summary>
/// Tests for Debug.cs's format-string overloads. These verify that a malformed
/// format string (e.g. a placeholder with no matching arg) is reported as a
/// log message instead of throwing FormatException back into caller code -
/// a logging API must never crash the caller just because the message it was
/// asked to log was malformed.
/// </summary>
public class DebugTests
{
    public DebugTests()
    {
        InternalCalls.Reset();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Log_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_DoesNotThrow()
    {
        Action act = () => Debug.Log("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        act.Should().NotThrow();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Log_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_LogsRawFormatAndErrorMarker()
    {
        Debug.Log("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        InternalCalls.InfoLogs.Should().ContainSingle();
        InternalCalls.InfoLogs[0].Should().Contain("bad {0} {1}");
        InternalCalls.InfoLogs[0].Should().Contain("[format error:");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Log_WithValidFormatString_FormatsNormally()
    {
        Debug.Log("value is {0}", 42);

        InternalCalls.InfoLogs.Should().ContainSingle("value is 42");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LogError_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_DoesNotThrow()
    {
        Action act = () => Debug.LogError("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        act.Should().NotThrow();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LogError_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_LogsRawFormatAndErrorMarker()
    {
        Debug.LogError("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        InternalCalls.ErrorLogs.Should().ContainSingle();
        InternalCalls.ErrorLogs[0].Should().Contain("bad {0} {1}");
        InternalCalls.ErrorLogs[0].Should().Contain("[format error:");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LogError_WithValidFormatString_FormatsNormally()
    {
        Debug.LogError("failed with code {0}", 7);

        InternalCalls.ErrorLogs.Should().ContainSingle("failed with code 7");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LogWarning_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_DoesNotThrow()
    {
        Action act = () => Debug.LogWarning("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        act.Should().NotThrow();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void LogWarning_WithMismatchedPlaceholderCount_LogsRawFormatAndErrorMarker()
    {
        Debug.LogWarning("bad {0} {1}", "onlyOneArg");

        InternalCalls.WarningLogs.Should().ContainSingle();
        InternalCalls.WarningLogs[0].Should().Contain("bad {0} {1}");
        InternalCalls.WarningLogs[0].Should().Contain("[format error:");
    }
}
```

Note: `LogDebug` is `[Conditional("DEBUG")] [Conditional("O3DE_DEBUG")]` — calls to it are stripped entirely at the call site unless the calling assembly defines `DEBUG` or `O3DE_DEBUG`. It is not included in the automated coverage above; its formatting path is identical to `Log`'s (`SafeFormat` shared helper) so `Log`'s coverage exercises the same fallback logic. This is called out explicitly rather than silently skipped.

### Task 4: Fix `Debugger.WaitForAttach(TimeSpan.Zero)` hanging forever instead of checking once

**Files:**
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Debugger.cs:72-104`
- Test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/DebuggerTests.cs` (create)
- Modify: `SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md:953`

- [ ] **Step 1: Confirm the current buggy behavior**

Read `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Debugger.cs`. The XML doc comment on `WaitForAttach` (lines 68-71) states:

```csharp
        /// <param name="timeout">Maximum time to wait. <see cref="TimeSpan.Zero"/>
        /// means "check once and return", a negative value or
        /// <see cref="System.Threading.Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan"/> means "wait forever".</param>
```

But the method body (lines 72-77) contradicts this:

```csharp
        public static bool WaitForAttach(TimeSpan timeout = default)
        {
            // Default(TimeSpan) is Zero - treat as "wait forever". Callers
            // that genuinely want a single-shot check should use IsAttached.
            // Negative spans (e.g. Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan) also mean infinite.
            bool waitForever = timeout <= TimeSpan.Zero;
```

`timeout <= TimeSpan.Zero` is `true` for `TimeSpan.Zero` itself (since `Zero <= Zero`), so passing `TimeSpan.Zero` — including via the default parameter, i.e. calling `WaitForAttach()` with no arguments — sets `waitForever = true` and blocks forever if no debugger is attached. This directly contradicts the XML doc's stated contract and matches the documented FAQ entry in `SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md:953`:

```
| Editor freezes after `WaitForAttach` and never resumes | Either the timeout was set to `TimeSpan.Zero` (= wait forever) and no debugger attached, or `IsAttached` never flipped. Restart the editor. Use a finite timeout in production. |
```

That FAQ entry is documenting the bug as if it were intended behavior — it needs to be corrected once the fix lands (Step 3 below).

- [ ] **Step 2: Fix `WaitForAttach` so only `Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` or a negative timeout means "wait forever"**

In `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Debugger.cs`, replace the method body:

Current code (lines 72-104):

```csharp
        public static bool WaitForAttach(TimeSpan timeout = default)
        {
            // Default(TimeSpan) is Zero - treat as "wait forever". Callers
            // that genuinely want a single-shot check should use IsAttached.
            // Negative spans (e.g. Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan) also mean infinite.
            bool waitForever = timeout <= TimeSpan.Zero;
            DateTime deadline = waitForever
                ? DateTime.MaxValue
                : DateTime.UtcNow + timeout;

            if (IsAttached)
            {
                return true;
            }

            // Log once so the user knows the editor is paused on purpose.
            Debug.Log(waitForever
                ? "[O3DESharp] Waiting for debugger to attach (no timeout)..."
                : $"[O3DESharp] Waiting for debugger to attach (timeout {timeout.TotalSeconds:F1}s)...");

            while (DateTime.UtcNow < deadline)
            {
                if (IsAttached)
                {
                    Debug.Log("[O3DESharp] Debugger attached, resuming script.");
                    return true;
                }
                Thread.Sleep(100);
            }

            Debug.LogWarning("[O3DESharp] WaitForAttach timed out; continuing without debugger.");
            return false;
        }
```

New code:

```csharp
        public static bool WaitForAttach(TimeSpan timeout = default)
        {
            if (IsAttached)
            {
                return true;
            }

            // Only a strictly negative timeout (e.g. Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan,
            // which is -1ms) means "wait forever". TimeSpan.Zero - including
            // the default parameter value, since default(TimeSpan) is Zero -
            // means "check IsAttached once and return immediately", matching
            // this method's documented contract above. This is a deliberate
            // behavior change from earlier versions where Zero (and therefore
            // the no-args call WaitForAttach()) silently blocked forever;
            // see SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md's troubleshooting FAQ for the symptom
            // this used to cause. Callers that want the old "block forever"
            // behavior must now pass Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan explicitly.
            bool waitForever = timeout < TimeSpan.Zero;
            if (!waitForever && timeout == TimeSpan.Zero)
            {
                // Single-shot check: IsAttached was already false above, so
                // there is nothing to poll for. Return immediately.
                return false;
            }

            DateTime deadline = waitForever
                ? DateTime.MaxValue
                : DateTime.UtcNow + timeout;

            // Log once so the user knows the editor is paused on purpose.
            Debug.Log(waitForever
                ? "[O3DESharp] Waiting for debugger to attach (no timeout)..."
                : $"[O3DESharp] Waiting for debugger to attach (timeout {timeout.TotalSeconds:F1}s)...");

            while (DateTime.UtcNow < deadline)
            {
                if (IsAttached)
                {
                    Debug.Log("[O3DESharp] Debugger attached, resuming script.");
                    return true;
                }
                Thread.Sleep(100);
            }

            Debug.LogWarning("[O3DESharp] WaitForAttach timed out; continuing without debugger.");
            return false;
        }
```

Note the behavior change this introduces: `Debugger.WaitForAttach()` called with no arguments now performs a single `IsAttached` check and returns immediately (matching the XML doc's contract), instead of blocking forever as it did before this fix. Any script relying on the old "no-args call blocks forever" behavior must be updated to call `Debugger.WaitForAttach(Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan)` explicitly. `WaitForAttachIfRequested()` (lines 175-222 of the same file) is unaffected — it always passes an explicit positive `timeout` (120s default or the `O3DESHARP_WAIT_FOR_DEBUGGER_TIMEOUT_MS` override), never the zero-arg default, so its behavior is unchanged except that its own `ms > 0 ? ... : Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` branch (which already only used `Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` for the "wait forever" case) continues to work exactly as before.

- [ ] **Step 3: Correct the SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md FAQ entry that documents the old buggy behavior**

Read `SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md` around line 953. Current row in the Troubleshooting table:

```
| Editor freezes after `WaitForAttach` and never resumes | Either the timeout was set to `TimeSpan.Zero` (= wait forever) and no debugger attached, or `IsAttached` never flipped. Restart the editor. Use a finite timeout in production. |
```

Replace with:

```
| Editor freezes after `WaitForAttach` and never resumes | The timeout was set to `Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` (or a negative `TimeSpan`) and no debugger attached, or `IsAttached` never flipped. Restart the editor. Use a finite timeout in production. Note: `TimeSpan.Zero` (and therefore the no-args call `WaitForAttach()`) means "check `IsAttached` once and return immediately" — it does **not** wait forever. |
```

Also update the doc comment's example usage block above it, since the class-level example on lines 29-37 already uses an explicit finite timeout (`TimeSpan.FromSeconds(30)`) and needs no change — verify this by re-reading lines 28-38 of `Debugger.cs` after your Step 2 edit to confirm it still reads correctly (it does; no edit needed there).

- [ ] **Step 4: Add `Debugger.cs` to the test project (verify it's already linked; it is per Task 0)**

Read `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj` and confirm it already contains:

```xml
    <Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" Link="O3DE.Core\Debugger.cs" />
```

in its `ItemGroup`. This file is already linked per Task 0's setup (it's listed among `Math/Vector2.cs`, `Math/Vector3.cs`, `Math/Quaternion.cs`, `Debug.cs`, `Debugger.cs`). If for any reason it is missing, add that exact line to the `<ItemGroup>` that contains the other `<Compile Include="..\O3DE.Core\..." Link="O3DE.Core\..." />` entries before proceeding.

- [ ] **Step 5: Write the xUnit regression tests**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/DebuggerTests.cs`:

```csharp
/*
 * Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
 * For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
 *
 * SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
 *
 */

using System;
using System.Diagnostics;
using O3DE;

namespace O3DE.Core.Tests
{
    public class DebuggerTests
    {
        // These tests run in a plain xUnit test host with no managed
        // debugger attached (Debugger.IsAttached == false throughout), so
        // WaitForAttach's polling loop - if it were entered - would spin
        // until its deadline. We assert on wall-clock time to prove the
        // Zero / default-parameter cases return immediately instead of
        // entering that loop at all.
        private static readonly TimeSpan MaxAllowedDuration = TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(500);

        [Fact]
        public void WaitForAttach_WithZeroTimeout_ReturnsImmediatelyWithoutBlocking()
        {
            var stopwatch = Stopwatch.StartNew();

            bool result = Debugger.WaitForAttach(TimeSpan.Zero);

            stopwatch.Stop();

            result.Should().BeFalse("no debugger is attached in the test host");
            stopwatch.Elapsed.Should().BeLessThan(MaxAllowedDuration,
                "TimeSpan.Zero must mean \"check IsAttached once and return\", not \"wait forever\"");
        }

        [Fact]
        public void WaitForAttach_WithDefaultParameter_ReturnsImmediatelyWithoutBlocking()
        {
            var stopwatch = Stopwatch.StartNew();

            // No-args call - exercises the `timeout = default` parameter,
            // which is TimeSpan.Zero. Before this fix this call blocked
            // forever because default(TimeSpan) was treated as "wait
            // forever" instead of "check once".
            bool result = Debugger.WaitForAttach();

            stopwatch.Stop();

            result.Should().BeFalse("no debugger is attached in the test host");
            stopwatch.Elapsed.Should().BeLessThan(MaxAllowedDuration,
                "WaitForAttach() with no arguments must check IsAttached once and return, not wait forever");
        }

        [Fact]
        public void WaitForAttach_WithNegativeTimeout_IsTreatedAsWaitForeverAndTimesOutOnlyAfterPolling()
        {
            // We can't actually wait forever in a test. Instead we confirm
            // that a negative-but-not-Infinite TimeSpan is routed into the
            // "wait forever" branch (not the "check once" branch) by racing
            // it against a short-lived thread: since IsAttached can never
            // become true in this test host, the only way to observe the
            // "wait forever" branch without hanging the test suite is to
            // confirm it does NOT return within one poll interval (100ms)
            // when given a negative span - i.e. it actually enters the
            // polling loop rather than short-circuiting like Zero does.
            // We bound the observation window well under the 100ms poll
            // interval by running on a background thread and aborting via
            // timeout, since Debugger.WaitForAttach itself has no
            // cancellation support.
            var stopwatch = Stopwatch.StartNew();
            var thread = new System.Threading.Thread(() => Debugger.WaitForAttach(Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan))
            {
                IsBackground = true
            };
            thread.Start();

            // Give it far less than one 100ms poll interval to prove it did
            // NOT return early the way the Zero case does.
            bool finishedQuickly = thread.Join(TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(50));
            stopwatch.Stop();

            finishedQuickly.Should().BeFalse(
                "Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan must enter the polling loop (wait forever), not return immediately like TimeSpan.Zero does");

            // The background thread is left running (IsBackground = true
            // means it will not prevent process exit); it polls IsAttached
            // every 100ms forever, which is harmless for the lifetime of
            // this test process.
        }
    }
}
```

Note on the `Timeout` type used in the third test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Debugger.cs` uses `System.Threading.Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` fully qualified in its own XML doc but the file has `using System.Threading;` at the top (line 10), and this test file does not — add `using System.Threading;` to `DebuggerTests.cs`'s using block if you keep the unqualified `Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan` reference in Step 5, or qualify it as `System.Threading.Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan`. Use the explicit `using System.Threading;` form for consistency with `Debugger.cs`:

```csharp
using System;
using System.Diagnostics;
using System.Threading;
using O3DE;
```

(Replace the using block at the top of `DebuggerTests.cs` from Step 5 with the four lines above.)

- [ ] **Step 8: Manual verification of the real editor-facing symptom**

Since `WaitForAttach`'s production entry point (`WaitForAttachIfRequested`, gated by the `O3DESHARP_WAIT_FOR_DEBUGGER` env var) never uses the zero-arg default and is therefore unaffected by this fix, the primary manual check is for script authors calling `WaitForAttach()` directly with no arguments, which is now a behavior change:

1. In a scratch script component (e.g. temporarily add to any existing `ScriptComponent`-derived class's `OnCreate`), add the line `O3DE.Debugger.WaitForAttach();` with no arguments.
2. Build and run the O3DE Editor with this script attached to an entity in a level, without attaching any IDE debugger beforehand.
3. Confirm the editor does **not** freeze — the entity activates normally and subsequent `OnCreate` code runs immediately, within well under a second.
4. Remove the scratch `WaitForAttach()` line before committing (it was only for manual verification; do not leave test code in production scripts).
5. Separately, confirm the "wait for real" path still works: set `Debugger.WaitForAttach(TimeSpan.FromSeconds(30))` in the same scratch spot, run the editor, and confirm the editor **does** pause for up to 30 seconds (or until you attach Rider/VS/VS Code via Attach to Process), logging `[O3DESharp] Waiting for debugger to attach (timeout 30.0s)...` to the Console panel, then `[O3DESharp] Debugger attached, resuming script.` once you attach.

- [ ] **Step 9: Commit**

```bash
git add Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Debugger.cs Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/DebuggerTests.cs SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: Debugger.WaitForAttach(TimeSpan.Zero) no longer waits forever

WaitForAttach's waitForever check used `timeout <= TimeSpan.Zero`, so
TimeSpan.Zero - including the default parameter value used by the
no-args call WaitForAttach() - blocked forever instead of performing
the single IsAttached check documented in the method's own XML doc
comment and in SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md's troubleshooting FAQ. Only
Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan or a negative TimeSpan now means "wait
forever"; TimeSpan.Zero checks once and returns immediately. This is
a behavior change for any caller relying on the old no-args-blocks-
forever behavior - such callers must now pass Timeout.InfiniteTimeSpan
explicitly.
EOF
)"
```

### Task 5: NativeReflection argument serialization — fail fast on unsupported types

**Rationale for testing approach:** `SerializeArgumentToObject` itself has no behavioral dependency on Coral (it only pattern-matches on CLR types like `Vector3`/`Entity`/`NativeObject`), but it lives in `NativeReflection.cs` alongside `ReflectionInternalCalls`, whose `delegate* unmanaged<...>` fields are typed in `NativeString`/`Bool32` from `Coral.Managed.Interop` — and `<Compile Include>` links the whole file, not one method, so the file won't compile in the test project without those two types existing somewhere. Both types are used only via implicit conversion (`string`→`NativeString` argument, `NativeString`→`string` return, `Bool32`→`bool` return) and are never invoked at runtime in the test (the real `ReflectionInternalCalls` fields stay null and are never called by this test). So the coupling is shallow enough to isolate cheaply with a two-type shim (`Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/CoralManagedInteropShim.cs`) providing a matching `Coral.Managed.Interop` namespace with just those two structs — no live Coral host needed. An automated xUnit test is used, not manual verification.

**Files:**
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/NativeReflection.cs:545-574`
- Create: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/CoralManagedInteropShim.cs`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj`
- Test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/NativeReflectionSerializationTests.cs`

- [ ] **Step 1: Fix the silent-stringify fallback in `SerializeArgumentToObject`**

Current code at `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/NativeReflection.cs:545-574`:

```csharp
        private static object? SerializeArgumentToObject(object arg)
        {
            if (arg is null) { return null; }
            return arg switch
            {
                bool b      => b,
                sbyte sb    => (int)sb,
                byte bv     => (int)bv,
                short sv    => (int)sv,
                ushort usv  => (int)usv,
                int i       => i,
                uint ui     => (long)ui,
                long l      => l,
                ulong ul    => ul,
                float f     => f,
                double d    => d,
                string s    => s,
                // Math types serialize as JSON arrays; C++ side maps the
                // 3- vs 4-element array shape to Vector3 / Vector4 /
                // Quaternion / Color based on the target parameter type.
                Vector3 v   => new[] { v.X, v.Y, v.Z },
                Quaternion q => new[] { q.X, q.Y, q.Z, q.W },
                // Entity wrapper exposes its underlying EntityId u64,
                // which the C++ side reads back via JsonValueToBehaviorParameter
                // when the target parameter is AZ::EntityId.
                Entity e    => e.Id,
                NativeObject no => no.Handle,
                _           => arg.ToString()
            };
        }
```

Replace the final arm (`_ => arg.ToString()`) so an unrecognized argument type throws immediately instead of silently degrading to a display string. Since `SerializeArgumentToObject` is shared by three public entry points (`BroadcastEBusEvent`, `SendEBusEvent`, `CreateInstance` — all of which funnel through `SerializeArguments(object[])` at lines 338, 425, and 456), there is no single caller name available inside the method itself; the exception message instead names the method that produced the bad value, `SerializeArgumentToObject`, which is precise enough to find in a stack trace and is what every caller ultimately shares:

```csharp
        private static object? SerializeArgumentToObject(object arg)
        {
            if (arg is null) { return null; }
            return arg switch
            {
                bool b      => b,
                sbyte sb    => (int)sb,
                byte bv     => (int)bv,
                short sv    => (int)sv,
                ushort usv  => (int)usv,
                int i       => i,
                uint ui     => (long)ui,
                long l      => l,
                ulong ul    => ul,
                float f     => f,
                double d    => d,
                string s    => s,
                // Math types serialize as JSON arrays; C++ side maps the
                // 3- vs 4-element array shape to Vector3 / Vector4 /
                // Quaternion / Color based on the target parameter type.
                Vector3 v   => new[] { v.X, v.Y, v.Z },
                Quaternion q => new[] { q.X, q.Y, q.Z, q.W },
                // Entity wrapper exposes its underlying EntityId u64,
                // which the C++ side reads back via JsonValueToBehaviorParameter
                // when the target parameter is AZ::EntityId.
                Entity e    => e.Id,
                NativeObject no => no.Handle,
                _ => throw new NotSupportedException(
                    $"Unsupported argument type {arg.GetType()} in NativeReflection.SerializeArgumentToObject. " +
                    "Add an explicit case for this type (and its native-side array/scalar shape) instead of " +
                    "letting it silently stringify - the C++ marshaler in " +
                    "O3DESharp::Marshaling::JsonValueToBehaviorParameter does not know how to consume a display " +
                    "string for this parameter type.")
            };
        }
```

Do not touch anything else in this file — `SerializeArguments`, `SerializeValue`, `DeserializeResult`, and the `ReflectionInternalCalls` class are all out of scope for this task.

- [ ] **Step 2: Add a minimal Coral.Managed.Interop shim so this file can compile standalone in the test project**

`NativeReflection.cs` has `using Coral.Managed.Interop;` at line 13 and its `ReflectionInternalCalls` class (lines 22-75) declares fields like `internal static delegate* unmanaged<NativeString, Bool32> Reflection_ClassExists;`. The real `Coral.Managed.Interop.NativeString`/`Bool32` types ship only inside `bin/Coral/Coral.Managed.dll`, a native-build artifact not present on a bare checkout, so `<Compile Include>`-ing the whole file into the test project requires a substitute for just those two types. Verify no other member of `Coral.Managed.Interop` is used in this file:

```bash
grep -n "NativeString\|Bool32" "Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/NativeReflection.cs"
```

Expected output: every match is either a `delegate* unmanaged<...>` field declaration inside `ReflectionInternalCalls`, or a `string`/`bool` variable being assigned from / passed to one of those delegate calls (e.g. `string json; ... json = ReflectionInternalCalls.Reflection_GetClassNames();` and `unsafe { return ReflectionInternalCalls.Reflection_ClassExists(className); }`) — no other `Coral.Managed.Interop` member is referenced.

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/CoralManagedInteropShim.cs`:

```csharp
namespace Coral.Managed.Interop
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Minimal stand-in for Coral.Managed.Interop.NativeString, used only so that
    /// NativeReflection.cs (which declares `delegate* unmanaged&lt;NativeString, ...&gt;`
    /// fields on ReflectionInternalCalls) can compile in this test project without the
    /// real Coral.Managed.dll, which is a native-build artifact not present on a bare
    /// checkout. Those delegate* fields are never populated or invoked by these tests -
    /// only the pure-managed SerializeArgumentToObject method is under test - so this
    /// shim only needs to satisfy the implicit string conversions NativeReflection.cs
    /// actually uses (string -> NativeString for call arguments, NativeString -> string
    /// for call results). It carries no other behavior.
    /// </summary>
    internal readonly struct NativeString
    {
        private readonly string? _value;

        private NativeString(string? value) => _value = value;

        public static implicit operator NativeString(string? value) => new(value);
        public static implicit operator string?(NativeString value) => value._value;

        public override string ToString() => _value ?? string.Empty;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Minimal stand-in for Coral.Managed.Interop.Bool32, used only so that
    /// NativeReflection.cs's ReflectionInternalCalls delegate* fields (e.g.
    /// Reflection_ClassExists returning Bool32, used directly as a C# bool) can
    /// compile in this test project. See NativeString above for why this exists.
    /// </summary>
    internal readonly struct Bool32
    {
        private readonly int _value;

        private Bool32(int value) => _value = value;

        public static implicit operator Bool32(bool value) => new(value ? 1 : 0);
        public static implicit operator bool(Bool32 value) => value._value != 0;
    }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Link `NativeReflection.cs` and the new shim into the test project**

Read the current `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj` (created by Task 0) before editing — confirm its `<Compile Include>` ItemGroup and package references match what's shown below; if Task 0 produced a differently-shaped file, adapt this edit to match the real structure instead of blindly pasting.

No ItemGroup entry is needed for it.

- [ ] **Step 4: Write the xUnit test**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/NativeReflectionSerializationTests.cs`:

```csharp
/*
 * Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
 * For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
 *
 * SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
 *
 */

using System;
using System.Reflection;
using O3DE;
using O3DE.Reflection;

namespace O3DE.Core.Tests
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Regression tests for NativeReflection's argument serialization. Covers the
    /// fix for a bug where an unrecognized argument type (e.g. Vector2) silently
    /// fell through to `arg.ToString()`, producing a display string the native
    /// marshaler could not consume, instead of failing immediately with a clear
    /// error naming the offending type.
    ///
    /// SerializeArgumentToObject is private, so these tests invoke it via
    /// reflection rather than widening its visibility just for tests.
    /// </summary>
    public class NativeReflectionSerializationTests
    {
        private static object? InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(object? arg)
        {
            MethodInfo method = typeof(NativeReflection).GetMethod(
                "SerializeArgumentToObject",
                BindingFlags.NonPublic | BindingFlags.Static)
                ?? throw new InvalidOperationException(
                    "NativeReflection.SerializeArgumentToObject not found - has it been renamed?");

            try
            {
                return method.Invoke(null, new object?[] { arg });
            }
            catch (TargetInvocationException ex) when (ex.InnerException is not null)
            {
                // Unwrap so callers can assert on the real exception type/message
                // instead of TargetInvocationException.
                throw ex.InnerException;
            }
        }

        [Fact]
        public void UnsupportedType_ThrowsNotSupportedException_NamingTheType()
        {
            var unsupported = new Vector2(1.0f, 2.0f);

            Action act = () => InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(unsupported);

            act.Should().Throw<NotSupportedException>()
                .WithMessage("*Vector2*")
                .WithMessage("*SerializeArgumentToObject*");
        }

        [Fact]
        public void UnsupportedType_DoesNotFallBackToToString()
        {
            var unsupported = new Vector2(1.0f, 2.0f);

            Action act = () => InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(unsupported);

            // Before the fix, this returned unsupported.ToString() (a display
            // string) instead of throwing - guard against regressing back to that.
            act.Should().Throw<NotSupportedException>();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void Null_ReturnsNull()
        {
            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(null);

            result.Should().BeNull();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void Vector3_SerializesToThreeElementFloatArray()
        {
            var v = new Vector3(1.0f, 2.0f, 3.0f);

            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(v);

            result.Should().BeOfType<float[]>();
            ((float[])result!).Should().Equal(1.0f, 2.0f, 3.0f);
        }

        [Fact]
        public void Quaternion_SerializesToFourElementFloatArray()
        {
            var q = new Quaternion(1.0f, 2.0f, 3.0f, 4.0f);

            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(q);

            result.Should().BeOfType<float[]>();
            ((float[])result!).Should().Equal(1.0f, 2.0f, 3.0f, 4.0f);
        }

        [Fact]
        public void Bool_PassesThroughUnchanged()
        {
            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(true);

            result.Should().Be(true);
        }

        [Fact]
        public void Int_PassesThroughUnchanged()
        {
            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject(42);

            result.Should().Be(42);
        }

        [Fact]
        public void String_PassesThroughUnchanged()
        {
            object? result = InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject("hello");

            result.Should().Be("hello");
        }
    }
}
```

Check that `Vector2` has a `(float, float)` constructor and `Vector3`/`Quaternion` have `(float, float, float)` / `(float, float, float, float)` constructors matching the calls above:

```bash
grep -n "public Vector2(" "Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector2.cs"
grep -n "public Vector3(" "Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Vector3.cs"
grep -n "public Quaternion(" "Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Math/Quaternion.cs"
```

If any constructor signature differs from what's shown above, adjust the corresponding test's constructor call to match the real signature (e.g. positional args in a different order, or a factory method instead of a constructor) rather than assuming the code above is correct.

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests**

```bash
"%LOCALAPPDATA%\Microsoft\dotnet\dotnet.exe" test Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo --logger "console;verbosity=normal" --filter "FullyQualifiedName~NativeReflectionSerializationTests"
```

Expected output ends with a line similar to:

```
Passed!  - Failed:     0, Passed:     8, Skipped:     0, Total:     8, ...
```

If `SerializeArgumentToObject` was not found via reflection (e.g. it was renamed since this task was written), the `InvokeSerializeArgumentToObject` helper's `InvalidOperationException` will surface as a test failure with a clear message naming the problem — re-read `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/NativeReflection.cs` and adjust the reflection lookup accordingly.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/NativeReflection.cs Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/CoralManagedInteropShim.cs Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/NativeReflectionSerializationTests.cs
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: NativeReflection throws on unsupported argument types instead of silently stringifying

SerializeArgumentToObject's fallback case (e.g. hit by Vector2, which
had no explicit switch arm) previously serialized unrecognized argument
types via arg.ToString(), producing a display string the native
marshaler cannot consume. This turned into a confusing type-mismatch
failure several layers away from the real cause. The fallback now
throws NotSupportedException naming the offending type immediately.
EOF
)"
```
