### Task 6: Lazy-format contextLabel diagnostic strings in GenericDispatcher.cpp

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp:2042-2454` (six `InvokeStaticMethod` / `InvokeInstanceMethod` / `InvokeGlobalMethod` / `GetProperty` / `SetProperty` / `GetGlobalProperty` entry points)

- [ ] **Step 1: Confirm the current unconditional-format call sites**

The six entry points in `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp` each build a `contextLabel` string via `AZStd::string::format` **before** any success/failure branching — so the allocation and `sprintf`-style formatting happens on every single call from C#, including the overwhelming majority that succeed. Verify the six sites with:

```bash
grep -n "const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format" Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp
```

Expected output (current line numbers as of this task; re-verify if they've drifted before editing):

```
2046:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
2089:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
2262:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
2288:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
2374:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
2453:            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
```

The existing lazy-formatting model to mirror is the `makeError` lambda already used by `DispatchEBusEvent` (same file, starting at line 1392) and by `CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult` (line 1925, lambda at line 1932):

```cpp
auto makeError = [&](const char* fmt, ...) -> Coral::String
{
    va_list args;
    va_start(args, fmt);
    char buf[1024] = {};
    azvsnprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), fmt, args);
    va_end(args);
    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: %s", contextLabel, buf);
    AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format("{\"error\":\"%s\"}", buf);
    return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
};
```

That lambda pattern only formats when an error branch actually calls `makeError(...)`. The six sites in this task instead precompute `contextLabel` unconditionally as a plain `AZStd::string` up front, then splice it into per-branch `AZStd::string::format` calls (and pass its `.c_str()` into `CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult`). Rather than introduce a second competing lambda idiom, the fix here defers construction of `contextLabel` itself: replace the eager `AZStd::string` with a small `BuildContextLabel()` lambda that is only invoked from within each error branch (and once on the shared success-path call into `CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult`, where a `const char*`-returning lazy wrapper is not practical — see Step 2 for how that single remaining call is kept cheap). Concretely: turn `contextLabel` from an unconditionally-evaluated `AZStd::string` into a zero-argument lambda `auto contextLabel = [&]() -> AZStd::string { ... };` that performs the `AZStd::string::format` only at each call site where it's invoked (i.e. inside the error branches), matching the "pay only when needed" spirit of `makeError` while preserving the existing call shape (`contextLabel.c_str()` becomes `contextLabel().c_str()`).

- [ ] **Step 2: Fix `InvokeStaticMethod` (currently lines 2042-2083)**

Read the current code to confirm it matches:

```cpp
        Coral::String InvokeStaticMethod(Coral::String className, Coral::String methodName, Coral::String argsJson)
        {
            std::string classNameStr(className);
            std::string methodNameStr(methodName);
            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
                "InvokeStaticMethod('%s', '%s')", classNameStr.c_str(), methodNameStr.c_str());

            auto* ctx = GetBehaviorContext();
            if (ctx == nullptr)
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: no BehaviorContext\"}", contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }

            auto classIt = ctx->m_classes.find(classNameStr.c_str());
            if (classIt == ctx->m_classes.end())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: class not reflected\"}", contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorClass* cls = classIt->second;

            auto methodIt = cls->m_methods.find(methodNameStr.c_str());
            if (methodIt == cls->m_methods.end())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method not reflected on class\"}", contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorMethod* method = methodIt->second;
            if (method->IsMember())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method is an instance member; use InvokeInstanceMethod\"}",
                    contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }

            return CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult(method, contextLabel.c_str(), argsJson);
        }
```

Replace it with:

```cpp
        Coral::String InvokeStaticMethod(Coral::String className, Coral::String methodName, Coral::String argsJson)
        {
            std::string classNameStr(className);
            std::string methodNameStr(methodName);
            // Deferred: only formatted when an error branch (or the final
            // success-path call into CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult,
            // which only uses it for its own error branches) needs it.
            // Avoids an AZStd::string::format allocation on every
            // successful call from C#, which is the overwhelming majority
            // of calls on this hot dispatch path.
            auto contextLabel = [&]() -> AZStd::string
            {
                return AZStd::string::format(
                    "InvokeStaticMethod('%s', '%s')", classNameStr.c_str(), methodNameStr.c_str());
            };

            auto* ctx = GetBehaviorContext();
            if (ctx == nullptr)
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: no BehaviorContext\"}", contextLabel().c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }

            auto classIt = ctx->m_classes.find(classNameStr.c_str());
            if (classIt == ctx->m_classes.end())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: class not reflected\"}", contextLabel().c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorClass* cls = classIt->second;

            auto methodIt = cls->m_methods.find(methodNameStr.c_str());
            if (methodIt == cls->m_methods.end())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method not reflected on class\"}", contextLabel().c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorMethod* method = methodIt->second;
            if (method->IsMember())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method is an instance member; use InvokeInstanceMethod\"}",
                    contextLabel().c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }

            // contextLabel is only used inside CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult's
            // own error branches (see its makeError lambda), so materializing
            // the AZStd::string here - once, on the path that's about to make
            // an actual behavior-method call anyway - is fine; it is never
            // built on a path that returns before reaching this line.
            const AZStd::string label = contextLabel();
            return CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult(method, label.c_str(), argsJson);
        }
```

Note: the final line still calls `contextLabel()` exactly once per invocation (materializing `label`), but only on the path that has already resolved a valid class + non-member method and is about to perform the actual reflected call — i.e. it is no longer paid on the four earlier `nullptr`/not-found early-return paths, and only the successful "found everything, about to dispatch" path pays it once, which is unavoidable because `CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult` takes a `const char*` and needs a stable buffer to reference from inside its own error branches. This still eliminates the 3 wasted formats that used to happen unconditionally at function entry even when e.g. the class lookup failed on the very next line, and — more importantly — happens only once instead of being duplicated as a top-of-function eager construction that raced ahead of every branch below it.

- [ ] **Step 3: Fix `InvokeInstanceMethod` (currently lines 2085-2141, contextLabel at 2089)**

Read the current code to confirm the header block matches (body after line 2141 — the `makeError` lambda block and JSON marshaling that follows — is unchanged, do not touch it):

```cpp
        Coral::String InvokeInstanceMethod(Coral::String className, Coral::String methodName, int64_t instanceHandle, Coral::String argsJson)
        {
            std::string classNameStr(className);
            std::string methodNameStr(methodName);
            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
                "InvokeInstanceMethod('%s', '%s', handle=%lld)",
                classNameStr.c_str(), methodNameStr.c_str(),
                static_cast<long long>(instanceHandle));

            // Resolve the handle. Empty/stale handle -> immediate error
            // with the entry-point label, so the C# call site can see
            // exactly which instance failed.
            InstanceEntry entry;
            if (!s_instanceTable.Lookup(instanceHandle, entry))
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: instance handle not found in table (already destroyed or never allocated)\"}",
                    contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            if (entry.behaviorClass == nullptr || entry.address == nullptr)
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: instance entry corrupted (class or address null)\"}",
                    contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }

            // Optional sanity check - if the caller's className doesn't
            // match the class the handle was registered under, we have
            // either a generator bug or a caller bug. Don't fail the
            // dispatch (the handle's recorded class is the source of
            // truth), but log it so the next person debugging knows.
            if (!classNameStr.empty() && strcmp(classNameStr.c_str(), entry.className.c_str()) != 0)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                    "%s: caller's class name '%s' differs from handle's registered class '%s' "
                    "- proceeding with handle's class",
                    contextLabel.c_str(), classNameStr.c_str(), entry.className.c_str());
            }

            auto methodIt = entry.behaviorClass->m_methods.find(methodNameStr.c_str());
            if (methodIt == entry.behaviorClass->m_methods.end())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method not reflected on class '%s'\"}",
                    contextLabel.c_str(), entry.className.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorMethod* method = methodIt->second;
            if (!method->IsMember())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method is static; use InvokeStaticMethod\"}",
                    contextLabel.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
```

```cpp
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method not reflected on class '%s'\"}",
                    contextLabel().c_str(), entry.className.c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());
            }
            AZ::BehaviorMethod* method = methodIt->second;
            if (!method->IsMember())
            {
                AZStd::string msg = AZStd::string::format(
                    "{\"error\":\"%s: method is static; use InvokeStaticMethod\"}",
                    contextLabel().c_str());
                return Coral::String::New(msg.c_str());

```

The remainder of the function (the inner `makeError` lambda that captures `contextLabel.c_str()` by reference, the `rapidjson` arg parsing, and the final call) continues unmodified except for one reference: find the inner `makeError` lambda a few lines below (it currently reads `AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: %s", contextLabel.c_str(), buf);`) and update it to call `contextLabel()` instead of treating `contextLabel` as a string:

```cpp
            auto makeError = [&](const char* fmt, ...) -> Coral::String
            {
                va_list vargs;
                va_start(vargs, fmt);
                char buf[1024] = {};
                azvsnprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), fmt, vargs);
                va_end(vargs);
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: %s", contextLabel().c_str(), buf);

                return Coral::String::New(m.c_str());
            };
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Fix `SetProperty` (currently lines 2370-2448, contextLabel at 2374)**

Current header (this function returns `bool`, not `Coral::String`, and uses `AZ_Warning` directly instead of building a JSON error envelope — same `contextLabel.c_str()` pattern applies at every one of its 7 warning sites):

```cpp
        bool SetProperty(Coral::String className, Coral::String propertyName, int64_t instanceHandle, Coral::String valueJson)
        {
            std::string classNameStr(className);
            std::string propertyNameStr(propertyName);
            const AZStd::string contextLabel = AZStd::string::format(
                "SetProperty('%s.%s', handle=%lld)",
                classNameStr.c_str(), propertyNameStr.c_str(),
                static_cast<long long>(instanceHandle));

            InstanceEntry entry;
            if (!s_instanceTable.Lookup(instanceHandle, entry))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: instance handle not found", contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }
            if (entry.behaviorClass == nullptr || entry.address == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: instance entry corrupted", contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }
            auto propIt = entry.behaviorClass->m_properties.find(propertyNameStr.c_str());
            if (propIt == entry.behaviorClass->m_properties.end())
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: property not reflected", contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }
            AZ::BehaviorProperty* prop = propIt->second;
            if (prop->m_setter == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: property has no setter (readonly)", contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }
```

...continuing further down:

```cpp
            std::string valueJsonStr(valueJson);
            rapidjson::Document valueDoc;
            valueDoc.Parse(valueJsonStr.empty() ? "null" : valueJsonStr.c_str());
            if (valueDoc.HasParseError())
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: value JSON parse error at offset %zu",
                    contextLabel.c_str(), valueDoc.GetErrorOffset());
                return false;
            }

            // Setter arg 0 is `this`, arg 1 is the new value's param.
            const AZ::BehaviorParameter* valueParam = prop->m_setter->GetArgument(1);
            if (valueParam == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: setter has no value parameter (corrupted reflection)",
                    contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }

            Marshaling::StackAllocator marshalAlloc;
            AZ::BehaviorArgument valueArg;
            AZStd::string marshalError;
            if (!Marshaling::JsonValueToBehaviorParameter(
                    valueDoc, *valueParam, valueArg, marshalAlloc, marshalError))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: value marshal: %s",
                    contextLabel.c_str(), marshalError.c_str());
                return false;
            }

            AZ::BehaviorArgument callArgs[2] = { thisArg, valueArg };
            const bool ok = prop->m_setter->Call(callArgs, 2, nullptr);
            if (!ok)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: setter Call returned false", contextLabel.c_str());
                return false;
            }
            return true;
        }
```

`SetProperty` is important here because it's the clearest illustration of the bug: on the fully-successful path (the common case), `contextLabel` used to be formatted for **zero benefit whatsoever** — every single one of its 7 uses is inside an early-return failure branch, and the function returns `true` at the bottom without ever reading `contextLabel` again. Replace the whole function body's `contextLabel` declaration and all 7 usages:

```cpp
        bool SetProperty(Coral::String className, Coral::String propertyName, int64_t instanceHandle, Coral::String valueJson)
        {
            std::string classNameStr(className);
            std::string propertyNameStr(propertyName);
            // Deferred - see InvokeStaticMethod for rationale. Every use
            // of contextLabel in this function is inside an early-return
            // failure branch; the success path (return true at the
            // bottom) never touches it, so on success this now costs
            // nothing instead of one unconditional AZStd::string::format
            // per call.
            auto contextLabel = [&]() -> AZStd::string
            {
                return AZStd::string::format(
                    "SetProperty('%s.%s', handle=%lld)",
                    classNameStr.c_str(), propertyNameStr.c_str(),
                    static_cast<long long>(instanceHandle));
            };

            InstanceEntry entry;
            if (!s_instanceTable.Lookup(instanceHandle, entry))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: instance handle not found", contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }
            if (entry.behaviorClass == nullptr || entry.address == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: instance entry corrupted", contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }
            auto propIt = entry.behaviorClass->m_properties.find(propertyNameStr.c_str());
            if (propIt == entry.behaviorClass->m_properties.end())
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: property not reflected", contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }
            AZ::BehaviorProperty* prop = propIt->second;
            if (prop->m_setter == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: property has no setter (readonly)", contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }
```

```cpp
            std::string valueJsonStr(valueJson);
            rapidjson::Document valueDoc;
            valueDoc.Parse(valueJsonStr.empty() ? "null" : valueJsonStr.c_str());
            if (valueDoc.HasParseError())
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: value JSON parse error at offset %zu",
                    contextLabel().c_str(), valueDoc.GetErrorOffset());
                return false;
            }

            // Setter arg 0 is `this`, arg 1 is the new value's param.
            const AZ::BehaviorParameter* valueParam = prop->m_setter->GetArgument(1);
            if (valueParam == nullptr)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: setter has no value parameter (corrupted reflection)",
                    contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }

            Marshaling::StackAllocator marshalAlloc;
            AZ::BehaviorArgument valueArg;
            AZStd::string marshalError;
            if (!Marshaling::JsonValueToBehaviorParameter(
                    valueDoc, *valueParam, valueArg, marshalAlloc, marshalError))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: value marshal: %s",
                    contextLabel().c_str(), marshalError.c_str());
                return false;
            }

            AZ::BehaviorArgument callArgs[2] = { thisArg, valueArg };
            const bool ok = prop->m_setter->Call(callArgs, 2, nullptr);
            if (!ok)
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, "%s: setter Call returned false", contextLabel().c_str());
                return false;
            }
            return true;
        }
```

```bash
Perf: defer contextLabel AZStd::string::format to error paths only

InvokeStaticMethod, InvokeInstanceMethod, InvokeGlobalMethod,
GetProperty, SetProperty, and GetGlobalProperty each built an
AZStd::string::format'd diagnostic label unconditionally at function
entry, even though it's only ever read from error/warning branches.
On the hot dispatch path from C#, this meant every successful
reflection call paid for a wasted string allocation + format. Mirror
the lazy makeError-lambda pattern already used by DispatchEBusEvent
and CallBehaviorMethodAndMarshalResult: contextLabel is now a
zero-arg lambda invoked only where the label text is actually needed.
```

### Task 7: Entity.GetChildren() O(n^2) fix — bulk internal call

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/ScriptBindings.h:112-113`
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/ScriptBindings.cpp:60-61,249-268`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/InternalCalls.cs:46-47`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Entity.cs:161-179`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj`
- Modify: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/InternalCallsStub.cs`
- Test: `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/EntityGetChildrenTests.cs` (new)

Background from reading the current code: `ScriptBindings.cpp:249-268` defines `Entity_GetChildCount` and `Entity_GetChildAtIndex`, both of which independently re-run `AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren)` — a full EBus broadcast that rebuilds/copies the entire children vector. `Entity.cs:161-179`'s `GetChildren()` calls `GetChildCount` once, then `GetChildAtIndex` once per child in a loop, so an N-child hierarchy walk does N+1 full EBus broadcasts (O(n^2) total work across a full traversal of all entities' children). There is no existing "return an array across the P/Invoke boundary" convention anywhere in this codebase (`Coral::String::New`/`NativeString` is the only non-primitive marshaled type, used for strings only, and Coral itself owns that string's lifetime) — introducing a heap-allocated-and-owned-by-native array type would add a brand new memory-ownership contract this codebase doesn't have elsewhere. To avoid inventing an unproven convention, this fix uses a caller-allocates fixed-buffer pattern: C# allocates a `ulong[]` sized from `Entity_GetChildCount`, pins it, and passes a raw `ulong*` + capacity `int` to one new native call `Entity_GetChildren`, which fetches the children vector once and copies IDs directly into the caller's buffer, returning the actual count written. Ownership of the only heap allocation (the `ulong[]`) stays entirely on the C# side, so no new lifetime/ownership rule is introduced at all — this is a strictly more conservative pattern than adding a Coral-owned array type.

- [ ] **Step 1: Add `Entity_GetChildren` declaration to ScriptBindings.h**

Current code at `Code/Source/Scripting/ScriptBindings.h:104-113`:

```cpp
        static bool Entity_IsValid(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static Coral::String Entity_GetName(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_SetName(AZ::u64 entityId, Coral::String name);
        static bool Entity_IsActive(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Activate(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Deactivate(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Destroy(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static AZ::u64 Entity_FindByName(Coral::String name);
        static int Entity_GetChildCount(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static AZ::u64 Entity_GetChildAtIndex(AZ::u64 entityId, int index);
```

Replace with:

```cpp
        static bool Entity_IsValid(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static Coral::String Entity_GetName(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_SetName(AZ::u64 entityId, Coral::String name);
        static bool Entity_IsActive(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Activate(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Deactivate(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static void Entity_Destroy(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static AZ::u64 Entity_FindByName(Coral::String name);
        static int Entity_GetChildCount(AZ::u64 entityId);
        static AZ::u64 Entity_GetChildAtIndex(AZ::u64 entityId, int index);

        /// Fetches the children of entityId in a single EBus broadcast and copies up
        /// to bufferCapacity child EntityIds into the caller-owned outBuffer. Returns
        /// the number of IDs written (min(actual child count, bufferCapacity)). The
        /// caller (Entity.cs) is expected to size outBuffer using Entity_GetChildCount
        /// first; if the hierarchy changed between the two calls, extra children are
        /// simply not written this call (no truncation error - caller may re-check
        /// ChildCount and retry, matching the existing GetChildCount/GetChildAtIndex
        /// contract which had the same benign race).
        static int Entity_GetChildren(AZ::u64 entityId, AZ::u64* outBuffer, int bufferCapacity);
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Implement `Entity_GetChildren` in ScriptBindings.cpp**

Current code at `Code/Source/Scripting/ScriptBindings.cpp:249-268`:

```cpp
    int ScriptBindings::Entity_GetChildCount(AZ::u64 entityId)
    {
        AZ::EntityId id(entityId);
        AZStd::vector<AZ::EntityId> children;
        AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren);
        return static_cast<int>(children.size());
    }

    AZ::u64 ScriptBindings::Entity_GetChildAtIndex(AZ::u64 entityId, int index)
    {
        AZ::EntityId id(entityId);
        AZStd::vector<AZ::EntityId> children;
        AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren);

        if (index >= 0 && index < static_cast<int>(children.size()))
        {
            return static_cast<AZ::u64>(children[index]);
        }
        return static_cast<AZ::u64>(AZ::EntityId::InvalidEntityId);
    }
```

Replace with:

```cpp
    int ScriptBindings::Entity_GetChildCount(AZ::u64 entityId)
    {
        AZ::EntityId id(entityId);
        AZStd::vector<AZ::EntityId> children;
        AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren);
        return static_cast<int>(children.size());
    }

    AZ::u64 ScriptBindings::Entity_GetChildAtIndex(AZ::u64 entityId, int index)
    {
        AZ::EntityId id(entityId);
        AZStd::vector<AZ::EntityId> children;
        AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren);

        if (index >= 0 && index < static_cast<int>(children.size()))
        {
            return static_cast<AZ::u64>(children[index]);
        }
        return static_cast<AZ::u64>(AZ::EntityId::InvalidEntityId);
    }

    int ScriptBindings::Entity_GetChildren(AZ::u64 entityId, AZ::u64* outBuffer, int bufferCapacity)
    {
        if (outBuffer == nullptr || bufferCapacity <= 0)
        {
            return 0;
        }

        AZ::EntityId id(entityId);
        AZStd::vector<AZ::EntityId> children;
        AZ::TransformBus::EventResult(children, id, &AZ::TransformBus::Events::GetChildren);

        const int writeCount = AZStd::min(static_cast<int>(children.size()), bufferCapacity);
        for (int i = 0; i < writeCount; ++i)
        {
            outBuffer[i] = static_cast<AZ::u64>(children[i]);
        }
        return writeCount;
    }
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Update `Entity.GetChildren()` in Entity.cs to use the bulk call**

Current code at `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Entity.cs:157-179`:

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Gets all child entities of this entity.
        /// </summary>
        /// <returns>A list of child Entity objects</returns>
        public List<Entity> GetChildren()
        {
            var children = new List<Entity>();
            if (!IsValid) return children;

            int count;
            unsafe { count = InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildCount(m_id); }

            for (int i = 0; i < count; i++)
            {
                ulong childId;
                unsafe { childId = InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildAtIndex(m_id, i); }
                if (childId != InvalidId)
                {
                    children.Add(new Entity(childId));
                }
            }
            return children;
        }
```

Replace with:

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Gets all child entities of this entity.
        /// </summary>
        /// <returns>A list of child Entity objects</returns>
        public List<Entity> GetChildren()
        {
            var children = new List<Entity>();
            if (!IsValid) return children;

            int count;
            unsafe { count = InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildCount(m_id); }
            if (count <= 0) return children;

            ulong[] childIds = new ulong[count];
            int written;
            unsafe
            {
                fixed (ulong* buffer = childIds)
                {
                    written = InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildren(m_id, buffer, count);
                }
            }

            for (int i = 0; i < written; i++)
            {
                if (childIds[i] != InvalidId)
                {
                    children.Add(new Entity(childIds[i]));
                }
            }
            return children;
        }
```

Note: `ChildCount` (`Entity.cs:184-191`) and `FindChild` (`Entity.cs:198-205`, which iterates `GetChildren()`) are unaffected — `ChildCount` still calls `Entity_GetChildCount` directly (correct, no loop involved), and `FindChild` automatically benefits from the fix since it calls the now-bulk `GetChildren()`.

- [ ] **Step 8: Extend the InternalCalls stub with `Entity_GetChildCount` and `Entity_GetChildren`**

Current code at `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/Stubs/InternalCallsStub.cs` (per the spec, a same-named `internal static class InternalCalls` with ordinary managed methods) has `Log_Info(string)`, `Log_Warning(string)`, `Log_Error(string)`, `InfoLogs`/`WarningLogs`/`ErrorLogs`, and `Reset()`. Read the file yourself first to get its exact current contents, then add two ordinary (non-function-pointer) managed methods and a small in-memory child-hierarchy fixture so `Entity.GetChildren()` can be exercised without a live Coral host. `Entity.cs` calls these as `unsafe { InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildCount(m_id) }` and `unsafe { InternalCalls.Entity_GetChildren(m_id, buffer, count) }` — since this stub class is an ordinary (non-`delegate*`) managed class compiled directly into the test assembly in place of the real `InternalCalls.cs`, these must be ordinary `internal static unsafe` methods with matching signatures (`ulong id` in, `int` out; `ulong id, ulong* outBuffer, int bufferCapacity` in, `int` out):

Add this to the stub class body (alongside the existing `Log_*` methods and `Reset()`):

```csharp
        // ------------------------------------------------------------
        // Entity hierarchy fixture — lets tests set up parent/child
        // relationships without a live Coral host. Keyed by entity ID.
        // ------------------------------------------------------------
        internal static readonly Dictionary<ulong, List<ulong>> ChildrenByEntity = new();

        internal static int Entity_GetChildCount(ulong entityId)
        {
            return ChildrenByEntity.TryGetValue(entityId, out var kids) ? kids.Count : 0;
        }

        internal static unsafe int Entity_GetChildren(ulong entityId, ulong* outBuffer, int bufferCapacity)
        {
            if (outBuffer == null || bufferCapacity <= 0)
            {
                return 0;
            }
            if (!ChildrenByEntity.TryGetValue(entityId, out var kids))
            {
                return 0;
            }

            int writeCount = Math.Min(kids.Count, bufferCapacity);
            for (int i = 0; i < writeCount; i++)
            {
                outBuffer[i] = kids[i];
            }
            return writeCount;
        }
```

If the stub file's `Reset()` helper clears the log lists, extend it to also clear the new fixture so tests stay isolated:

```csharp
        internal static void Reset()
        {
            InfoLogs.Clear();
            WarningLogs.Clear();
            ErrorLogs.Clear();
            ChildrenByEntity.Clear();
        }
```

(Match this against whatever `Reset()` actually contains — add the `ChildrenByEntity.Clear();` line alongside the existing `.Clear()` calls rather than replacing the whole method if it does more than shown here.)

Also confirm the stub file has `using System;` and `using System.Collections.Generic;` at the top; add them if missing, since `Dictionary<ulong, List<ulong>>` and `Math.Min` require both.

Note: `Entity.IsValid` (used at the top of `GetChildren()`, `Entity.cs:164`) itself calls `InternalCalls.Entity_IsValid(m_id)`, which is not yet in the stub. Read `Entity.cs`'s `IsValid` property to confirm which internal call it invokes, then add a matching stub method too, e.g.:

```csharp
        internal static readonly HashSet<ulong> ValidEntities = new();

        internal static Bool32 Entity_IsValid(ulong entityId)
        {
            return ValidEntities.Contains(entityId) ? (Bool32)true : (Bool32)false;
        }
```

Check the real `InternalCalls.cs` signature (`internal static delegate* unmanaged<ulong, Bool32> Entity_IsValid;`, confirmed at `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/InternalCalls.cs:38`) — `Bool32` is a `Coral.Managed.Interop` type. If the stub project already has that interop reference from Step 7, use `Bool32` as shown; if `Bool32`'s constructor/cast isn't accessible the same way in the stub context, use a plain `bool`-returning stub only if `Entity.cs`'s `IsValid` getter itself does the `Bool32`-to-`bool` conversion inline (read the property to confirm before deciding). Add `ValidEntities.Clear();` to `Reset()` as well.

- [ ] **Step 9: Write the xUnit test**

Create `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/EntityGetChildrenTests.cs`:

```csharp
/*
 * Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
 * For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
 *
 * SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
 *
 */

using System.Collections.Generic;
using FluentAssertions;
using O3DE;
using Xunit;

namespace O3DE.Core.Tests
{
    public class EntityGetChildrenTests
    {
        public EntityGetChildrenTests()
        {
            InternalCalls.Reset();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void GetChildren_ReturnsEmptyList_WhenEntityHasNoChildren()
        {
            InternalCalls.ValidEntities.Add(1);
            InternalCalls.ChildrenByEntity[1] = new List<ulong>();
            var entity = new Entity(1);

            var children = entity.GetChildren();

            children.Should().BeEmpty();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void GetChildren_ReturnsEmptyList_WhenEntityIsInvalid()
        {
            var entity = new Entity(999);

            var children = entity.GetChildren();

            children.Should().BeEmpty();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void GetChildren_ReturnsAllChildIds_InOrder()
        {
            InternalCalls.ValidEntities.Add(1);
            InternalCalls.ChildrenByEntity[1] = new List<ulong> { 10, 11, 12 };
            var entity = new Entity(1);

            var children = entity.GetChildren();

            children.Should().HaveCount(3);
            children[0].Equals(new Entity(10)).Should().BeTrue();
            children[1].Equals(new Entity(11)).Should().BeTrue();
            children[2].Equals(new Entity(12)).Should().BeTrue();
        }

        [Fact]
        public void GetChildren_SkipsInvalidIdSentinel_IfPresentInBuffer()
        {
            InternalCalls.ValidEntities.Add(1);
            InternalCalls.ChildrenByEntity[1] = new List<ulong> { 10, Entity.InvalidId, 12 };
            var entity = new Entity(1);

            var children = entity.GetChildren();

            children.Should().HaveCount(2);
        }

        [Fact]
        public void GetChildren_MakesExactlyOneChildCountCallAndOneBulkCall_NotOneCallPerChild()
        {
            InternalCalls.ValidEntities.Add(1);
            var manyChildren = new List<ulong>();
            for (ulong i = 0; i < 50; i++)
            {
                manyChildren.Add(100 + i);
            }
            InternalCalls.ChildrenByEntity[1] = manyChildren;
            var entity = new Entity(1);

            InternalCalls.GetChildrenCallCount = 0;
            var children = entity.GetChildren();

            children.Should().HaveCount(50);
            InternalCalls.GetChildrenCallCount.Should().Be(1);
        }
    }
}
```

The last test (`MakesExactlyOneChildCountCallAndOneBulkCall_NotOneCallPerChild`) asserts the actual perf fix — it fails against the old per-child-loop implementation (which would never call the new bulk method at all, `GetChildrenCallCount` would stay 0 while a correctness-only check wouldn't catch that the fast path is used) and passes against the new one. It requires a call counter in the stub. Add this to `InternalCallsStub.cs` alongside the other new members from Step 8:

```csharp
        internal static int GetChildrenCallCount;
```

and increment it inside the stub's `Entity_GetChildren` method from Step 8:

```csharp
        internal static unsafe int Entity_GetChildren(ulong entityId, ulong* outBuffer, int bufferCapacity)
        {
            GetChildrenCallCount++;
            if (outBuffer == null || bufferCapacity <= 0)
            {
                return 0;
            }
            if (!ChildrenByEntity.TryGetValue(entityId, out var kids))
            {
                return 0;
            }

            int writeCount = Math.Min(kids.Count, bufferCapacity);
            for (int i = 0; i < writeCount; i++)
            {
                outBuffer[i] = kids[i];
            }
            return writeCount;
        }
```

Add `GetChildrenCallCount = 0;` to `Reset()` too.

### Task 8: StackAllocator arena allocator for marshaling

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.h:31-45`
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.cpp:203-220`

- [ ] **Step 1: Read the current `StackAllocator` interface and every call site**

Current `StackAllocator` declaration, `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.h:31-45`:

```cpp
    class StackAllocator
    {
    public:
        StackAllocator() = default;
        ~StackAllocator();
        StackAllocator(const StackAllocator&) = delete;
        StackAllocator& operator=(const StackAllocator&) = delete;

        AZStd::string* AllocString();
        AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>* AllocBlittableBuffer(size_t bytes);

    private:
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::string*> m_strings;
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>*> m_buffers;
    };
```

Current implementation, `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.cpp:203-220`:

```cpp
    StackAllocator::~StackAllocator()
    {
        for (auto* s : m_strings) { delete s; }
        for (auto* b : m_buffers) { delete b; }
    }

    AZStd::string* StackAllocator::AllocString()
    {
        m_strings.push_back(new AZStd::string());
        return m_strings.back();
    }

    AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>* StackAllocator::AllocBlittableBuffer(size_t bytes)
    {
        auto* buf = new AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>(bytes);
        m_buffers.push_back(buf);
        return buf;
    }
```

Confirm every call site before touching anything:

```bash
grep -rn "AllocString\|AllocBlittableBuffer\|StackAllocator" Code/Source Code/Tests
```

Expected matches (already verified in this task's research):
- `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.h` — the class declaration and the `StackAllocator&` parameters on `JsonValueToBehaviorParameter` and `MarshalJsonArrayToArguments`.
- `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.cpp` — the implementation, plus the single call to `alloc.AllocString()` inside `MarshalStringJson` (line 148).
- `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp` — four call sites that each construct a local `Marshaling::StackAllocator marshalAlloc;` on the stack for the duration of one marshaling pass (lines 1467, 1965, 2186, 2429), then pass it by reference into `MarshalJsonArrayToArguments` / `JsonValueToBehaviorParameter`. None of these locals are copied, moved, stored past the call, or shared across calls — each dispatch gets its own fresh instance that is destroyed at the end of the enclosing scope.

Note that `AllocBlittableBuffer` has **zero call sites** anywhere in `Code/Source` today (only its own declaration/definition) — it is unused but part of the public interface and must be preserved with identical signature and semantics (returns a stable, non-moving pointer valid for the allocator's lifetime).

This confirms: (1) no caller needs to change, since none of them touch `m_strings`/`m_buffers` directly or rely on any behavior beyond "call `AllocString()`, get back a pointer that stays valid until the `StackAllocator` is destroyed"; (2) each `StackAllocator` instance's lifetime is exactly one marshaling pass (a handful of args, at most), so a modestly-sized inline arena will cover the overwhelming majority of calls without ever touching the heap fallback.

- [ ] **Step 2: Replace the class declaration with an arena-backed design**

Replace the class body in `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.h:31-45`:

```cpp
    /**
     * Stack allocator for transient string storage used while a
     * BehaviorArgument is being populated. The BehaviorContext invocation
     * machinery expects argument string buffers to outlive the call, but
     * not the surrounding scope - so we keep them in a flat arena that
     * dies with the marshaling pass.
     *
     * Modeled on EditorPythonBindings' Convert::StackVariableAllocator
     * (we don't reuse it directly because the EPB header isn't usable
     * outside that gem, and Phase 18-A.1 of the spec calls for this
     * helper to live independently so the runtime path doesn't depend
     * on EditorPythonBindings being loaded).
     *
     * Implementation: a fixed-size inline byte arena (bump allocator) is
     * used first for both AZStd::string and AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>
     * objects; the arena services the common case of a handful of small
     * marshaled arguments per call with zero heap traffic. Once the
     * inline arena is exhausted for a given instance (which spans
     * exactly one marshaling pass - see call sites in
     * GenericDispatcher.cpp, each of which constructs a StackAllocator
     * on the stack immediately before one MarshalJsonArrayToArguments /
     * JsonValueToBehaviorParameter call and lets it fall out of scope
     * right after), subsequent allocations fall back to individual heap
     * allocations tracked in m_heapStrings/m_heapBuffers, exactly like
     * the old implementation, so correctness never depends on staying
     * under the inline budget.
     */
    class StackAllocator
    {
    public:
        // Inline arena size in bytes. Sized for the common case: most
        // marshaled calls pass a handful of short strings (entity names,
        // ids-as-strings, small labels) or small blittable buffers. 512
        // bytes covers e.g. 8 AZStd::string objects (avg ~40 bytes each
        // incl. SSO payload and alignment) or a couple of small binary
        // buffers, per marshaling pass, before falling back to heap.
        static constexpr size_t kInlineArenaBytes = 512;

        StackAllocator() = default;
        ~StackAllocator();
        StackAllocator(const StackAllocator&) = delete;
        StackAllocator& operator=(const StackAllocator&) = delete;

        AZStd::string* AllocString();
        AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>* AllocBlittableBuffer(size_t bytes);

    private:
        // Bump-allocates `bytes` (aligned to `alignment`) out of the
        // inline arena. Returns nullptr if the arena doesn't have enough
        // room left, in which case the caller falls back to heap.
        void* BumpAlloc(size_t bytes, size_t alignment);

        alignas(alignof(AZStd::max_align_t)) AZStd::array<AZ::u8, kInlineArenaBytes> m_arena;
        size_t m_arenaOffset = 0;

        // Objects placement-new'd into m_arena. Tracked so the
        // destructor can call their destructors explicitly (placement
        // new means the arena's raw bytes don't run destructors on
        // their own).
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::string*> m_arenaStrings;
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>*> m_arenaBuffers;

        // Heap fallback for allocations that don't fit in the inline
        // arena. Same ownership model as the original implementation:
        // plain `new`, `delete`d in the destructor.
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::string*> m_heapStrings;
        AZStd::vector<AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>*> m_heapBuffers;
    };
```

Add the one new include this needs — `<AzCore/std/containers/array.h>` — alongside the existing includes at the top of the header:

```cpp
#include <AzCore/RTTI/BehaviorContext.h>
#include <AzCore/std/containers/array.h>
#include <AzCore/std/containers/vector.h>
#include <AzCore/std/string/string.h>
#include <AzCore/JSON/document.h>
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Replace the implementation with the real bump-allocator logic**

Replace `Code/Source/Scripting/Marshaling/BehaviorContextMarshaling.cpp:203-220` with:

```cpp
    StackAllocator::~StackAllocator()
    {
        // Arena-backed objects were placement-new'd into m_arena's raw
        // bytes, so they need an explicit destructor call; their storage
        // itself is reclaimed for free when m_arena (a member array)
        // goes out of scope.
        for (auto* s : m_arenaStrings) { s->~basic_string(); }
        for (auto* b : m_arenaBuffers) { b->~vector(); }

        // Heap-fallback objects own their storage via plain `new` and
        // need both destruction and deallocation.
        for (auto* s : m_heapStrings) { delete s; }
        for (auto* b : m_heapBuffers) { delete b; }
    }

    void* StackAllocator::BumpAlloc(size_t bytes, size_t alignment)
    {
        // Round the current offset up to the requested alignment.
        const size_t misalignment = m_arenaOffset % alignment;
        const size_t alignedOffset = misalignment == 0
            ? m_arenaOffset
            : m_arenaOffset + (alignment - misalignment);

        if (alignedOffset + bytes > m_arena.size())
        {
            return nullptr; // exhausted - caller falls back to heap
        }

        void* ptr = m_arena.data() + alignedOffset;
        m_arenaOffset = alignedOffset + bytes;
        return ptr;
    }

    AZStd::string* StackAllocator::AllocString()
    {
        if (void* mem = BumpAlloc(sizeof(AZStd::string), alignof(AZStd::string)))
        {
            auto* s = new (mem) AZStd::string();
            m_arenaStrings.push_back(s);
            return s;
        }
        // Arena exhausted for this marshaling pass - fall back to heap,
        // same as the original always-heap implementation.
        m_heapStrings.push_back(new AZStd::string());
        return m_heapStrings.back();
    }

    AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>* StackAllocator::AllocBlittableBuffer(size_t bytes)
    {
        if (void* mem = BumpAlloc(sizeof(AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>), alignof(AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>)))
        {
            // The AZStd::vector<AZ::u8> control block is placed in the
            // arena, but its `bytes`-sized backing storage is still a
            // separate heap allocation performed by the vector itself
            // (AZStd::vector always owns heap storage for its elements -
            // there is no small-buffer optimization to preserve here).
            // What we've saved versus the old implementation is the
            // `new AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>` control-block allocation
            // itself, which is the per-call overhead this task targets.
            auto* buf = new (mem) AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>(bytes);
            m_arenaBuffers.push_back(buf);
            return buf;
        }
        auto* buf = new AZStd::vector<AZ::u8>(bytes);
        m_heapBuffers.push_back(buf);
        return buf;
    }
```



### Task 9: Cache resolved Coral::Type* in ForwardEventToManaged

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp:1775-1780` (struct `ManagedEBusProxy`)
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp:1838-1912` (function `ForwardEventToManaged`)
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp:2676-2692` (event-hook installation loop inside `RegisterEBusHandler`)

- [ ] **Step 1: Read the current code to confirm line numbers before editing**

Open `Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp` and confirm these three spots still match (the file may have shifted slightly since this plan was written; search for the literal strings below rather than trusting line numbers blindly):

Current `ManagedEBusProxy` struct (around line 1775):

```cpp
            struct ManagedEBusProxy
            {
                AZ::BehaviorEBus* bus = nullptr;
                AZ::BehaviorEBusHandler* handler = nullptr;
                int64_t managedToken = 0;
            };
```

Current `ForwardEventToManaged` function (around line 1838):

```cpp
            void ForwardEventToManaged(
                void* userData,
                const char* eventName,
                int eventIndex,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* /*result*/,
                int numParameters,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* parameters)
            {
                AZ_UNUSED(eventIndex);
                const int64_t token = static_cast<int64_t>(reinterpret_cast<uintptr_t>(userData));
                if (token == 0) return;

                // Build the args JSON array. Each parameter goes through
                // BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue which handles all the
                // primitive + math marshaling we've already shipped.
                rapidjson::Document argsDoc;
                argsDoc.SetArray();
                for (int i = 0; i < numParameters; ++i)
                {
                    rapidjson::Value v;
                    AZStd::string marshalErr;
                    if (!Marshaling::BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue(
                            parameters[i], v, argsDoc.GetAllocator(), marshalErr))
                    {
                        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                            "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): arg[%d] marshal failed: %s - skipping handler call",
                            eventName, i, marshalErr.c_str());
                        return;
                    }
                    argsDoc.PushBack(v, argsDoc.GetAllocator());
                }

                rapidjson::StringBuffer buffer;
                rapidjson::Writer<rapidjson::StringBuffer> writer(buffer);
                argsDoc.Accept(writer);
                const char* argsJson = buffer.GetString();

                // Invoke EBusHandlerRegistry.DispatchEvent via Coral.
                // We need the CoralHostManager to resolve the static
                // method; if it's not available (gem teardown), the
                // event is dropped (logged at the warning level).
                ICoralHostManager* hostMgr = CoralHostManagerInterface::Get();
                if (hostMgr == nullptr)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): CoralHostManager unavailable; dropping event",
                        eventName);
                    return;
                }
                Coral::Type* registryType = hostMgr->GetCoreType("O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry");
                if (registryType == nullptr)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry type not found; dropping event",
                        eventName);
                    return;
                }
                // DispatchEvent(long token, string eventName, string argsJson) -> string?
                // Coral::Type::InvokeStaticMethod marshals string + long
                // arguments via its built-in primitive support.
                Coral::ScopedString eventNameStr = Coral::String::New(eventName);
                Coral::ScopedString argsJsonStr = Coral::String::New(argsJson);
                try
                {
                    registryType->InvokeStaticMethod(
                        "DispatchEvent", token, eventNameStr, argsJsonStr);
                }
                catch (...)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): exception from managed DispatchEvent; "
                        "event dropped",
                        eventName);
                }
            }
```

Current hook-installation loop inside `RegisterEBusHandler` (around line 2676):

```cpp
            // Install our generic hook on every event the handler
            // exposes. userData carries the managed token (cast via
            // uintptr_t since BehaviorEBusHandler typedefs userData
            // as void*).
            void* userData = reinterpret_cast<void*>(static_cast<uintptr_t>(managedToken));
            for (const auto& evt : handler->GetEvents())
            {
                if (!handler->InstallGenericHook(
                        evt.m_name, &ForwardEventToManaged, userData))
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "RegisterEBusHandler(token=%lld): InstallGenericHook failed for event '%s' on bus '%s'",
                        static_cast<long long>(managedToken), evt.m_name, busNameStr.c_str());
                    // Continue with the other events - partial hook
                    // installation is still useful.
                }
            }
```

If line numbers differ from those cited, locate these blocks by searching for `struct ManagedEBusProxy`, `void ForwardEventToManaged(`, and `void* userData = reinterpret_cast<void*>` respectively, and proceed using the real locations.

- [ ] **Step 2: Add a cached `Coral::Type*` field to `ManagedEBusProxy` and change the hook's `userData` to carry the proxy pointer instead of the bare token**

`ForwardEventToManaged` is installed as a plain C-style function pointer (`AZ::BehaviorEBusHandler::InstallGenericHook` takes a `GenericHookType` free-function pointer, not a `std::function`, so no per-registration capture is possible — the only per-registration context it can see is the single `void* userData` set once at install time). `ManagedEBusProxy` is heap-allocated via `AZStd::make_unique` and stored in `s_managedHandlers`; on unregister, `s_managedHandlers.Release()` moves the `unique_ptr` out of the map into a local before `handler->Disconnect()` is called, so the `ManagedEBusProxy` object's address stays valid for the entire time the hook could still fire — making `proxy.get()` a safe, stable value to pass as `userData` instead of re-encoding the bare token.

Because the proxy is per-registration (one per `RegisterEBusHandler` call) and never re-registered with a new type at a different address, caching the resolved `Coral::Type*` directly on the proxy — populated once when the hook is installed — is the least-disruptive option: it needs no new global map, no extra locking, and reuses a struct that already exists solely to carry per-registration state.

Replace the `ManagedEBusProxy` struct:

```cpp
            struct ManagedEBusProxy
            {
                AZ::BehaviorEBus* bus = nullptr;
                AZ::BehaviorEBusHandler* handler = nullptr;
                int64_t managedToken = 0;
            };
```

with:

```cpp
            struct ManagedEBusProxy
            {
                AZ::BehaviorEBus* bus = nullptr;
                AZ::BehaviorEBusHandler* handler = nullptr;
                int64_t managedToken = 0;

                // Perf: resolved once (lazily, on first event fire) and
                // reused for every subsequent event on this handler -
                // avoids re-doing CoralHostManager's string-keyed
                // m_coreTypeCache lookup (plus a fresh AZStd::string
                // construction from the literal) on every single event
                // dispatch. Populated by ForwardEventToManaged the first
                // time this proxy forwards an event; nullptr until then.
                Coral::Type* cachedRegistryType = nullptr;
            };
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Rewrite `ForwardEventToManaged` to take the proxy pointer and memoize the type lookup on it**

Replace the entire function:

```cpp
            void ForwardEventToManaged(
                void* userData,
                const char* eventName,
                int eventIndex,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* /*result*/,
                int numParameters,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* parameters)
            {
                AZ_UNUSED(eventIndex);
                const int64_t token = static_cast<int64_t>(reinterpret_cast<uintptr_t>(userData));
                if (token == 0) return;

                // Build the args JSON array. Each parameter goes through
                // BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue which handles all the
                // primitive + math marshaling we've already shipped.
                rapidjson::Document argsDoc;
                argsDoc.SetArray();
                for (int i = 0; i < numParameters; ++i)
                {
                    rapidjson::Value v;
                    AZStd::string marshalErr;
                    if (!Marshaling::BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue(
                            parameters[i], v, argsDoc.GetAllocator(), marshalErr))
                    {
                        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                            "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): arg[%d] marshal failed: %s - skipping handler call",
                            eventName, i, marshalErr.c_str());
                        return;
                    }
                    argsDoc.PushBack(v, argsDoc.GetAllocator());
                }

                rapidjson::StringBuffer buffer;
                rapidjson::Writer<rapidjson::StringBuffer> writer(buffer);
                argsDoc.Accept(writer);
                const char* argsJson = buffer.GetString();

                // Invoke EBusHandlerRegistry.DispatchEvent via Coral.
                // We need the CoralHostManager to resolve the static
                // method; if it's not available (gem teardown), the
                // event is dropped (logged at the warning level).
                ICoralHostManager* hostMgr = CoralHostManagerInterface::Get();
                if (hostMgr == nullptr)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): CoralHostManager unavailable; dropping event",
                        eventName);
                    return;
                }
                Coral::Type* registryType = hostMgr->GetCoreType("O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry");
                if (registryType == nullptr)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry type not found; dropping event",
                        eventName);
                    return;
                }
                // DispatchEvent(long token, string eventName, string argsJson) -> string?
                // Coral::Type::InvokeStaticMethod marshals string + long
                // arguments via its built-in primitive support.
                Coral::ScopedString eventNameStr = Coral::String::New(eventName);
                Coral::ScopedString argsJsonStr = Coral::String::New(argsJson);
                try
                {
                    registryType->InvokeStaticMethod(
                        "DispatchEvent", token, eventNameStr, argsJsonStr);
                }
                catch (...)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): exception from managed DispatchEvent; "
                        "event dropped",
                        eventName);
                }
            }
```

with:

```cpp
            void ForwardEventToManaged(
                void* userData,
                const char* eventName,
                int eventIndex,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* /*result*/,
                int numParameters,
                AZ::BehaviorArgument* parameters)
            {
                AZ_UNUSED(eventIndex);
                ManagedEBusProxy* proxy = static_cast<ManagedEBusProxy*>(userData);
                if (proxy == nullptr || proxy->managedToken == 0) return;
                const int64_t token = proxy->managedToken;

                // Build the args JSON array. Each parameter goes through
                // BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue which handles all the
                // primitive + math marshaling we've already shipped.
                rapidjson::Document argsDoc;
                argsDoc.SetArray();
                for (int i = 0; i < numParameters; ++i)
                {
                    rapidjson::Value v;
                    AZStd::string marshalErr;
                    if (!Marshaling::BehaviorArgumentToJsonValue(
                            parameters[i], v, argsDoc.GetAllocator(), marshalErr))
                    {
                        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                            "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): arg[%d] marshal failed: %s - skipping handler call",
                            eventName, i, marshalErr.c_str());
                        return;
                    }
                    argsDoc.PushBack(v, argsDoc.GetAllocator());
                }

                rapidjson::StringBuffer buffer;
                rapidjson::Writer<rapidjson::StringBuffer> writer(buffer);
                argsDoc.Accept(writer);
                const char* argsJson = buffer.GetString();

                // Resolve EBusHandlerRegistry's Coral::Type once per
                // registration and cache it on the proxy. Previously this
                // called CoralHostManager::GetCoreType (a string-keyed
                // hashmap lookup plus a fresh AZStd::string construction
                // from the "O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry" literal)
                // on EVERY event fire, even though the type can never
                // change once resolved for a given handler registration.
                Coral::Type* registryType = proxy->cachedRegistryType;
                if (registryType == nullptr)
                {
                    ICoralHostManager* hostMgr = CoralHostManagerInterface::Get();
                    if (hostMgr == nullptr)
                    {
                        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                            "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): CoralHostManager unavailable; dropping event",
                            eventName);
                        return;
                    }
                    registryType = hostMgr->GetCoreType("O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry");
                    if (registryType == nullptr)
                    {
                        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                            "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry type not found; dropping event",
                            eventName);
                        return;
                    }
                    proxy->cachedRegistryType = registryType;
                }
                // DispatchEvent(long token, string eventName, string argsJson) -> string?
                // Coral::Type::InvokeStaticMethod marshals string + long
                // arguments via its built-in primitive support.
                Coral::ScopedString eventNameStr = Coral::String::New(eventName);
                Coral::ScopedString argsJsonStr = Coral::String::New(argsJson);
                try
                {
                    registryType->InvokeStaticMethod(
                        "DispatchEvent", token, eventNameStr, argsJsonStr);
                }
                catch (...)
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "ForwardEventToManaged('%s'): exception from managed DispatchEvent; "
                        "event dropped",
                        eventName);
                }
            }
```

Note: `proxy->cachedRegistryType` is written without a lock. This is safe because a given `ManagedEBusProxy` only receives event callbacks that originate from its own bus connection, and `AZ::BehaviorEBusHandler` (per O3DE's EBus contract) delivers its generic-hook callbacks on the thread(s) that broadcast the bus event — the same threading model that already applied before this change (the old code had no per-proxy state at all, so there was nothing to race on; the new `cachedRegistryType` field is written at most idempotently — every writer computes the same pointer value from the same process-wide core assembly, so even a benign data race on first-populate would only ever store the same value twice, never a torn or inconsistent one).

- [ ] **Step 4: Update the hook-installation call site in `RegisterEBusHandler` to pass the proxy pointer**

The proxy must exist before the hook is installed, since the hook's `userData` now needs the proxy's address. The current code builds the `AZStd::unique_ptr<ManagedEBusProxy>` named `proxy` AFTER the hook-install loop (it's constructed further down, right before `s_managedHandlers.Register`). Move the proxy construction earlier so the hook can be installed against a live `ManagedEBusProxy*`.

Current code (the hook-install loop, followed later by proxy construction — shown together for context; they are ~50 lines apart in the file):

```cpp
            // Install our generic hook on every event the handler
            // exposes. userData carries the managed token (cast via
            // uintptr_t since BehaviorEBusHandler typedefs userData
            // as void*).
            void* userData = reinterpret_cast<void*>(static_cast<uintptr_t>(managedToken));
            for (const auto& evt : handler->GetEvents())
            {
                if (!handler->InstallGenericHook(
                        evt.m_name, &ForwardEventToManaged, userData))
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "RegisterEBusHandler(token=%lld): InstallGenericHook failed for event '%s' on bus '%s'",
                        static_cast<long long>(managedToken), evt.m_name, busNameStr.c_str());
                    // Continue with the other events - partial hook
                    // installation is still useful.
                }
            }
```

and, later in the same function:

```cpp
            // Register in the managed-handler table so Unregister can
            // find it and disconnect cleanly.
            auto proxy = AZStd::make_unique<ManagedEBusProxy>();
            proxy->bus = bus;
            proxy->handler = handler;
            proxy->managedToken = managedToken;
            if (!s_managedHandlers.Register(managedToken, AZStd::move(proxy)))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                    "RegisterEBusHandler(token=%lld): duplicate token; rolling back",
                    static_cast<long long>(managedToken));
                handler->Disconnect();
                bus->m_destroyHandler->Call(&handlerResult, 1, nullptr);
                return 0;
            }
```

Replace the hook-install loop with:

```cpp
            // Allocate the proxy up front (before installing hooks) so
            // its stable heap address can be handed to InstallGenericHook
            // as userData. The proxy carries the managed token AND (once
            // populated on first event fire) the cached Coral::Type* for
            // EBusHandlerRegistry, so ForwardEventToManaged never needs
            // to re-resolve the type by name after the first event.
            auto proxy = AZStd::make_unique<ManagedEBusProxy>();
            proxy->bus = bus;
            proxy->handler = handler;
            proxy->managedToken = managedToken;

            // Install our generic hook on every event the handler
            // exposes. userData carries a pointer to the ManagedEBusProxy
            // itself (stable for the proxy's lifetime - see the
            // ManagedHandlerTable::Release ordering in
            // UnregisterEBusHandler, which disconnects the handler before
            // the proxy's unique_ptr goes out of scope).
            void* userData = proxy.get();
            for (const auto& evt : handler->GetEvents())
            {
                if (!handler->InstallGenericHook(
                        evt.m_name, &ForwardEventToManaged, userData))
                {
                    AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                        "RegisterEBusHandler(token=%lld): InstallGenericHook failed for event '%s' on bus '%s'",
                        static_cast<long long>(managedToken), evt.m_name, busNameStr.c_str());
                    // Continue with the other events - partial hook
                    // installation is still useful.
                }
            }
```

Replace the later proxy-construction block with:

```cpp
            // Register in the managed-handler table so Unregister can
            // find it and disconnect cleanly.
            if (!s_managedHandlers.Register(managedToken, AZStd::move(proxy)))
            {
                AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
                    "RegisterEBusHandler(token=%lld): duplicate token; rolling back",
                    static_cast<long long>(managedToken));
                handler->Disconnect();
                bus->m_destroyHandler->Call(&handlerResult, 1, nullptr);
                return 0;
            }
```

After this edit, verify the connect-failure rollback path slightly earlier in the same function (the `if (!connected)` block, ~15 lines above "Register in the managed-handler table") still compiles: it calls `bus->m_destroyHandler->Call(&handlerResult, 1, nullptr)` and returns 0 WITHOUT touching `proxy` — that is fine, since `proxy` (now declared earlier, before the connect attempt) simply goes out of scope and is destroyed normally when the function returns in that branch, which is the same cleanup behavior as before (it previously wasn't constructed yet at that point; now it is constructed but unused on that path, which is harmless — the hooks were already installed on `handler` regardless of `Connect` outcome in the pre-existing code, so this is not a behavior change).

```bash
git add Code/Source/Scripting/Reflection/GenericDispatcher.cpp
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Perf: cache resolved Coral::Type* in ForwardEventToManaged

ForwardEventToManaged previously re-resolved the
O3DE.Reflection.EBusHandlerRegistry Coral::Type via
CoralHostManager::GetCoreType (a string-keyed hashmap lookup plus a
fresh AZStd::string construction) on every single EBus event fire,
even though the type never changes after a handler is registered.
Change userData from the bare managed token to a pointer to the
ManagedEBusProxy itself, and memoize the resolved Coral::Type* on
```
