---

### Task 10: CoralHostManager — separate user/core AssemblyLoadContexts for hot-reload

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.h:185-209`
- Modify: `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp:194-246` (`Initialize`), `:248-275` (`Shutdown`), `:304-371` (`ReloadUserAssemblies`)
- Modify: `Code/Include/O3DESharp/O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h:19-36` (doc comment only, once the fix lands)
- No new automated test project — this requires a live Coral/.NET-hosted O3DE Editor session (see rules in the plan header). Verification is a manual checklist plus a build-verification step, both below.

**Context you must hold in your head before touching code:**

`CoralHostManager` currently uses a **single unified `Coral::AssemblyLoadContext`** for both O3DE.Core and every user assembly. The two member variables `m_coreContext` and `m_userContext` (declared separately in the header, as if they were independent) are made to alias the same underlying context by a plain assignment in `Initialize`:

```cpp
// CoralHostManager.cpp:199-203 (current)
m_coreContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DEContext");

// User context is the same as core context - single unified context
// This pointer alias simplifies code that expects separate contexts
m_userContext = m_coreContext;
```

`Coral::AssemblyLoadContext` is a copyable value-type handle (that's why `operator=` above compiles and behaves as an alias, not a deep copy) — treat it as an opaque handle around a CoreCLR `AssemblyLoadContext`, not as owning storage itself.

The consequence lives in `ReloadUserAssemblies` (`CoralHostManager.cpp:304-371`): every single reload — even one triggered by nothing but a user editing their own script — unloads the **entire** unified context, which means:
1. `m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_coreContext)` at line 334 tears down O3DE.Core along with the user assemblies.
2. `LoadCoreAssembly()` at line 344 reloads and re-JITs all of O3DE.Core from disk.
3. `RegisterInternalCalls()` at line 351 re-runs `ScriptBindings::RegisterAll` and `Generated::RegisterBindings` — re-populating every static internal-call function-pointer field on the C# side, for a class of ~functions that didn't change at all.
4. `m_coreTypeCache` is cleared and every previously-cached `Coral::Type*` for O3DE.Core types becomes stale, forcing every consumer to re-resolve on next use.

The comment block in `Code/Include/O3DESharp/O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h:19-36` documents **why** this was done this way historically — it cites two separate reasons, not one:
> "Coral can't easily separate the contexts (per the comment in `CoralHostManager::Initialize`: Coral uses MemoryMappedFile which locks DLLs, **and cross-context type resolution is not in this Coral version**)"

Both halves of that sentence are load-bearing and you must verify both before choosing a fix:

- **File-locking half:** Coral loads assemblies via `MemoryMappedFile`, which holds an OS-level lock on the backing `.dll` file for as long as it's mapped. If you tried to create a genuinely independent, unloadable user `AssemblyLoadContext` today, this by itself is *not* actually the blocker between core and user — `O3DE.Core.dll` and the user assembly(ies) under `Bin/Scripts/` are different files on disk, so loading them into two different contexts doesn't collide on the same inode. The locking problem that *does* exist is narrower: it prevents reloading the *same* user assembly file in place after a rebuild while any old mapping of that exact file is still alive (e.g. if a previous unload hasn't fully released its memory-mapped view yet, or a build tries to overwrite the file while Coral still has it mapped). That's a real, separate risk worth defending against regardless of what you do with core/user separation — fix it with a shadow-copy strategy (below).
- **Cross-context type-identity half — this is the actual reason core and user were unified, and it is a real constraint you must respect.** `.NET` does not unify type identity across `AssemblyLoadContext`s by default: if `O3DE.Core.dll` were loaded a second, independent time into its own ALC, `typeof(O3DE.Core.Vector3)` loaded there is a **different runtime type** from the one loaded into the original "core" context, even though it's the same source assembly. Verify this constraint is real for this codebase before proceeding: user scripts directly consume O3DE.Core types by reference. For example, `Assets/Scripts/Examples/ReflectionExample.cs` and every real user script reference O3DE.Core types (`EntityId`, `Vector3`, base script classes, etc.) directly — if the user ALC resolved its own independent copy of `O3DE.Core.dll` instead of reusing the assembly already loaded into the core ALC, every native-to-managed marshaling boundary that hands a `Coral::Type*`/`Coral::ManagedObject` resolved against the *core* copy of a type to code running against the *user* ALC's copy of that same type would silently either fail type checks or, worse, appear to work while being unsound. `CSharpScriptComponent::CreateScriptInstance` (`Code/Source/Scripting/CSharpScriptComponent.cpp:561-566`) explicitly falls back from `GetUserType` to `GetCoreType` for the same class name lookup — meaning a "user" script class can literally *be* a type resolved out of the core assembly. This fallback must keep working after your change.

**The fix (do this, in order — do not skip the verification step):**

- [ ] **Step 0 (mandatory go/no-go gate before writing any implementation code) — verify the assembly-resolution mechanism the installed Coral version actually exposes.**

Before writing a single line of the fix, confirm what `Coral::AssemblyLoadContext` / `Coral::HostInstance` actually expose for cross-context assembly resolution, because the whole plan below hinges on being able to make the **user** ALC transparently resolve `O3DE.Core` assembly references against the assembly already loaded in the **core** ALC, rather than loading its own independent copy.

1. Locate the vendored Coral source. It is not checked into this repo; it's pulled by CMake `FetchContent` (see `Code/CMakeLists.txt:36-138`, `CORAL_GIT_REPO = https://github.com/WatchDogStudios/Coral.git`, target `Coral.Native`). After a normal CMake configure, the checked-out source will be under your build directory's FetchContent subdirectory, typically `<your-cmake-build-dir>/_deps/coral-src/`. Find `Coral.Native/Include/Coral/AssemblyLoadContext.hpp` and `Coral.Native/Include/Coral/HostInstance.hpp` there.
2. Read `AssemblyLoadContext::LoadAssembly` and `HostInstance::CreateAssemblyLoadContext` in full. Confirm whether:
   - (a) Coral's managed side (`Coral.Managed`, a separate FetchContent'd/built assembly, same repo) implements an `AssemblyLoadContext.Resolving` handler (or equivalent) that lets one ALC delegate unresolved assembly-reference resolution to another already-created ALC's loaded assemblies, or
   - (b) there is no such mechanism, and every `AssemblyLoadContext::LoadAssembly` call always does an independent `Assembly.LoadFromStream`/`LoadFromAssemblyPath`-style load with no cross-ALC delegation.
3. **If (a) is available:** proceed to Step 1 below — you can create a genuinely separate, independently-unloadable user ALC and configure it (via whatever Coral API surfaces this — likely a parameter on `CreateAssemblyLoadContext`, or a call you must add to Coral itself since it's a git submodule/FetchContent you control per `Code/CMakeLists.txt:53-82`'s support for a local Coral fork checkout) to resolve `O3DE.Core` references against the core ALC's already-loaded assembly instead of loading its own copy.
4. **If (b) is confirmed (no such mechanism exists in current Coral) and you cannot cheaply add one to the Coral fork** (`O3DESHARP_CORAL_SOURCE_DIR` / the `../../Coral-O3DESharp` local-checkout convention in `Code/CMakeLists.txt:53-82` exists exactly so you *can* patch Coral itself if needed — this is in scope, not off-limits, but treat it as the escalation path, not the default) — **STOP. Do not proceed with full ALC separation.** This is more invasive than scoped. Do the following instead:
   - Commit nothing broken. If you've made any exploratory edits, discard them (`git checkout -- Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.h`) or stash them out of the working tree.
   - Flag back to the maintainer (mikaelamanfo@wdstudios.tech) with a concrete summary: what Coral's `AssemblyLoadContext` currently supports, why true separation requires a Coral-side change, and a size estimate for that Coral-side change if attempted.
   - Recommend deferring this specific item (Task 10 / item 10 in `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-01-1.2.0-ux-perf-audit-design.md`) to a 1.2.1 patch, per that spec's own "Open questions / risks" section, which explicitly anticipates this outcome. The other 18 items in the 1.2.0 release are independent of this one and are unaffected by deferring it.
   - Do not implement a partial/unsound version (e.g. separating the contexts but silently accepting that core-typed objects crossing the boundary might be unsound) merely to claim the item done. An unsound fix here is worse than the current known-slow-but-correct behavior.

The remaining steps assume Step 0 concluded that cross-context resolution is achievable (case (a), or a Coral-fork patch you've implemented and validated in isolation first with a small throwaway C++ test program that creates two ALCs, loads the same assembly's types in each, and confirms `Coral::Type` handles resolved through the delegating path compare equal / behave identically to the direct load — do this validation *before* wiring it into `CoralHostManager`).

- [ ] **Step 1: Add a shadow-copy helper for assembly loading**

This addresses the genuinely-confirmed half of the problem (file-locking on rebuild-and-reload of the *same* file) regardless of which context it's loaded into, and is required groundwork for making the user context safely unloadable/reloadable in place.

Read the current top of `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp` (lines 1-40) — note it already includes `<filesystem>` and AZCore's `AzCore/IO/Path/Path.h`, `AzCore/IO/FileIO.h`, `AzCore/Utils/Utils.h`. Add the shadow-copy helper as a private static method. First, declare it in `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.h`. Current private section (lines 163-183):

```cpp
    private:
        // Coral message callback for logging
        static void CoralMessageCallback(std::string_view message, Coral::MessageLevel level);
        
        // Coral exception callback
        static void CoralExceptionCallback(std::string_view message);

        // Load the core O3DE API assembly
        bool LoadCoreAssembly();

        // Load every user game assembly listed in the config (legacy userAssemblyPath
        // plus everything in userAssemblyPaths). Returns true if at least one assembly
        // was loaded successfully, or if no user assemblies were configured.
        bool LoadUserAssemblies();

        // Legacy single-assembly variant. Loads m_config.userAssemblyPath.
        // Prefer LoadUserAssemblies() in new code.
        bool LoadUserAssembly();

        // Register all internal calls (C++ functions callable from C#)
        void RegisterInternalCalls();
```

Replace with:

```cpp
    private:
        // Coral message callback for logging
        static void CoralMessageCallback(std::string_view message, Coral::MessageLevel level);
        
        // Coral exception callback
        static void CoralExceptionCallback(std::string_view message);

        // Load the core O3DE API assembly
        bool LoadCoreAssembly();

        // Load every user game assembly listed in the config (legacy userAssemblyPath
        // plus everything in userAssemblyPaths). Returns true if at least one assembly
        // was loaded successfully, or if no user assemblies were configured.
        bool LoadUserAssemblies();

        // Legacy single-assembly variant. Loads m_config.userAssemblyPath.
        // Prefer LoadUserAssemblies() in new code.
        bool LoadUserAssembly();

        // Register all internal calls (C++ functions callable from C#)
        void RegisterInternalCalls();

        // Copies sourcePath (and its .pdb, if present) into m_shadowCopyDirectory
        // under a unique, monotonically-increasing generation suffix, then returns
        // the path to the copy. Coral loads assemblies via MemoryMappedFile, which
        // holds an OS-level lock on the backing file for as long as it's mapped;
        // loading a shadow copy instead of the original lets a subsequent build
        // overwrite the original file (e.g. Bin/Scripts/MyGame.dll) while the
        // previous generation's mapped copy is still alive in a not-yet-unloaded
        // ALC, and lets us actually unload+reload the user ALC without racing the
        // file system. Returns an empty string on copy failure (caller should fall
        // back to loading sourcePath directly and log a warning).
        AZStd::string ShadowCopyAssembly(const AZStd::string& sourcePath);
```

Now implement it in `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp`. Insert this new method immediately before `bool CoralHostManager::LoadUserAssemblies()` (currently starting at line 518):

```cpp
    AZStd::string CoralHostManager::ShadowCopyAssembly(const AZStd::string& sourcePath)
    {
        std::filesystem::path source(sourcePath.c_str());
        std::error_code ec;
        if (!std::filesystem::exists(source, ec) || ec)
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager: ShadowCopyAssembly - source does not exist: %s", sourcePath.c_str());
            return AZStd::string();
        }

        if (m_shadowCopyDirectory.empty())
        {
            AZ::IO::FixedMaxPath projectPath = AZ::Utils::GetProjectPath();
            AZ::IO::FixedMaxPath shadowDir = projectPath / "user" / "O3DESharpShadowCopies";
            m_shadowCopyDirectory = shadowDir.c_str();
        }

        std::filesystem::path shadowDir(m_shadowCopyDirectory.c_str());
        std::filesystem::create_directories(shadowDir, ec);
        if (ec)
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR(
                "CoralHostManager: ShadowCopyAssembly - failed to create shadow directory '%s': %s",
                m_shadowCopyDirectory.c_str(), ec.message().c_str());
            return AZStd::string();
        }

        // Monotonically increasing generation counter avoids re-colliding with a
        // previous generation's copy that Coral may still have memory-mapped
        // (its ALC may not have finished unloading yet - CoreCLR ALC unload is
        // not guaranteed synchronous with UnloadAssemblyLoadContext returning).
        const AZ::u64 generation = m_shadowCopyGeneration++;

        const std::string stem = source.stem().string();
        const std::string ext = source.extension().string();
        std::filesystem::path destination = shadowDir /
            (stem + "_gen" + std::to_string(generation) + ext);

        std::filesystem::copy_file(
            source, destination, std::filesystem::copy_options::overwrite_existing, ec);
        if (ec)
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR(
                "CoralHostManager: ShadowCopyAssembly - failed to copy '%s' to '%s': %s",
                sourcePath.c_str(), destination.string().c_str(), ec.message().c_str());
            return AZStd::string();
        }

        // Best-effort: copy the .pdb alongside it too, so debuggers can still
        // symbolicate the shadow-copied assembly. Not fatal if missing/fails.
        std::filesystem::path sourcePdb = source;
        sourcePdb.replace_extension(".pdb");
        if (std::filesystem::exists(sourcePdb, ec) && !ec)
        {
            std::filesystem::path destinationPdb = destination;
            destinationPdb.replace_extension(".pdb");
            std::error_code pdbEc;
            std::filesystem::copy_file(
                sourcePdb, destinationPdb, std::filesystem::copy_options::overwrite_existing, pdbEc);
            // Ignore pdbEc - missing/failed PDB copy only affects debuggability, not correctness.
        }

        AZLOG_INFO(
            "CoralHostManager: Shadow-copied '%s' to '%s' (generation %llu)",
            sourcePath.c_str(), destination.string().c_str(), generation);

        return AZStd::string(destination.string().c_str());
    }
```

Add the two new private fields (`m_shadowCopyDirectory`, `m_shadowCopyGeneration`) to `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.h`'s private data section. Current tail of the class (lines 185-210):

```cpp
    private:
        bool m_initialized = false;
        CoralHostConfig m_config;

        // The Coral host instance - manages the .NET runtime
        AZStd::unique_ptr<Coral::HostInstance> m_hostInstance;

        // Assembly load context for core assemblies (O3DE.Core.dll)
        Coral::AssemblyLoadContext m_coreContext;

        // Assembly load context for user assemblies (for hot-reload, we can unload this)
        Coral::AssemblyLoadContext m_userContext;

        // Cached pointers to our assemblies
        Coral::ManagedAssembly* m_coreAssembly = nullptr;

        // All user assemblies currently loaded. m_userAssembly (below) is kept as a
        // convenience pointer to the first one so existing single-assembly APIs keep
        // working; type lookups via GetUserType iterate the full vector.
        AZStd::vector<Coral::ManagedAssembly*> m_userAssemblies;
        Coral::ManagedAssembly* m_userAssembly = nullptr;

        // Type cache for faster lookups
        AZStd::unordered_map<AZStd::string, Coral::Type*> m_coreTypeCache;
        AZStd::unordered_map<AZStd::string, Coral::Type*> m_userTypeCache;
    };
```

Replace with:

```cpp
    private:
        bool m_initialized = false;
        CoralHostConfig m_config;

        // The Coral host instance - manages the .NET runtime
        AZStd::unique_ptr<Coral::HostInstance> m_hostInstance;

        // Assembly load context for core assemblies (O3DE.Core.dll). Created once in
        // Initialize() and never unloaded/recreated by ReloadUserAssemblies() - only
        // Shutdown() tears it down. This is what makes user-script hot-reload NOT
        // re-JIT O3DE.Core or re-run RegisterInternalCalls.
        Coral::AssemblyLoadContext m_coreContext;

        // Assembly load context for user assemblies. Genuinely independent of
        // m_coreContext (not an alias - see Initialize()). Unloaded and recreated on
        // every ReloadUserAssemblies() call; O3DE.Core assembly references from
        // within it resolve against m_coreContext's already-loaded O3DE.Core
        // assembly rather than loading a second independent copy.
        Coral::AssemblyLoadContext m_userContext;

        // Cached pointers to our assemblies
        Coral::ManagedAssembly* m_coreAssembly = nullptr;

        // All user assemblies currently loaded. m_userAssembly (below) is kept as a
        // convenience pointer to the first one so existing single-assembly APIs keep
        // working; type lookups via GetUserType iterate the full vector.
        AZStd::vector<Coral::ManagedAssembly*> m_userAssemblies;
        Coral::ManagedAssembly* m_userAssembly = nullptr;

        // Type cache for faster lookups. m_coreTypeCache is populated once at
        // LoadCoreAssembly() time and is NOT cleared by ReloadUserAssemblies() -
        // O3DE.Core's Coral::Type* pointers stay valid across a user-only reload
        // now that the contexts are genuinely separate.
        AZStd::unordered_map<AZStd::string, Coral::Type*> m_coreTypeCache;
        AZStd::unordered_map<AZStd::string, Coral::Type*> m_userTypeCache;

        // Directory shadow-copied user assemblies are written to before loading, so
        // Coral's MemoryMappedFile-backed load doesn't lock the original file under
        // Bin/Scripts/ and block a subsequent rebuild. Lazily resolved to
        // <ProjectPath>/user/O3DESharpShadowCopies on first use.
        AZStd::string m_shadowCopyDirectory;

        // Monotonically increasing counter used to give every shadow copy of a given
        // assembly a unique filename per reload generation, so a not-yet-fully-
        // unloaded previous generation's memory-mapped copy is never overwritten.
        AZ::u64 m_shadowCopyGeneration = 0;
    };
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Genuinely separate the two contexts in `Initialize`**

Read the current code at `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp:194-204`:

```cpp
        // Create a single unified assembly load context
        // NOTE: We use a single context for both O3DE.Core and user assemblies because:
        // 1. Coral uses MemoryMappedFile which locks DLL files, preventing loading the same file twice
        // 2. Assemblies in the same context can reference each other directly
        // For hot-reload, we'll unload and recreate the entire context
        m_coreContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DEContext");
        
        // User context is the same as core context - single unified context
        // This pointer alias simplifies code that expects separate contexts
        m_userContext = m_coreContext;
```

Replace with:

```cpp
        // Two genuinely independent assembly load contexts.
        //
        // Previously these aliased the same context (see git history /
        // O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h) because (a) Coral's MemoryMappedFile-backed
        // loader locks the backing file, and (b) cross-ALC type identity isn't
        // unified by default in .NET. (a) is addressed by shadow-copying every
        // user assembly before load (ShadowCopyAssembly, above) instead of loading
        // Bin/Scripts/*.dll directly - the shadow copy is what gets mapped and
        // locked, not the original the build system needs to overwrite. (b) is
        // addressed by having the user context resolve O3DE.Core assembly
        // references against m_coreContext's already-loaded assembly instead of
        // loading its own independent copy - see LoadUserAssemblies() /
        // ConfigureUserContextAssemblyResolution() below.
        //
        // The core context is created once here and is only ever destroyed in
        // Shutdown(). ReloadUserAssemblies() never touches it - that's the whole
        // point of this split.
        m_coreContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DECoreContext");
        m_userContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DEUserContext");
```

At this point, insert whatever call Step 0 determined is the correct Coral API for wiring cross-context resolution (e.g. `m_userContext.SetAssemblyResolutionFallback(m_coreContext)` or equivalent — the exact name depends on what you found in `AssemblyLoadContext.hpp`; there is no single correct API name to give here since it depends on Coral's actual surface, which is why Step 0 is mandatory before this step). Add it directly after the two `CreateAssemblyLoadContext` calls above, with a comment explaining exactly which Coral API you're calling and why (mirroring the level of detail in the comment block already shown).

- [ ] **Step 3: Load user assemblies through the shadow copy, into the user context**

Read the current code at `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp:518-591` (`LoadUserAssemblies`). The load call at line 571 currently is:

```cpp
            // NOTE: O3DE.Core.dll is already loaded in the same unified context
            // (m_userContext == m_coreContext), so the user assembly can resolve
            // its O3DE.Core dependency automatically.
            Coral::ManagedAssembly& assembly = m_userContext.LoadAssembly(std::string(assemblyPath.c_str()));
```

Replace with:

```cpp
            // Shadow-copy before loading: Coral's MemoryMappedFile-backed loader
            // locks whatever file it loads, and we need the *original* file under
            // Bin/Scripts/ to stay writable for the next build. Fall back to
            // loading the original path directly (with a warning) if the copy
            // fails, rather than hard-failing the whole load.
            AZStd::string pathToLoad = ShadowCopyAssembly(assemblyPath);
            if (pathToLoad.empty())
            {
                AZLOG_WARN(
                    "CoralHostManager: Shadow copy failed for '%s'; loading original path directly. "
                    "A subsequent rebuild of this assembly may fail while it's loaded.",
                    assemblyPath.c_str());
                pathToLoad = assemblyPath;
            }

            // O3DE.Core is loaded independently in m_coreContext; the user context
            // resolves O3DE.Core assembly references against that already-loaded
            // assembly (configured in Initialize()/ReloadUserAssemblies()) rather
            // than loading its own copy, so type identity for shared O3DE.Core
            // types (EntityId, Vector3, base script classes, etc.) stays unified
            // between core and user code.
            Coral::ManagedAssembly& assembly = m_userContext.LoadAssembly(std::string(pathToLoad.c_str()));
```

Note: the existence check a few lines above this block (`AZ::IO::FileIOBase::GetInstance()->Exists(assemblyPath.c_str())`) still checks the **original** `assemblyPath`, which is correct — that's still the real source of truth on disk; only the `LoadAssembly` call itself should point at the shadow copy.

- [ ] **Step 4: Make `ReloadUserAssemblies` unload/recreate ONLY the user context**

Read the current full method at `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp:304-371`:

```cpp
    bool CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies()
    {
        if (!m_initialized)
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies - Host not initialized");
            return false;
        }

        if (!m_config.enableHotReload)
        {
            AZLOG_WARN("CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies - Hot-reload is disabled");
            return false;
        }

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Reloading user assemblies...");

        // Broadcast OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload so every CSharpScriptComponent
        // (and anything else that caches Coral handles) can release its
        // managed state BEFORE the context unload below. Without this, every
        // cached Coral::Type* / Coral::ManagedObject becomes a dangling
        // pointer the instant UnloadAssemblyLoadContext runs and the next
        // dispatch through them crashes.
        O3DESharpHotReloadNotificationBus::Broadcast(
            &O3DESharpHotReloadNotifications::OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload);

        // Clear type caches - both need to be cleared since we're reloading everything
        m_userTypeCache.clear();
        m_coreTypeCache.clear();

        // Unload the unified context (which contains both O3DE.Core and user assemblies)
        m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_coreContext);
        m_coreAssembly = nullptr;
        m_userAssembly = nullptr;
        m_userAssemblies.clear();

        // Create a new unified context
        m_coreContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DEContext");
        m_userContext = m_coreContext;  // Same context

        // Reload O3DE.Core first
        if (!LoadCoreAssembly())
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager: Failed to reload O3DE.Core assembly");
            return false;
        }

        // Re-register internal calls for the new context
        RegisterInternalCalls();

        // Reload all user assemblies
        if (!m_config.userAssemblyPaths.empty() || !m_config.userAssemblyPath.empty())
        {
            if (!LoadUserAssemblies())
            {
                AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager: Failed to reload user assemblies");
                return false;
            }
        }

        // Broadcast OnAfterUserAssemblyReload so every script component
        // re-resolves its Coral::Type and reconstructs its managed instance
        // against the freshly-loaded user assemblies.
        O3DESharpHotReloadNotificationBus::Broadcast(
            &O3DESharpHotReloadNotifications::OnAfterUserAssemblyReload);

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: User assemblies reloaded successfully");
        return true;
    }
```

Replace with:

```cpp
    bool CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies()
    {
        if (!m_initialized)
        {
            AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies - Host not initialized");
            return false;
        }

        if (!m_config.enableHotReload)
        {
            AZLOG_WARN("CoralHostManager::ReloadUserAssemblies - Hot-reload is disabled");
            return false;
        }

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Reloading user assemblies...");

        // Broadcast OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload so every CSharpScriptComponent
        // (and anything else that caches Coral handles into the USER context)
        // can release its managed state BEFORE the context unload below.
        // Without this, every cached Coral::Type* / Coral::ManagedObject pointing
        // into m_userContext becomes a dangling pointer the instant
        // UnloadAssemblyLoadContext runs and the next dispatch through it crashes.
        //
        // NOTE: this no longer needs to cover O3DE.Core handles - m_coreContext is
        // untouched by this method, so Coral::Type* values obtained via
        // GetCoreType() remain valid across this entire call. CSharpScriptComponent
        // still unconditionally tears down and rebuilds m_scriptType/m_scriptInstance
        // on every reload regardless of whether the resolved type came from core or
        // user (see CSharpScriptComponent::CreateScriptInstance's GetUserType-then-
        // GetCoreType fallback), so this is safe even for scripts whose class lives
        // in O3DE.Core.
        O3DESharpHotReloadNotificationBus::Broadcast(
            &O3DESharpHotReloadNotifications::OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload);

        // Only the user type cache is invalidated - m_coreTypeCache stays valid
        // because m_coreContext/m_coreAssembly are never touched by this method.
        m_userTypeCache.clear();

        // Unload ONLY the user context. O3DE.Core (m_coreContext / m_coreAssembly)
        // is untouched - this is the entire point of the fix: a user-script reload
        // no longer re-JITs O3DE.Core or re-runs RegisterInternalCalls.
        m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_userContext);
        m_userAssembly = nullptr;
        m_userAssemblies.clear();

        // Create a new, independent user context. Re-apply whatever cross-context
        // resolution Step 2 wired up in Initialize() so the new user context still
        // resolves O3DE.Core references against m_coreContext's still-loaded
        // assembly instead of loading its own copy.
        m_userContext = m_hostInstance->CreateAssemblyLoadContext("O3DEUserContext");
        // TODO(reviewer of this task): mirror here the exact call Step 2 used to
        // configure cross-context resolution on m_userContext.

        // Reload all user assemblies (via shadow copy - see LoadUserAssemblies).
        // O3DE.Core is NOT reloaded and RegisterInternalCalls is NOT re-run.
        if (!m_config.userAssemblyPaths.empty() || !m_config.userAssemblyPath.empty())
        {
            if (!LoadUserAssemblies())
            {
                AZLOG_ERROR("CoralHostManager: Failed to reload user assemblies");
                return false;
            }
        }

        // Broadcast OnAfterUserAssemblyReload so every script component
        // re-resolves its Coral::Type and reconstructs its managed instance
        // against the freshly-loaded user assemblies.
        O3DESharpHotReloadNotificationBus::Broadcast(
            &O3DESharpHotReloadNotifications::OnAfterUserAssemblyReload);

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: User assemblies reloaded successfully");
        return true;
    }
```

Do not leave the `TODO(reviewer of this task)` marker in the final commit — replace it with the real call once Step 2's API is known; it's included above only because this plan cannot name Coral's exact method until Step 0 is executed against the real vendored source.

- [ ] **Step 5: Update `Shutdown` to unload both contexts explicitly**

Read the current code at `Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp:248-275`:

```cpp
    void CoralHostManager::Shutdown()
    {
        if (!m_initialized)
        {
            return;
        }

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Shutting down...");

        // Clear type caches
        m_coreTypeCache.clear();
        m_userTypeCache.clear();

        // Unload the unified context (contains both O3DE.Core and user assemblies)
        if (m_coreAssembly != nullptr || !m_userAssemblies.empty())
        {
            m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_coreContext);
            m_coreAssembly = nullptr;
            m_userAssembly = nullptr;
            m_userAssemblies.clear();
        }

        // Shutdown the .NET runtime
        m_hostInstance->Shutdown();

        m_initialized = false;
        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Shutdown complete");
    }
```

Replace with:

```cpp
    void CoralHostManager::Shutdown()
    {
        if (!m_initialized)
        {
            return;
        }

        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Shutting down...");

        // Clear type caches
        m_coreTypeCache.clear();
        m_userTypeCache.clear();

        // Unload both contexts independently - they are no longer aliased.
        if (!m_userAssemblies.empty())
        {
            m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_userContext);
            m_userAssembly = nullptr;
            m_userAssemblies.clear();
        }
        if (m_coreAssembly != nullptr)
        {
            m_hostInstance->UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_coreContext);
            m_coreAssembly = nullptr;
        }

        // Shutdown the .NET runtime
        m_hostInstance->Shutdown();

        m_initialized = false;
        AZLOG_INFO("CoralHostManager: Shutdown complete");
    }
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Update the stale doc comment in `O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h`**

Read the current comment block at `Code/Include/O3DESharp/O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h:19-36`:

```cpp
     * Phase 13 addresses a real correctness risk identified in the audit:
     * <c>m_userContext</c> aliased <c>m_coreContext</c>, so reloading user
     * assemblies tore down O3DE.Core as well. Every <c>CSharpScriptComponent</c>
     * cached a <c>Coral::Type*</c> in <c>m_scriptType</c> that became a
     * dangling pointer after the context unload, plus a <c>Coral::ManagedObject</c>
     * in <c>m_scriptInstance</c> with the same problem. The first call into
     * either after the reload would dereference freed memory.
     *
     * Coral can't easily separate the contexts (per the comment in
     * <c>CoralHostManager::Initialize</c>: Coral uses MemoryMappedFile which
     * locks DLLs, and cross-context type resolution is not in this Coral
     * version), so this bus is the alternative: every script component
     * tears down its managed state on <c>OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload</c>
     * and rebuilds it on <c>OnAfterUserAssemblyReload</c>. The notification
     * order matches Coral's lifecycle - "before" fires before
     * <c>UnloadAssemblyLoadContext</c>, "after" fires after the new context
     * + assemblies are ready and internal calls are re-registered.
     */
```

Replace with:

```cpp
     * Phase 13 addressed a real correctness risk identified in the audit:
     * <c>m_userContext</c> aliased <c>m_coreContext</c>, so reloading user
     * assemblies tore down O3DE.Core as well. Every <c>CSharpScriptComponent</c>
     * cached a <c>Coral::Type*</c> in <c>m_scriptType</c> that became a
     * dangling pointer after the context unload, plus a <c>Coral::ManagedObject</c>
     * in <c>m_scriptInstance</c> with the same problem. The first call into
     * either after the reload would dereference freed memory.
     *
     * 1.2.0 (item 10 of the UX/perf audit) separated <c>m_userContext</c> from
     * <c>m_coreContext</c> for real - see <c>CoralHostManager::Initialize</c> and
     * <c>ReloadUserAssemblies</c>. O3DE.Core is no longer torn down by a
     * user-assembly reload, so <c>Coral::Type*</c> values obtained from
     * <c>GetCoreType</c> now stay valid across a reload. This bus is still
     * required, though: <c>m_userContext</c> itself is still unloaded and
     * recreated on every reload, so any cached <c>Coral::Type*</c> /
     * <c>Coral::ManagedObject</c> resolved from the USER context (including a
     * user script class that happened to resolve via <c>GetCoreType</c>'s
     * fallback, since <c>CSharpScriptComponent</c> doesn't distinguish the two at
     * the call site) still becomes dangling the instant
     * <c>UnloadAssemblyLoadContext(m_userContext)</c> runs. Every script
     * component still tears down its managed state on
     * <c>OnBeforeUserAssemblyReload</c> and rebuilds it on
     * <c>OnAfterUserAssemblyReload</c>, unconditionally, regardless of which
     * context the type actually resolved from - that's still the simplest
     * correct behavior and this task deliberately did not change it.
     */
```

- [ ] **Step 8: Manual verification checklist (no automated test exists for this — this replaces one)**

Perform every one of these, in order, against a real O3DE project with a C# script attached (use one of the existing example scripts under `Assets/Scripts/Examples/` if the target project doesn't already have one):

1. **Cold start (non-reload) baseline.** Launch the O3DE Editor against a project configured for this gem. In the Console panel, confirm you see `CoralHostManager: Initialization complete` and, earlier in the same log, `CoralHostManager: Internal calls registered successfully` exactly once. Add a C# Script component to an entity in the level, set its script class to one of the example scripts, and enter Game Mode (Ctrl+G or the Play button). Confirm the script's `OnCreate`/`OnUpdate` behavior runs as expected (e.g. if using `ReflectionExample.cs`, confirm its expected log output/behavior appears). Exit Game Mode.
2. **Trigger a hot-reload via source edit.** With the Editor still open and the entity/script from step 1 still active, open the user script's `.cs` source file in your editor of choice and make a visible behavior change (e.g. change a logged string literal or a numeric constant it prints). Rebuild the user C# project (via `Tools > C# Scripting > Build Project` in the Editor menu, or your normal `dotnet build` workflow against the project's C# csproj under its `Scripts/` folder — check `Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py` if unsure which path your project uses). Confirm the build succeeds and drops an updated `.dll` under `<ProjectPath>/Bin/Scripts/`.
3. **Trigger the reload.** If `Tools > C# Scripting > Reload Scripts on File Change` is enabled (checkable menu item under the same menu), the reload should fire automatically within ~500ms of the build finishing (the debounce window in `CSharpAssemblyWatcher`). Otherwise, trigger it manually via `Tools > C# Scripting > Reload Scripts` (`O3DESharpEditorSystemComponent::ReloadCSharpScripts`, action id `o3de.action.o3desharp.reloadScripts`). Confirm the Console panel prints `CoralHostManager: Reloading user assemblies...` followed by `CoralHostManager: User assemblies reloaded successfully`.
4. **Confirm O3DE.Core was NOT reloaded/re-JITted during that reload.** Check the Console panel output produced between the `Reloading user assemblies...` and `User assemblies reloaded successfully` lines from step 3: confirm `CoralHostManager: Registering internal calls...` / `CoralHostManager: Internal calls registered successfully` do **NOT** appear in that span (they should only ever have appeared once, back in step 1's cold-start log, and never again). Also confirm `CoralHostManager: Core API assembly loaded:` (from `LoadCoreAssembly`) does not reappear. If you have a native debugger attached to the Editor process, an equivalent and more rigorous check is to set a breakpoint on `CoralHostManager::RegisterInternalCalls` (`Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp`) before step 3 and confirm it does not hit again during the reload.
5. **Confirm existing live references into O3DE.Core remain valid.** Before triggering the reload in step 3, note the entity from step 1 still has its C# Script component attached and configured. After the reload completes, re-enter Game Mode on the same entity without re-adding the component. Confirm the script still runs without errors in the Console (no `CoralHostManager` or `CSharpScriptComponent` errors about invalid/dangling handles) — this exercises `CSharpScriptComponent::OnAfterUserAssemblyReload`'s full re-resolve-and-recreate path (`CreateScriptInstance` → `GetUserType`/`GetCoreType` fallback → `CreateInstance`), which must succeed cleanly against the now-separated contexts.
6. **Confirm the actual code change took effect.** With the entity in Game Mode (or via whatever the script's example behavior triggers), confirm the specific change you made to the script's source in step 2 (the changed string/constant) is now visible in the running behavior/log output — proving the reload picked up the rebuilt DLL and not a stale cached one.
7. **Repeat step 2-6 a second time** (edit again, rebuild, reload again) to confirm the shadow-copy generation counter (`m_shadowCopyGeneration`) correctly avoids colliding with the first reload's shadow copy, and that a second reload doesn't fail or leak a locked file. Check `<ProjectPath>/user/O3DESharpShadowCopies/` on disk and confirm you now see two distinct generation-suffixed copies of the user assembly (e.g. `MyGame_gen0.dll`, `MyGame_gen1.dll`), not a single file that failed to update.
8. **Confirm a normal project rebuild is not blocked by a locked file.** After the manual verification above, close the Editor, then rebuild the user C# project one more time from a clean shell (`dotnet build` against the project's script csproj, or via `Tools > C# Scripting > Build Project` before closing in step above). Confirm the build succeeds with no "file in use by another process" error against `Bin/Scripts/*.dll` — this is the regression check for the original file-locking concern.

If any of steps 3-8 fail, do not proceed to Step 9 (commit) — treat it as Step 0's escalation path retroactively triggered: stop, leave `development` in a clean state (revert your changes if needed), and flag the specific failure to the maintainer for a go/no-go on deferring this item to 1.2.1.

- [ ] **Step 9: Commit**

Per the approved spec, this item ships as its own isolated, independently-revertable commit (or short series). If you executed Step 0's escalation path and made no code changes, skip this step entirely — there is nothing to commit. Otherwise, if Steps 1-6 all landed as a single coherent change (the expected case for this task), commit them together:

```bash
git add Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.h Code/Source/Scripting/CoralHostManager.cpp Code/Include/O3DESharp/O3DESharpHotReloadBus.h
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: separate user/core AssemblyLoadContexts so hot-reload no longer rebuilds O3DE.Core

CoralHostManager previously aliased m_userContext to m_coreContext, so every
user-script hot-reload unloaded and re-JITted all of O3DE.Core and re-ran
RegisterInternalCalls, on top of reloading the user assembly that actually
changed. The two contexts are now genuinely independent: m_coreContext is
created once in Initialize() and only torn down in Shutdown(); user
assemblies are shadow-copied into <ProjectPath>/user/O3DESharpShadowCopies
before loading (so Coral's MemoryMappedFile-backed loader doesn't lock the
original file under Bin/Scripts/ and block a rebuild), and the user context
resolves O3DE.Core assembly references against the core context's
already-loaded assembly rather than loading its own copy, preserving type
identity for shared types (EntityId, Vector3, base script classes) across
the boundary. m_coreTypeCache and m_coreAssembly are no longer cleared/
reloaded by ReloadUserAssemblies.
EOF
)"
```

If instead the fix required a Coral-fork patch (Step 0 case (a) via a local fork) that lives in a separate repository/submodule, note that separately here rather than bundling it: commit the O3DESharp-side changes above in this repo, and record in the commit body (append to the message above) the exact Coral fork commit hash the build now depends on, so a reviewer can trace the cross-repo dependency.

---

### Task 11: C# Project Manager — Build/Build All UI freeze fix

**Files:**
- Modify: `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py` (new worker classes near line 1247, after `_BindingBuildWorker`; call-site rewrites at `_build_selected_project` line 563-587, `_build_project` line 2029-2056, `_build_all` line 2058-2089)
- Modify: `Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py:1438-1443` (add timeout to the remaining direct `subprocess.run` call inside `build_project()`)
- Test: `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_build.py` (new — pure-logic pieces only; see manual-verification step for the QThread wiring itself)

- [ ] **Step 1: Add a timeout to `build_project()`'s own `subprocess.run` call**

`build_project()` in `Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py` is still the function every worker will eventually shell out through, and today its `subprocess.run` has no timeout at all — a hung `dotnet build` (e.g. a stuck NuGet restore against an unreachable feed) blocks forever with no way out other than killing the process externally. Read the current code (confirmed at lines 1397-1511):

```python
        try:
            # Phase 16b: set the BuildInProgress flag so the editor's file watcher
            # (Phase 16a) coalesces every intermediate write during this build into
            # a single reload at the end. The watcher polls this flag on each
            # debounce expiry and reschedules itself while it's set. Best-effort -
            # the settings registry might not exist in non-editor contexts.
            _set_build_in_progress(True)
            try:
                result = subprocess.run(
                    ["dotnet", "build", str(csproj_path), "-c", configuration],
                    capture_output=True,
                    text=True,
                    cwd=str(project_path)
                )
            finally:
                _set_build_in_progress(False)

            if result.returncode == 0:
```

Replace it with a version that passes `timeout=300` (matching `_BindingBuildWorker`'s existing 5-minute convention) and turns a timeout into the same `{"success": False, ...}` shape the rest of the function already returns, instead of letting `subprocess.TimeoutExpired` propagate as an uncaught exception:

```python
        try:
            # Phase 16b: set the BuildInProgress flag so the editor's file watcher
            # (Phase 16a) coalesces every intermediate write during this build into
            # a single reload at the end. The watcher polls this flag on each
            # debounce expiry and reschedules itself while it's set. Best-effort -
            # the settings registry might not exist in non-editor contexts.
            _set_build_in_progress(True)
            try:
                # 300s timeout matches _BindingBuildWorker's convention in
                # csharp_editor_tools.py (Phase 18-D auto-build). Without a
                # timeout, a hung `dotnet build` (e.g. a stuck NuGet restore
                # against an unreachable feed) blocks this call - and every
                # caller of it - forever.
                result = subprocess.run(
                    ["dotnet", "build", str(csproj_path), "-c", configuration],
                    capture_output=True,
                    text=True,
                    cwd=str(project_path),
                    timeout=300,
                )
            except subprocess.TimeoutExpired as timeout_err:
                return {
                    "success": False,
                    "message": "Build timed out after 300 seconds",
                    "output_path": None,
                    "build_output": (
                        (timeout_err.stdout or "") + "\n" + (timeout_err.stderr or "")
                    ),
                }
            finally:
                _set_build_in_progress(False)

            if result.returncode == 0:
```

Note the `except subprocess.TimeoutExpired` sits between the inner `try` and its `finally` — `_set_build_in_progress(False)` still runs in both the timeout and non-timeout paths because `finally` always executes.

- [ ] **Step 2: Add a `_BindingBuildWorker`-based single-project build worker in `csharp_editor_tools.py`**

`_BindingBuildWorker` (already at lines 1180-1246) only accepts a list of `.csproj` **file** paths and always builds `Debug`. The three freeze sites (`_build_selected_project`, `_build_project`, `_build_all`) instead have a project **directory** (`project["path"]`), a caller-chosen configuration (`Release`/`Debug` from `self.config_combo`), and need `CSharpProjectManager.build_project()`'s full behavior — csproj discovery inside the directory, the `ensure_runtime_deployed()` pre-check, and the Bin/Scripts DLL+PDB deploy copy — not just a bare `dotnet build`. Reusing `_BindingBuildWorker` as-is would silently drop all of that. Add a new, small QThread subclass immediately after `_BindingBuildWorker` (after line 1246, before `class CSharpProjectManagerWindow`) that runs `project_manager.build_project()` off the UI thread and hands back its result dict:

```python
class _ProjectBuildWorker(QThread):
    """
    Runs CSharpProjectManager.build_project() on a background thread so
    the C# Project Manager's UI (and the Script Browser's "Build" button)
    stay responsive during a build.

    Previously all three call sites (_build_selected_project,
    _build_project, _build_all) invoked build_project() directly on the
    Qt UI thread. build_project() shells out to `dotnet build` via
    subprocess.run(), which blocks the calling thread until the process
    exits - for the UI thread that means the whole dialog stops
    repainting and stops responding to input for the entire build
    (seconds for an incremental build, much longer on a cold restore or
    a large solution). This worker moves that blocking call off the UI
    thread; build_project() itself now also carries a timeout (see
    csharp_project_manager.py) so a hung `dotnet build` can no longer
    block forever even on this background thread.

    One result dict per build, emitted via finished_signal so the UI
    handler can render success/failure exactly as before.
    """

    finished_signal = Signal(dict)  # build_project()'s result dict

    def __init__(self, project_manager, project_path, configuration):
        super().__init__()
        self._project_manager = project_manager
        self._project_path = project_path
        self._configuration = configuration

    def run(self):
        try:
            result = self._project_manager.build_project(
                self._project_path, self._configuration)
        except Exception as e:
            import traceback
            result = {
                "success": False,
                "message": f"Build worker raised: {e}",
                "output_path": None,
                "build_output": traceback.format_exc(),
            }
        self.finished_signal.emit(result)
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Route `ScriptBrowserDialog._build_selected_project` through the worker**

Current code (confirmed at lines 563-587 of `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py`):

```python
    def _build_selected_project(self):
        """Build the project containing the selected item."""
        items = self.tree.selectedItems()
        project_path = None
        if items:
            item_data = items[0].data(0, Qt.UserRole)
            if item_data:
                if item_data["type"] == "project":
                    project_path = item_data["data"]["path"]
                elif item_data["type"] == "script":
                    parent = items[0].parent()
                    if parent:
                        parent_data = parent.data(0, Qt.UserRole)
                        if parent_data and parent_data["type"] == "project":
                            project_path = parent_data["data"]["path"]
        
        if not project_path:
            QMessageBox.information(self, "Build", "Select a project or script first.")
            return
        
        result = self.project_manager.build_project(project_path)
        if result["success"]:
            QMessageBox.information(self, "Build Succeeded", f"Output: {result.get('output_path', 'OK')}")
        else:
            QMessageBox.warning(self, "Build Failed", result.get("message", "Unknown error"))
```

This dialog is modal (`self.setModal(True)`, line 347) and has a `build_btn` (line 364) that stays enabled the whole time today, so a user can also double-click it mid-build. Replace with an async version that disables the Build button for the duration and re-enables it (or closes out) when the worker finishes:

```python
    def _build_selected_project(self):
        """Build the project containing the selected item."""
        if getattr(self, "_build_worker", None) is not None and self._build_worker.isRunning():
            QMessageBox.information(self, "Build", "A build is already in progress.")
            return

        items = self.tree.selectedItems()
        project_path = None
        if items:
            item_data = items[0].data(0, Qt.UserRole)
            if item_data:
                if item_data["type"] == "project":
                    project_path = item_data["data"]["path"]
                elif item_data["type"] == "script":
                    parent = items[0].parent()
                    if parent:
                        parent_data = parent.data(0, Qt.UserRole)
                        if parent_data and parent_data["type"] == "project":
                            project_path = parent_data["data"]["path"]
        
        if not project_path:
            QMessageBox.information(self, "Build", "Select a project or script first.")
            return

        self.build_btn.setEnabled(False)
        self.build_btn.setText("Building...")

        self._build_worker = _ProjectBuildWorker(
            self.project_manager, project_path, "Release")
        self._build_worker.finished_signal.connect(self._on_build_selected_finished)
        self._build_worker.start()

    def _on_build_selected_finished(self, result):
        self.build_btn.setEnabled(True)
        self.build_btn.setText("Build")
        self._build_worker = None

        if result["success"]:
            QMessageBox.information(self, "Build Succeeded", f"Output: {result.get('output_path', 'OK')}")
        else:
            QMessageBox.warning(self, "Build Failed", result.get("message", "Unknown error"))
```


```python
    def _build_project(self):
        if getattr(self, "_project_build_worker", None) is not None and self._project_build_worker.isRunning():
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Route `CSharpProjectManagerWindow._build_all` through a sequential multi-project worker**

`_build_all` needs to build every project one after another and report a running success/fail tally — `_ProjectBuildWorker` only handles one project per run, so `_build_all` needs its own worker that loops. Current code (confirmed at lines 2058-2089):

```python
    def _build_all(self):
        projects = self.project_manager.list_projects()
        config = self.config_combo.currentText()
        
        self._log(f"========== Building all projects ({config}) ==========", "INFO")
        self._log(f"Total projects: {len(projects)}", "INFO")
        
        success_count = 0
        fail_count = 0
        
        for i, project in enumerate(projects, 1):
            self.status_label.setText(f"Building {project['name']} ({i}/{len(projects)})...")
            self._log(f"--- Building {project['name']} ({i}/{len(projects)}) ---", "INFO")
            QtWidgets.QApplication.processEvents()
            
            result = self.project_manager.build_project(project["path"], config)
            
            # Log the build output
            if result.get("build_output"):
                self._log_build_output(result["build_output"], not result["success"])
            
            if result["success"]:
                self._log(f"✓ {project['name']}: Build succeeded", "SUCCESS")
                success_count += 1
            else:
                self._log(f"✗ {project['name']}: Build failed - {result['message']}", "ERROR")
                fail_count += 1
                
        self.status_label.setText(f"Build complete: {success_count} succeeded, {fail_count} failed")
        self._log(f"========== Build complete: {success_count} succeeded, {fail_count} failed ==========", 
                  "SUCCESS" if fail_count == 0 else "WARNING")
        self._log("", "INFO")  # Blank line for readability
```

First add a new worker class right after `_ProjectBuildWorker` (from Step 2), in `csharp_editor_tools.py`:

```python
class _BuildAllWorker(QThread):
    """
    Runs CSharpProjectManager.build_project() for every project in
    `projects`, one at a time, on a background thread - the "Build All"
    counterpart to _ProjectBuildWorker. Sequential (not parallel) so the
    per-project log lines stay attributable and two builds never race
    writing to the same Bin/Scripts/ output.

    progress_signal fires once per project as it starts, so the UI can
    update its status label in step. finished_signal fires once at the
    end with (success_count, fail_count) and the raw list of per-project
    result dicts (each augmented with "name") for detailed logging.
    """

    progress_signal = Signal(str, int, int)  # (project_name, index_1_based, total)
    project_done_signal = Signal(str, dict)  # (project_name, result_dict)
    finished_signal = Signal(int, int)  # (success_count, fail_count)

    def __init__(self, project_manager, projects, configuration):
        super().__init__()
        self._project_manager = project_manager
        self._projects = list(projects)
        self._configuration = configuration

    def run(self):
        success_count = 0
        fail_count = 0
        total = len(self._projects)
        for i, project in enumerate(self._projects, 1):
            self.progress_signal.emit(project["name"], i, total)
            try:
                result = self._project_manager.build_project(
                    project["path"], self._configuration)
            except Exception as e:
                import traceback
                result = {
                    "success": False,
                    "message": f"Build worker raised: {e}",
                    "output_path": None,
                    "build_output": traceback.format_exc(),
                }
            self.project_done_signal.emit(project["name"], result)
            if result["success"]:
                success_count += 1
            else:
                fail_count += 1
        self.finished_signal.emit(success_count, fail_count)
```

Then replace `_build_all` itself with the async version, wiring its three signals to log/status updates:

```python
    def _build_all(self):
        if getattr(self, "_build_all_worker", None) is not None and self._build_all_worker.isRunning():
            self._log("A 'Build All' run is already in progress; ignoring duplicate request.", "WARNING")
            return

        projects = self.project_manager.list_projects()
        config = self.config_combo.currentText()
        
        self._log(f"========== Building all projects ({config}) ==========", "INFO")
        self._log(f"Total projects: {len(projects)}", "INFO")

        if hasattr(self, "build_all_btn") and self.build_all_btn is not None:
            self.build_all_btn.setEnabled(False)

        self._build_all_worker = _BuildAllWorker(self.project_manager, projects, config)
        self._build_all_worker.progress_signal.connect(self._on_build_all_progress)
        self._build_all_worker.project_done_signal.connect(self._on_build_all_project_done)
        self._build_all_worker.finished_signal.connect(self._on_build_all_finished)
        self._build_all_worker.start()

    def _on_build_all_progress(self, project_name, index, total):
        self.status_label.setText(f"Building {project_name} ({index}/{total})...")
        self._log(f"--- Building {project_name} ({index}/{total}) ---", "INFO")

    def _on_build_all_project_done(self, project_name, result):
        if result.get("build_output"):
            self._log_build_output(result["build_output"], not result["success"])
        if result["success"]:
            self._log(f"✓ {project_name}: Build succeeded", "SUCCESS")
        else:
            self._log(f"✗ {project_name}: Build failed - {result['message']}", "ERROR")

    def _on_build_all_finished(self, success_count, fail_count):
        if hasattr(self, "build_all_btn") and self.build_all_btn is not None:
            self.build_all_btn.setEnabled(True)
        self._build_all_worker = None

        self.status_label.setText(f"Build complete: {success_count} succeeded, {fail_count} failed")
        self._log(f"========== Build complete: {success_count} succeeded, {fail_count} failed ==========", 
                  "SUCCESS" if fail_count == 0 else "WARNING")
        self._log("", "INFO")  # Blank line for readability
```

`build_btn` ("Build All", the button that calls `_build_all`) is currently a local variable too — give it a `self.` reference. Current code (confirmed at lines 1277-1279):

```python
        build_btn = QPushButton("Build All")
        build_btn.clicked.connect(self._build_all)
        toolbar.addWidget(build_btn)
```

Replace with:

```python
        self.build_all_btn = QPushButton("Build All")
        self.build_all_btn.clicked.connect(self._build_all)
        toolbar.addWidget(self.build_all_btn)
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Write a pytest test for the parts that don't need PySide2/azlmbr/Qt**

`Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py` imports `PySide2` and `azlmbr.bus`/`azlmbr.editor` at module scope (confirmed lines 24-36), and neither package is installed in the TeamCity `PythonTests` build type (`.teamcity/settings.kts` lines 302-334 install only `pytest` via pip, and that build type is Linux-only with no Qt/O3DE runtime) or in a typical bare checkout. That means this module cannot be imported at all in the pytest environment, so the QThread classes themselves (`_ProjectBuildWorker`, `_BuildAllWorker`) cannot be exercised by an automated test without first building out PySide2/azlmbr stub packages — out of scope for this fix. The genuinely test-worthy, Qt-independent unit is the timeout/error-shape change to `CSharpProjectManager.build_project()` from Step 1, which lives in `csharp_project_manager.py` — a plain module with no PySide2/azlmbr imports at all. Confirm that:

```bash
python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py', encoding='utf-8').read())" && echo "parses OK"
grep -n "^import PySide2\|^from PySide2\|^import azlmbr\|^from azlmbr" Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py || echo "no Qt/azlmbr imports in csharp_project_manager.py"
```

Expected output:
```
parses OK
no Qt/azlmbr imports in csharp_project_manager.py
```

`csharp_project_manager.py` does import `azlmbr.paths` (line 22-23) though, which pytest also can't import directly — so the test needs to stub that module the same way any future test of this file would. Create `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_build.py`:

```python
#
# Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
# For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
#
# SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
#
"""
Unit tests for CSharpProjectManager.build_project()'s timeout handling.

These exercise only the pure-Python timeout/error-shape behavior added to
build_project() (Task 11, v1.2.0). The QThread wiring that moves
build_project() off the Qt UI thread lives in csharp_editor_tools.py,
which imports PySide2 and azlmbr.bus/azlmbr.editor at module scope -
neither is installed in this pytest environment (see Editor/Tests/README.md
and .teamcity/settings.kts's PythonTests build type), so that wiring is
covered by a manual verification checklist instead (see the v1.2.0 plan).
"""

import subprocess
import sys
import types
from pathlib import Path
from unittest.mock import MagicMock, patch

import pytest


def _install_azlmbr_stub():
    """
    csharp_project_manager.py does `import azlmbr.bus`, `import
    azlmbr.editor`, and `import azlmbr.paths` at module scope. None of
    those packages exist outside a running O3DE Editor process, so stub
    them in sys.modules before the module under test is imported.
    """
    azlmbr = types.ModuleType("azlmbr")
    azlmbr_bus = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.bus")
    azlmbr_editor = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.editor")
    azlmbr_paths = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.paths")
    azlmbr_paths.projectroot = str(Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2])
    azlmbr.bus = azlmbr_bus
    azlmbr.editor = azlmbr_editor
    azlmbr.paths = azlmbr_paths
    sys.modules["azlmbr"] = azlmbr
    sys.modules["azlmbr.bus"] = azlmbr_bus
    sys.modules["azlmbr.editor"] = azlmbr_editor
    sys.modules["azlmbr.paths"] = azlmbr_paths


_install_azlmbr_stub()

from csharp_project_manager import CSharpProjectManager  # noqa: E402


@pytest.mark.unit
class TestBuildProjectTimeout:
    """Test suite for build_project()'s subprocess timeout (Task 11)."""

    def _make_manager(self, tmp_path):
        manager = CSharpProjectManager.__new__(CSharpProjectManager)
        manager.project_path = tmp_path
        manager.gem_path = tmp_path
        manager.scripts_path = tmp_path
        return manager

    def test_build_times_out_returns_failure_dict(self, tmp_path):
        """A dotnet build that exceeds the timeout must return a failure
        dict, not raise subprocess.TimeoutExpired up to the caller."""
        project_dir = tmp_path / "MyGame"
        project_dir.mkdir()
        (project_dir / "MyGame.csproj").write_text("<Project />", encoding="utf-8")

        manager = self._make_manager(tmp_path)

        with patch.object(manager, "ensure_runtime_deployed",
                           return_value={"success": True, "message": "ok"}), \
             patch("csharp_project_manager._set_build_in_progress"), \
             patch("csharp_project_manager.subprocess.run",
                   side_effect=subprocess.TimeoutExpired(
                       cmd=["dotnet", "build"], timeout=300,
                       output="partial stdout", stderr="partial stderr")):
            result = manager.build_project(project_dir, "Release")

        assert result["success"] is False
        assert "timed out" in result["message"].lower()
        assert result["output_path"] is None
        assert "partial stdout" in result["build_output"]
        assert "partial stderr" in result["build_output"]

    def test_build_passes_timeout_to_subprocess_run(self, tmp_path):
        """subprocess.run must be called with timeout=300 so a hung
        dotnet build cannot block build_project() forever."""
        project_dir = tmp_path / "MyGame"
        project_dir.mkdir()
        (project_dir / "MyGame.csproj").write_text("<Project />", encoding="utf-8")

        manager = self._make_manager(tmp_path)

        mock_result = MagicMock()
        mock_result.returncode = 1
        mock_result.stdout = ""
        mock_result.stderr = "error"

        with patch.object(manager, "ensure_runtime_deployed",
                           return_value={"success": True, "message": "ok"}), \
             patch("csharp_project_manager._set_build_in_progress"), \
             patch("csharp_project_manager.subprocess.run",
                   return_value=mock_result) as mock_run:
            manager.build_project(project_dir, "Release")

        _, kwargs = mock_run.call_args
        assert kwargs.get("timeout") == 300

    def test_build_in_progress_flag_cleared_on_timeout(self, tmp_path):
        """_set_build_in_progress(False) must still run (via `finally`)
        even when the build times out, so the file-watcher coalescing
        flag never gets stuck on."""
        project_dir = tmp_path / "MyGame"
        project_dir.mkdir()
        (project_dir / "MyGame.csproj").write_text("<Project />", encoding="utf-8")

        manager = self._make_manager(tmp_path)

        with patch.object(manager, "ensure_runtime_deployed",
                           return_value={"success": True, "message": "ok"}), \
             patch("csharp_project_manager._set_build_in_progress") as mock_flag, \
             patch("csharp_project_manager.subprocess.run",
                   side_effect=subprocess.TimeoutExpired(
                       cmd=["dotnet", "build"], timeout=300)):
            manager.build_project(project_dir, "Release")

        mock_flag.assert_any_call(True)
        mock_flag.assert_any_call(False)
```

Run it:

```bash
python -m pytest test_csharp_editor_tools_build.py -v
```

```
test_csharp_editor_tools_build.py::TestBuildProjectTimeout::test_build_in_progress_flag_cleared_on_timeout PASSED
```

The three call-site rewrites in `csharp_editor_tools.py` (Steps 3-5) require a live O3DE Editor with PySide2 and the C# Project Manager panel registered — not reachable from pytest (Step 6 explains why). Verify by hand:

1. Launch the O3DE Editor with the O3DESharp gem enabled, open the C# Project Manager panel (menu: Tools → C# Project Manager, or the equivalent entry point registered by `csharp_editor_bootstrap.py`).
2. Select a project in the list, click **Build Project**. Confirm:
   - The **Build Project** button becomes disabled (grayed out) immediately on click and stays disabled until the build finishes.
   - While the build is running, drag/resize the C# Project Manager window and confirm it repaints immediately (no "Not Responding" / frozen frame) — this is the regression this task fixes.
   - The log panel shows `========== Building <name> (<config>) ==========` immediately, and the success/failure line appears only after the build actually completes, not instantly.
   - After completion, the **Build Project** button re-enables and the status label shows the final success/failure text.
3. Click **Build Project** again immediately while a build is still running (double-click fast, or click again within ~1s). Confirm the log shows `A build is already in progress; ignoring duplicate request.` and no second `dotnet build` process is spawned (check Task Manager / `ps` for a duplicate `dotnet` process).
4. Click **Build All** with 2+ projects present. Confirm:
   - The **Build All** button disables for the duration.
   - The status label updates per-project (`Building <name> (1/N)...`, `(2/N)...`, etc.) and the window stays responsive throughout (drag/resize test again).
   - The final summary line (`Build complete: X succeeded, Y failed`) appears only after every project has been attempted, and the button re-enables.
5. Open **Select C# Script** (the `ScriptBrowserDialog`, e.g. from the C# Script component's "..." picker), select a script belonging to a project, click **Build**. Confirm the button reads "Building..." and is disabled during the build, the dialog remains draggable/responsive, and a `QMessageBox` reporting success or failure appears only once the build actually completes (not immediately).
6. To confirm the timeout path without waiting 5 minutes: temporarily rename `dotnet.exe` (or shadow it earlier on `PATH` with a batch/shell script that does `ping -n 400 127.0.0.1 >nul` on Windows or `sleep 400` on Linux/macOS before exiting 0) so `dotnet build` effectively hangs, trigger **Build Project**, and confirm that after 300 seconds the log reports a timeout failure and the UI recovers (button re-enables) rather than hanging indefinitely. Restore the real `dotnet` on `PATH` afterward.

### Task 12: "Clear Selection" script picker no-ops + prints a misleading warning

**Files:**
- Modify: `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py:2639-2667` (`CSharpEditorToolsHandler.OpenScriptPicker`)
- Modify: `Code/Source/Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h:147-152` (doc comment for `OpenScriptPicker`, no signature change)
- Modify: `Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp:248-284` (`OnBrowseScript`)
- Modify: `Code/Source/Tools/Components/CSharpScriptClassPropertyHandler.cpp:160-176` (Browse button handler in `CreateGUI`)
- Test: `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py` (new)

Root cause: `CSharpEditorToolsBus::OpenScriptPicker` is declared to return a plain (non-optional) `AZStd::string`, so there is no existing "no value at all" channel across this EBus call — every path already collapses to a concrete `AZStd::string` on the C++ side (there is no `AZStd::optional<AZStd::string>` or similar sentinel used anywhere else in `CSharpEditorToolsBus.h`). On the Python side, `ScriptClassPickerDialog._select_none()` sets `self._selected_class = ""` and accepts the dialog, and `CSharpEditorToolsHandler.OpenScriptPicker` then returns that same literal `""`. If the user instead clicks **Cancel**, the dialog is rejected, `dialog.exec_()` returns something other than `QDialog.Accepted`, and `OpenScriptPicker` falls through to its own `return ""  # Cancelled` line. Both user actions therefore produce the exact same wire value, `""`, so `EditorCSharpScriptComponent::OnBrowseScript` and `CSharpScriptClassPropertyHandler::CreateGUI`'s Browse handler cannot tell them apart — both currently treat "result is empty" as "nothing to do", and `OnBrowseScript` additionally logs a warning that says "Either the user cancelled or the Python CSharpEditorToolsBus handler is not connected", which is actively misleading when the user did explicitly clear the field.

Fix: since the bus's return channel is a plain string with no reserved "no value" representation, introduce one reserved sentinel string that cannot collide with any real (or empty) class name, and use it only for the explicit-clear case. Cancel keeps returning literal `""` (unchanged meaning: "no value produced"). This keeps the wire type unchanged (`AZStd::string`, no `CSharpEditorToolsBus.h` signature edit needed) while giving both C++ call sites a way to distinguish "user explicitly blanked the field" (sentinel) from "nothing happened" (empty string).

- [ ] **Step 1: Add a shared sentinel constant on the Python side**

Read the current top of `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py` (already confirmed at lines 1-43) — there is no existing module-level constants block near the dialog classes, so add one immediately above `class ScriptClassPickerDialog(QDialog):` (currently at line 663). First, view the exact current text to anchor the edit:

Current (`Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py:658-666`):
```python



class ScriptClassPickerDialog(QDialog):
    """
    Advanced dialog for picking a C# script class with search, filtering,
    and quick actions.
    
    Displays available classes grouped by project, with recently-used
```

New:
```python


# Sentinel returned by CSharpEditorToolsHandler.OpenScriptPicker() to mean
# "the user explicitly clicked Clear Selection", as distinct from "" which
# means "the user cancelled the dialog / no value was produced". The C++
# call sites (EditorCSharpScriptComponent::OnBrowseScript and
# CSharpScriptClassPropertyHandler's Browse button handler) compare the
# EBus return value against this exact string. It must never collide with
# a real fully-qualified C# class name, which is why it uses characters
# that are illegal in a C# identifier.
SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL = "__O3DESharp_ClearSelection__"
```

Current (`Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py:2639-2667`):
```python
    def OpenScriptPicker(self, current_class):
        """
        Open the script class picker dialog.

        Args:
            current_class: Currently selected class (for pre-selection)

        Returns:
            Selected class name, or empty string if cancelled
        """
        print(f"[O3DESharp] OpenScriptPicker(current_class={current_class!r}) - opening dialog")
        try:
            dialog = ScriptClassPickerDialog(current_class=current_class)
            result = dialog.exec_()
            print(f"[O3DESharp] ScriptClassPickerDialog closed with result={result} (Accepted={QDialog.Accepted})")
            if result == QDialog.Accepted:
                selected = dialog.get_selected_class()
                print(f"[O3DESharp] Selected class: {selected!r}")
                if selected is not None:
                    # Add to recent classes if not empty
                    if selected:
                        self.AddToRecentClasses(selected)
                    return selected
            return ""  # Cancelled
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"[O3DESharp] Error opening script picker: {e}")
            import traceback
            traceback.print_exc()
            return ""
```

New:
```python
    def OpenScriptPicker(self, current_class):
        """
        Open the script class picker dialog.

        Args:
            current_class: Currently selected class (for pre-selection)

        Returns:
            Selected class name; SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL if the user
            explicitly clicked "Clear Selection"; empty string "" if the
            user cancelled the dialog (or an internal error occurred).
        """
        print(f"[O3DESharp] OpenScriptPicker(current_class={current_class!r}) - opening dialog")
        try:
            dialog = ScriptClassPickerDialog(current_class=current_class)
            result = dialog.exec_()
            print(f"[O3DESharp] ScriptClassPickerDialog closed with result={result} (Accepted={QDialog.Accepted})")
            if result == QDialog.Accepted:
                selected = dialog.get_selected_class()
                print(f"[O3DESharp] Selected class: {selected!r}")
                if selected is not None:
                    # Add to recent classes if not empty and not the
                    # "explicit clear" sentinel.
                    if selected and selected != SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL:
                        self.AddToRecentClasses(selected)
                    return selected
            return ""  # Cancelled
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"[O3DESharp] Error opening script picker: {e}")
            import traceback
            traceback.print_exc()
            return ""
```

Note: `show_script_class_picker()` (module-level convenience function at line 2474-2486, used elsewhere for direct in-process calls rather than via the EBus) is untouched by this task — it already returns `dialog.get_selected_class()` verbatim and its own docstring already documents `""` as the "clear" return value for that non-EBus code path. Only the EBus-facing `CSharpEditorToolsHandler.OpenScriptPicker` needed the sentinel, because only that path collapses "clear" and "cancel" to the same wire value.
