- [ ] **Step 4: Fix `EditorCSharpScriptComponent::OnBrowseScript` to treat clear vs cancel differently**

Current (`Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp:248-284`):
```cpp
    AZ::Crc32 EditorCSharpScriptComponent::OnBrowseScript()
    {
        // Go through the CSharpEditorToolsBus instead of inline Python. The bus
        // dispatches to OpenScriptPicker() on the connected Python handler,
        // which pops the dialog AND returns the selected class - so we can
        // assign it directly to the config field. The previous inline-Python
        // implementation opened the dialog but only printed the result, never
        // updating the component, which is why "Browse Scripts..." appeared to
        // do nothing.
        AZ_TracePrintf("O3DESharp", "OnBrowseScript: broadcasting OpenScriptPicker (current='%s')",
            m_config.m_scriptClassName.c_str());

        AZStd::string selectedClass;
        CSharpEditorToolsBus::BroadcastResult(
            selectedClass,
            &CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::OpenScriptPicker,
            m_config.m_scriptClassName);

        AZ_TracePrintf("O3DESharp", "OnBrowseScript: BroadcastResult returned '%s'",
            selectedClass.c_str());

        if (!selectedClass.empty())
        {
            m_config.m_scriptClassName = selectedClass;
            ValidateScript();
            return AZ::Edit::PropertyRefreshLevels::EntireTree;
        }

        // Empty result = user cancelled or the Python EBus handler isn't
        // connected. Warn so the user can tell those two apart.
        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
            "OnBrowseScript: OpenScriptPicker returned empty. Either the user cancelled "
            "or the Python CSharpEditorToolsBus handler is not connected. Check the "
            "console for '[O3DESharp] CSharpEditorToolsBus handler connected' on editor "
            "startup; if missing, csharp_editor_bootstrap did not import the tools module.");
        return AZ::Edit::PropertyRefreshLevels::None;
    }
```

New:
```cpp
    AZ::Crc32 EditorCSharpScriptComponent::OnBrowseScript()
    {
        // Go through the CSharpEditorToolsBus instead of inline Python. The bus
        // dispatches to OpenScriptPicker() on the connected Python handler,
        // which pops the dialog AND returns the selected class - so we can
        // assign it directly to the config field. The previous inline-Python
        // implementation opened the dialog but only printed the result, never
        // updating the component, which is why "Browse Scripts..." appeared to
        // do nothing.
        AZ_TracePrintf("O3DESharp", "OnBrowseScript: broadcasting OpenScriptPicker (current='%s')",
            m_config.m_scriptClassName.c_str());

        AZStd::string selectedClass;
        CSharpEditorToolsBus::BroadcastResult(
            selectedClass,
            &CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::OpenScriptPicker,
            m_config.m_scriptClassName);

        AZ_TracePrintf("O3DESharp", "OnBrowseScript: BroadcastResult returned '%s'",
            selectedClass.c_str());

        // The Python-side picker returns one of three distinct values:
        //   1. A real class name            -> user picked a script.
        //   2. ScriptPickerClearedSentinel   -> user explicitly clicked
        //      "Clear Selection"; blank the field and re-validate exactly
        //      like a normal selection would (this is NOT an error).
        //   3. Empty string ""              -> user cancelled the dialog,
        //      or the Python EBus handler isn't connected. This is the
        //      only case that stays a true no-op.
        if (selectedClass == ScriptPickerClearedSentinel)
        {
            m_config.m_scriptClassName.clear();
            ValidateScript();
            return AZ::Edit::PropertyRefreshLevels::EntireTree;
        }

        if (!selectedClass.empty())
        {
            m_config.m_scriptClassName = selectedClass;
            ValidateScript();
            return AZ::Edit::PropertyRefreshLevels::EntireTree;
        }

        // Empty result = user cancelled or the Python EBus handler isn't
        // connected. Warn so the user can tell those two apart. Explicit
        // "Clear Selection" clicks are handled above and never reach here.
        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false,
            "OnBrowseScript: OpenScriptPicker returned empty. Either the user cancelled "
            "or the Python CSharpEditorToolsBus handler is not connected. Check the "
            "console for '[O3DESharp] CSharpEditorToolsBus handler connected' on editor "
            "startup; if missing, csharp_editor_bootstrap did not import the tools module.");
        return AZ::Edit::PropertyRefreshLevels::None;
    }
```

Now add the `ScriptPickerClearedSentinel` constant that both C++ call sites share. Read the current includes/namespace-open of `EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp` (already confirmed at lines 9-27) and add the constant right after the `namespace O3DESharp {` opening line, before `EditorCSharpScriptConfig::Reflect`:

Current (`Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp:26-31`):
```cpp

{
    // ============================================================
    // EditorCSharpScriptConfig
    // ============================================================
```

New:
```cpp
namespace O3DESharp
{
    // Mirrors SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL in Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py.
    // CSharpEditorToolsBus::OpenScriptPicker returns a plain AZStd::string with
    // no reserved "no value" representation, so this sentinel is the only way
    // for the Python side to tell the C++ side "the user explicitly cleared
    // the field" apart from "the user cancelled / produced nothing" (which is
    // the plain empty string). Keep this string in sync with the Python
    // constant if either side ever changes it.
    static constexpr const char* ScriptPickerClearedSentinel = "__O3DESharp_ClearSelection__";

    // ============================================================
    // EditorCSharpScriptConfig
    // ============================================================
```

```cpp
        QObject::connect(browseBtn, &QPushButton::clicked, [container, comboBox]()
        {
            AZStd::string currentClass = comboBox->currentText().toUtf8().constData();
            AZStd::string selectedClass;

            CSharpEditorToolsBus::BroadcastResult(selectedClass, &CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::OpenScriptPicker, currentClass);

            // "Clear Selection" returns a reserved sentinel (see
            // ScriptPickerClearedSentinel in EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp)
            // distinct from "" (Cancel). Treat an explicit clear as blanking
            // the field and committing that change like a normal selection;

                AzToolsFramework::PropertyEditorGUIMessages::Bus::Broadcast(
                    &AzToolsFramework::PropertyEditorGUIMessages::OnEditingFinished, container);

            {
                comboBox->setCurrentText(selectedClass.c_str());
                comboBox->lineEdit()->selectAll();
                AzToolsFramework::PropertyEditorGUIMessages::Bus::Broadcast(
                    &AzToolsFramework::PropertyEditorGUIMessages::RequestWrite, container);
```

```cpp
    // no reserved "no value" representation, so this sentinel is the only way
    // for the Python side to tell C++ callers "the user explicitly cleared the
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Add a pytest test for the sentinel/cancel distinction**

`csharp_editor_tools.py` imports `PySide2` and `azlmbr` at module scope (confirmed: `from PySide2 import QtWidgets, QtCore, QtGui` at line 24, `import azlmbr.bus as bus` at line 35), neither of which is installed in the CI Python environment (verified: `python -c "import PySide2"` and `python -c "import azlmbr"` both raise `ModuleNotFoundError` in this repo's checkout). There is no existing precedent in `Editor/Tests/` for stubbing `sys.modules` to fake out Qt/azlmbr for a whole-module import, and building that stub layer is out of scope for this fix. Instead, add a narrowly-scoped pytest test that reads the *source text* of `csharp_editor_tools.py` and asserts the sentinel-handling logic is present and self-consistent, without importing the module. This still catches the concrete regression this task fixes (the two return paths collapsing to the same value) if someone reverts the change.

Create `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py`:

```python
#
# Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
# For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
#
# SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
#
"""
Regression tests for the "Clear Selection" vs "Cancel" script picker fix.

csharp_editor_tools.py imports PySide2 and azlmbr at module scope, neither of
which is available outside a running O3DE Editor process, so this module
cannot be imported directly in the CI Python environment. These tests instead
parse the module's source text to verify the sentinel-based fix is present
and internally consistent:
  - _select_none() sets the sentinel, not "".
  - OpenScriptPicker()'s cancelled path still returns "".
  - The sentinel constant is defined exactly once, with a value that cannot
    collide with a legal C# fully-qualified class name (it contains "__"
    surrounding text, which is unusual but technically legal in a C#
    identifier -- the real uniqueness comes from the "ClearSelection"
    payload, asserted below to not look like a class name).
"""

import re
from pathlib import Path

import pytest

_MODULE_PATH = Path(__file__).parent.parent / "Scripts" / "csharp_editor_tools.py"


@pytest.fixture(scope="module")
def source_text() -> str:
    return _MODULE_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8")


@pytest.mark.unit
class TestScriptPickerClearVsCancelSentinel:
    def test_sentinel_constant_defined_once(self, source_text):
        matches = re.findall(
            r'^SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL\s*=\s*"([^"]+)"',
            source_text,
            re.MULTILINE,
        )
        assert len(matches) == 1, (
            "Expected exactly one SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL definition, "
            f"found {len(matches)}"
        )
        sentinel_value = matches[0]
        assert sentinel_value != "", "Sentinel must not itself be the empty string"

    def test_select_none_uses_sentinel_not_empty_string(self, source_text):
        # Isolate the _select_none method body.
        match = re.search(
            r"def _select_none\(self\):.*?(?=\n    def |\Z)",
            source_text,
            re.DOTALL,
        )
        assert match is not None, "_select_none method not found"
        body = match.group(0)

        assert "SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL" in body, (
            "_select_none must assign the sentinel to self._selected_class "
            "so OpenScriptPicker can distinguish explicit clear from cancel"
        )
        # Guard against a regression where someone re-adds a bare ""
        # assignment to _selected_class alongside (or instead of) the
        # sentinel.
        assert 'self._selected_class = ""' not in body, (
            "_select_none must not set _selected_class to a bare empty "
            "string -- that collides with the Cancel return value"
        )

    def test_open_script_picker_cancel_path_returns_empty_string(self, source_text):
        match = re.search(
            r"def OpenScriptPicker\(self, current_class\):.*?(?=\n    def |\Z)",
            source_text,
            re.DOTALL,
        )
        assert match is not None, "OpenScriptPicker method not found"
        body = match.group(0)

        # The line immediately handling the non-Accepted dialog result must
        # still return "" (Cancel semantics are unchanged by this fix).
        assert re.search(r'return\s+""\s*#\s*Cancelled', body), (
            "OpenScriptPicker must still return \"\" for the cancelled path"
        )

    def test_open_script_picker_does_not_add_sentinel_to_recent_classes(self, source_text):
        match = re.search(
            r"def OpenScriptPicker\(self, current_class\):.*?(?=\n    def |\Z)",
            source_text,
            re.DOTALL,
        )
        assert match is not None, "OpenScriptPicker method not found"
        body = match.group(0)

        assert "SCRIPT_PICKER_CLEARED_SENTINEL" in body, (
            "OpenScriptPicker must reference the sentinel (to exclude it "
            "from AddToRecentClasses)"
        )
```

Run it:

```bash
cd F:/O3DESharp/Editor/Tests
python -m pytest test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py -v
```

Expected output: all 4 tests pass, e.g.
```

test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py::TestScriptPickerClearVsCancelSentinel::test_select_none_uses_sentinel_not_empty_string PASSED
test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py::TestScriptPickerClearVsCancelSentinel::test_open_script_picker_cancel_path_returns_empty_string PASSED
test_csharp_editor_tools_picker.py::TestScriptPickerClearVsCancelSentinel::test_open_script_picker_does_not_add_sentinel_to_recent_classes PASSED
```

After building the gem with the Step 4/5 changes, perform this checklist in the O3DE Editor:

1. Launch the O3DE Editor with the O3DESharp gem enabled, open a level, and select (or create) an entity.
2. Add a "C# Script" component to the entity via the Add Component menu.
3. In the component's inspector, set the script class to any valid, compiling C# script class (use the "Browse" button or combo box) so the field is non-empty. Confirm the field shows the class name and no warning appears in the Console panel.

5. In the picker dialog, click **"Clear Selection"**.
   - Expected: the dialog closes, the script class field on the component is now blank, `ValidateScript()` has re-run (the validation status/readout in the inspector updates to reflect "no script" rather than stale "valid" text from the previous class), and the Console panel shows **no** `AZ_Warning` from `OnBrowseScript`.
6. Set the script class again to a valid class (repeat step 3).
7. Reopen the picker (step 4), and this time click **"Cancel"** (the bottom "Cancel" button, not "Clear Selection").
   - Expected: the dialog closes, the script class field is **unchanged** (still shows the previously set class), and the Console panel shows **no** `AZ_Warning` from `OnBrowseScript`.
8. Repeat steps 3-7 using the property handler's own "Browse" button (`CSharpScriptClassPropertyHandler::CreateGUI`'s `browseBtn`, the combo-box row's Browse button) instead of the component's `OnBrowseScript` action, confirming the same two behaviors (explicit clear blanks the combo box and commits via `RequestWrite`/`OnEditingFinished`; Cancel leaves the combo box untouched).
9. As a negative-path sanity check, temporarily stop the Python `CSharpEditorToolsBus` handler from being connected (e.g. rename/disable `csharp_editor_bootstrap`'s import of `csharp_editor_tools` and restart the Editor), then click "Browse Scripts…" again: confirm the `AZ_Warning` in `OnBrowseScript` **does** still appear in this genuine not-connected case (i.e. Step 4's fix did not accidentally silence the legitimate warning, only the false-positive "Clear Selection" case). Restore the import afterward.

```bash
Fix: distinguish explicit script-picker clear from cancel

OpenScriptPicker() returned the same empty string for both "user clicked
```

### Task 13: ValidateScriptClass — wire up the richer Python-side validator

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp:199-240`
- Test: `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_validation.py` (new)

- [ ] **Step 1: Confirm the two validators and why the native one is strictly worse**

Read `Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp:199-240` — the current `ValidateScript()`:

```cpp
    void EditorCSharpScriptComponent::ValidateScript()
    {
        if (m_config.m_scriptClassName.empty())
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "No script class specified";
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
            return;
        }

        // Basic format validation - check for namespace.classname pattern
        if (m_config.m_scriptClassName.find('.') == AZStd::string::npos)
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "Warning: Class should include namespace (e.g., MyGame.MyScript)";
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
            return;
        }

        // If the Coral host is up, ask it whether the class actually exists in any
        // loaded user assembly. This is the only way to catch typos against the
        // live assemblies short of running the game.
        if (ClassExistsInAssembly(m_config.m_scriptClassName, m_config.m_assemblyPath))
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "OK - class found in loaded assemblies";
            m_config.m_isValid = true;
        }
        else
        {
            // Coral host not initialized yet, or the class isn't present in any
            // loaded user assembly. Report the latter; the former only happens
            // in early Activate / before the runtime gem comes up.
            if (auto* coralHost = AZ::Interface<ICoralHostManager>::Get())
            {
                AZ_UNUSED(coralHost);
                m_config.m_validationStatus = "Error: class not found in any loaded assembly";
            }
            else
            {
                m_config.m_validationStatus = "Coral host not initialized yet";
            }
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
        }
    }
```

This only ever tells the user "found in a *loaded* assembly" vs. "not found" vs. "Coral host not initialized yet" — it cannot distinguish "the .cs file doesn't exist at all", "the class exists but derives from the wrong base class", or "the class exists on disk but hasn't been compiled into any loaded assembly yet" (a very common state right after creating a new script, since Coral only loads assemblies that were built).

The already-wired EBus event `CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::ValidateScriptClass` (declared in `Code/Source/Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h:145`, reflected to Python in `Code/Source/Tools/O3DESharpEditorSystemComponent.cpp:144`) dispatches to `CSharpEditorToolsHandler.ValidateScriptClass` in `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py:2582-2637`:

```python
    def ValidateScriptClass(self, class_name):
        """
        Validate a script class name.
        
        Args:
            class_name: Fully qualified class name to validate
            
        Returns:
            ScriptValidationResult dict with validation info
        """
        try:
            # Empty class name is valid (means "no script")
            if not class_name or class_name.strip() == "":
                return {
                    'isValid': True,
                    'message': 'No script class specified',
                    'filePath': '',
                    'baseClass': ''
                }
            
            # Basic format check
            if '.' not in class_name:
                return {
                    'isValid': False,
                    'message': 'Warning: Class should include namespace (e.g., MyGame.MyScript)',
                    'filePath': '',
                    'baseClass': ''
                }
            
            # Check if class exists in any project
            all_classes = self.GetAvailableScriptClasses(scripts_only=False)
            for cls in all_classes:
                if cls['fullName'] == class_name:
                    return {
                        'isValid': True,
                        'message': f"Valid script class (base: {cls['baseClass'] or 'none'})",
                        'filePath': cls['filePath'],
                        'baseClass': cls['baseClass']
                    }
            
            # Class not found - might be valid but not yet compiled
            return {
                'isValid': False,
                'message': f"Class '{class_name}' not found in any C# project. Ensure it's compiled.",
                'filePath': '',
                'baseClass': ''
            }
            
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"[O3DESharp] Error in ValidateScriptClass: {e}")
            return {
                'isValid': False,
                'message': f'Validation error: {str(e)}',
                'filePath': '',
                'baseClass': ''
            }
```

This scans `GetAvailableScriptClasses`, which is built from the real `.cs` files discovered on disk across every registered C# project (`_refresh_cache` → `self.project_manager.list_projects()` / `list_scripts()`), independent of whether Coral has loaded a compiled assembly. So it genuinely distinguishes: (a) empty name — valid/no-op, (b) missing-namespace format warning, (c) found on disk with known base class — success with `filePath`/`baseClass` populated, (d) not found on disk at all / wrong path — the "not found... Ensure it's compiled" message. This is strictly more informative than the native-only check, which can only say "not found in loaded assemblies" for every one of cases (c)-not-yet-built and (d).

The C++ side already has a `ScriptValidationResult` struct with matching fields (`Code/Source/Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h:73-108`, `m_isValid`, `m_message`, `m_filePath`, `m_baseClass`) — it was reflected for exactly this purpose but `ValidateScript()` never calls the bus event.

- [ ] **Step 2: Match the existing "unconnected bus" handling pattern in this file**

`OnBrowseScript()` (same file, lines 248-284) is the existing precedent for calling a `CSharpEditorToolsBus` event and falling back when nothing answers:

```cpp
        AZStd::string selectedClass;
        CSharpEditorToolsBus::BroadcastResult(
            selectedClass,
            &CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::OpenScriptPicker,
            m_config.m_scriptClassName);
        ...
        if (!selectedClass.empty())
        {
            ...
        }

        // Empty result = user cancelled or the Python EBus handler isn't
        // connected. Warn so the user can tell those two apart.
        AZ_Warning("O3DESharp", false, ...);
```

There is no `HasHandlers`/`BusIsConnected` check anywhere in this file — the pattern is simply: call `BroadcastResult` (which is a no-op leaving the out-param at its default-constructed value if nothing is connected, since `AddressPolicy = Single` / `HandlerPolicy = Single` and no handler exists), then branch on whether the result looks "empty"/default. For `ScriptValidationResult` the equivalent empty/default sentinel is `m_message.empty()` (a connected Python handler always sets a non-empty `message` string in every one of its 4 return paths above; a default-constructed `ScriptValidationResult` has `m_isValid = false` and `m_message` empty per `Code/Source/Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h:78-79`).

- [ ] **Step 3: Rewrite `ValidateScript()` to call the bus first, falling back to the native check**

In `Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp`, replace the full body of `ValidateScript()` (lines 199-240):

```cpp
    void EditorCSharpScriptComponent::ValidateScript()
    {
        if (m_config.m_scriptClassName.empty())
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "No script class specified";
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
            return;
        }

        // Basic format validation - check for namespace.classname pattern
        if (m_config.m_scriptClassName.find('.') == AZStd::string::npos)
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "Warning: Class should include namespace (e.g., MyGame.MyScript)";
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
            return;
        }

        // Prefer the Python-side validator reached via CSharpEditorToolsBus. Unlike
        // the native Coral-only check below, it scans the actual .cs files discovered
        // on disk across every registered C# project, so it can distinguish:
        //   - class found and its base class is known (valid, independent of whether
        //     Coral has a compiled assembly loaded yet)
        //   - class not found in any project's .cs files at all (bad name / bad path)
        // versus the native check, which can only ever say "not found in a loaded
        // assembly" for both of those cases. Same "call then check for empty/default
        // result" pattern as OnBrowseScript()/OnEditScript() in this file: if no
        // Python handler is connected, BroadcastResult leaves scriptValidation at its
        // default-constructed value (m_message empty), and we fall through to the
        // native-only check below instead of reporting a false negative.
        ScriptValidationResult scriptValidation;
        CSharpEditorToolsBus::BroadcastResult(
            scriptValidation,
            &CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::ValidateScriptClass,
            m_config.m_scriptClassName);

        if (!scriptValidation.m_message.empty())
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = scriptValidation.m_message;
            m_config.m_isValid = scriptValidation.m_isValid;
            return;
        }

        // No Python CSharpEditorToolsBus handler connected (e.g. csharp_editor_bootstrap
        // did not import the tools module) - fall back to the native-only Coral check.
        // If the Coral host is up, ask it whether the class actually exists in any
        // loaded user assembly. This is a strictly weaker check than the Python path
        // above (it cannot tell "bad path" from "found but not compiled yet"), but it
        // is better than nothing when the Python side is unavailable.
        if (ClassExistsInAssembly(m_config.m_scriptClassName, m_config.m_assemblyPath))
        {
            m_config.m_validationStatus = "OK - class found in loaded assemblies";
            m_config.m_isValid = true;
        }
        else
        {
            // Coral host not initialized yet, or the class isn't present in any
            // loaded user assembly. Report the latter; the former only happens
            // in early Activate / before the runtime gem comes up.
            if (auto* coralHost = AZ::Interface<ICoralHostManager>::Get())
            {
                AZ_UNUSED(coralHost);
                m_config.m_validationStatus = "Error: class not found in any loaded assembly";
            }
            else
            {
                m_config.m_validationStatus = "Coral host not initialized yet";
            }
            m_config.m_isValid = false;
        }
    }
```

Use the Edit tool with this exact `old_string` (the current full method body from Step 1) and `new_string` (the block above).

- [ ] **Step 4: Verify the header already declares everything needed**

`Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.h` already includes `#include <Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h>` transitively via the `.cpp`'s own `#include <Tools/CSharpEditorToolsBus.h>` at line 24 (used by `OnBrowseScript`/`OnCreateScript`/`OnEditScript` already) — `ScriptValidationResult` is declared in that same header, so no new `#include` is needed in either the `.h` or `.cpp`. No signature changes are needed to `ValidateScript()` (still `void`, still reads/writes `m_config` only), so `EditorCSharpScriptComponent.h` requires no edits.

- [ ] **Step 6: Add a pytest test for the Python-side `ValidateScriptClass` logic**

Check first: `grep -rl "ValidateScriptClass" Editor/Tests/` returns nothing — there is no existing coverage of this method, so this is not a duplicate.

`Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py` imports `PySide2` (line 24) and `azlmbr` (line 35) at module scope, and its dependency `Editor/Scripts/csharp_project_manager.py` imports `azlmbr` at module scope too (line 21) — neither package is installed in the TeamCity pytest environment (`.teamcity/settings.kts`'s `PythonTests` build only installs `pip`/`pytest`, see Step 8). Importing `csharp_editor_tools` directly would raise `ModuleNotFoundError` in CI. Stub both modules in `sys.modules` before import, matching this repo's existing test style (`@pytest.mark.unit`, class-based `Test*` suites, as seen in `Editor/Tests/test_gem_dependency_resolver.py`).

Create `Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_validation.py`:

```python
#
# Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
# For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
#
# SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
#
"""
Unit tests for CSharpEditorToolsHandler.ValidateScriptClass.

csharp_editor_tools.py imports PySide2 and azlmbr at module scope (neither is
installed in the CI pytest environment), so both are stubbed out in
sys.modules before import. ValidateScriptClass itself only touches
GetAvailableScriptClasses, string formatting, and dict construction - no Qt
or azlmbr calls - so once the module imports cleanly the method under test
can be exercised directly.
"""

import sys
import types
import pytest
from unittest.mock import MagicMock


def _install_stub_modules():
    """Install minimal fake PySide2 / azlmbr packages so csharp_editor_tools
    imports without the real Qt / O3DE-editor runtime present."""
    if "PySide2" not in sys.modules:
        pyside2 = types.ModuleType("PySide2")

        qtwidgets = types.ModuleType("PySide2.QtWidgets")
        for name in [
            "QDialog", "QVBoxLayout", "QHBoxLayout", "QLabel", "QLineEdit",
            "QPushButton", "QListWidget", "QListWidgetItem", "QComboBox",
            "QCheckBox", "QMessageBox", "QWidget", "QSplitter", "QTextEdit",
            "QGroupBox", "QFormLayout", "QApplication", "QMenu", "QAction",
            "QFileDialog", "QProgressDialog", "QTreeWidget", "QTreeWidgetItem",
            "QAbstractItemView", "QFrame", "QScrollArea", "QSizePolicy",
            "QToolButton", "QStyle",
        ]:
            setattr(qtwidgets, name, MagicMock())

        qtcore = types.ModuleType("PySide2.QtCore")
        qtcore.Qt = MagicMock()
        qtcore.Signal = MagicMock(return_value=MagicMock())
        qtcore.QThread = MagicMock()

        qtgui = types.ModuleType("PySide2.QtGui")
        qtgui.QFont = MagicMock()
        qtgui.QIcon = MagicMock()

        pyside2.QtWidgets = qtwidgets
        pyside2.QtCore = qtcore
        pyside2.QtGui = qtgui

        sys.modules["PySide2"] = pyside2
        sys.modules["PySide2.QtWidgets"] = qtwidgets
        sys.modules["PySide2.QtCore"] = qtcore
        sys.modules["PySide2.QtGui"] = qtgui

    if "azlmbr" not in sys.modules:
        azlmbr = types.ModuleType("azlmbr")
        azlmbr_bus = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.bus")
        azlmbr_editor = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.editor")
        azlmbr_paths = types.ModuleType("azlmbr.paths")
        azlmbr.bus = azlmbr_bus
        azlmbr.editor = azlmbr_editor
        azlmbr.paths = azlmbr_paths

        sys.modules["azlmbr"] = azlmbr
        sys.modules["azlmbr.bus"] = azlmbr_bus
        sys.modules["azlmbr.editor"] = azlmbr_editor
        sys.modules["azlmbr.paths"] = azlmbr_paths


_install_stub_modules()

from csharp_editor_tools import CSharpEditorToolsHandler  # noqa: E402


@pytest.mark.unit
class TestValidateScriptClass:
    """Test suite for CSharpEditorToolsHandler.ValidateScriptClass."""

    @pytest.fixture
    def handler(self, monkeypatch):
        """A CSharpEditorToolsHandler with project-manager construction
        short-circuited, so tests don't depend on a real project layout."""
        monkeypatch.setattr(
            "csharp_editor_tools.get_project_manager",
            lambda: MagicMock(),
        )
        return CSharpEditorToolsHandler()

    def test_empty_class_name_is_valid(self, handler):
        """Empty class name means 'no script' and is reported valid."""
        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("")

        assert result["isValid"] is True
        assert result["message"] == "No script class specified"
        assert result["filePath"] == ""
        assert result["baseClass"] == ""

    def test_whitespace_only_class_name_is_valid(self, handler):
        """Whitespace-only class name is treated the same as empty."""
        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("   ")

        assert result["isValid"] is True
        assert result["message"] == "No script class specified"

    def test_missing_namespace_is_invalid(self, handler):
        """A class name with no '.' fails the namespace format check."""
        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("MyScript")

        assert result["isValid"] is False
        assert "namespace" in result["message"].lower()

    def test_class_found_on_disk_is_valid_with_metadata(self, handler, monkeypatch):
        """A class discovered on disk is valid and returns its real file
        path / base class - this is the case the native-only Coral check
        cannot distinguish from 'not found', because a freshly-created
        script may not be in a loaded assembly yet."""
        monkeypatch.setattr(
            handler,
            "GetAvailableScriptClasses",
            lambda scripts_only=True: [
                {
                    "fullName": "MyGame.PlayerController",
                    "className": "PlayerController",
                    "namespace": "MyGame",
                    "projectName": "MyGame",
                    "filePath": "C:/MyProject/Scripts/PlayerController.cs",
                    "baseClass": "ScriptComponent",
                    "isScriptComponent": True,
                    "isRecent": False,
                }
            ],
        )

        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("MyGame.PlayerController")

        assert result["isValid"] is True
        assert result["baseClass"] == "ScriptComponent"
        assert result["filePath"] == "C:/MyProject/Scripts/PlayerController.cs"
        assert "PlayerController" not in result["message"]  # message reports base class, not re-echoing name
        assert "ScriptComponent" in result["message"]

    def test_class_not_found_reports_not_compiled_hint(self, handler, monkeypatch):
        """A well-formed name that matches no discovered .cs file (bad path,
        typo, or a script that hasn't been compiled yet) gets the specific
        'not found ... Ensure it's compiled' message, with no stale
        filePath/baseClass."""
        monkeypatch.setattr(
            handler, "GetAvailableScriptClasses", lambda scripts_only=True: []
        )

        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("MyGame.DoesNotExist")

        assert result["isValid"] is False
        assert "MyGame.DoesNotExist" in result["message"]
        assert "compiled" in result["message"].lower()
        assert result["filePath"] == ""
        assert result["baseClass"] == ""

    def test_exception_in_lookup_is_caught_and_reported(self, handler, monkeypatch):
        """If GetAvailableScriptClasses blows up, ValidateScriptClass must
        not propagate - it should degrade to an isValid=False result."""
        def _raise(scripts_only=True):
            raise RuntimeError("simulated project scan failure")

        monkeypatch.setattr(handler, "GetAvailableScriptClasses", _raise)

        result = handler.ValidateScriptClass("MyGame.PlayerController")

        assert result["isValid"] is False
        assert "simulated project scan failure" in result["message"]
```

No edits to `.teamcity/settings.kts` are required for this task.

- [ ] **Step 9: Manual verification of the C++ wiring change**

Automated coverage above proves the Python validator's own branching is correct; this step confirms the C++ side actually calls it and falls back correctly, which requires a live O3DE Editor process:

1. Launch the O3DE Editor with the O3DESharp gem enabled, on a project that has at least one discovered C# project under `Scripts/`, `CSharp/`, or `Gem/Code/Scripts/`.
2. Confirm the console shows `[O3DESharp] CSharpEditorToolsBus handler connected` during editor startup (proves the Python handler is wired).
3. Create an entity, add a "C# Script" component to it.
4. In the component's "Script Class Name" field, type `MyGame.DoesNotExistScript` (a namespaced name that does not correspond to any real `.cs` file) and press Enter/Tab to commit the edit.
5. Confirm the inspector's validation status readout now shows: `Class 'MyGame.DoesNotExistScript' not found in any C# project. Ensure it's compiled.` — NOT the old generic `Error: class not found in any loaded assembly` or `Coral host not initialized yet`.
6. Change the field to a real, already-compiled script class that exists in a loaded assembly (e.g. an existing sample script's fully-qualified name). Confirm the status now shows `Valid script class (base: <BaseClassName>)` — proving the success path also switched to the richer message instead of the old `OK - class found in loaded assemblies`.
7. As a fallback-path check: temporarily rename/comment out the `azlmbr.editor.CSharpEditorToolsBusHandler()` connect call in `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_bootstrap.py` (or otherwise prevent the Python tools module from loading), restart the Editor, and repeat step 4. Confirm the status now falls back to one of the two original native-only messages (`Error: class not found in any loaded assembly` or `Coral host not initialized yet`) instead of silently showing an empty/blank status — this proves the "no handler connected" fallback branch (`scriptValidation.m_message.empty()`) works. Revert the temporary change afterward.

- [ ] **Step 10: Commit**

```bash
git add Code/Source/Tools/Components/EditorCSharpScriptComponent.cpp Editor/Tests/test_csharp_editor_tools_validation.py
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Fix: wire ValidateScript() to the richer Python-side validator

EditorCSharpScriptComponent::ValidateScript() only ever checked whether
the class was present in a Coral-loaded assembly, so it could not tell
a bad file path apart from a class that simply hadn't been compiled
yet. CSharpEditorToolsBus::Events::ValidateScriptClass already existed
and is backed by a Python handler that scans the actual .cs files
discovered on disk, returning a specific filePath/baseClass/message -
but nothing called it. ValidateScript() now calls that bus event first
and falls back to the native Coral-only check only when no Python
handler is connected, following the same BroadcastResult-then-check
pattern already used by OnBrowseScript()/OnEditScript() in this file.
EOF
)"
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Update TeamCity CI — remove the now-unnecessary .NET 8.0 SDK install and stale "(net8 tool)" labels**

Read `.teamcity/settings.kts` yourself first — the block structure is duplicated once for the Linux build type (`CSharpLinux`, roughly lines 60-192) and once for Windows (`CSharpWindows`, roughly lines 198+). Only the Linux job explicitly installs a .NET 8.0 SDK; it exists solely because the BindingGenerator tool used to require net8.0. After Step 1, nothing in this repo targets net8.0 anymore, so this install step and its surrounding comments become dead weight — remove them so the CI script accurately reflects what's actually needed.

The top-of-file doc comment currently reads (lines 43-52):

```kotlin
 * DOTNET RUNNER NOTE: we use plain `script { }` build steps that
 * invoke the explicit dotnet binary path, NOT TC's dotnetBuild /
 * dotnetTest runners. Reason: TC's Linux cloud agent ships with
 * .NET 8.0 preinstalled at /usr/share/dotnet, but we need .NET 9
 * for O3DE.Core. The dotnet* runners locate the dotnet binary
 * eagerly (before the previous step's ##teamcity[setParameter] PATH
 * update takes effect), so they always pick up 8.0 from
 * /usr/share/dotnet and fail with NETSDK1045 "current .NET SDK does
 * not support targeting .NET 9.0". script-runner steps that call
 * $HOME/.dotnet/dotnet directly sidestep the discovery entirely.
 */
```

Replace with (this keeps the still-true explanation of why we use explicit `script{}` steps instead of the `dotnetBuild`/`dotnetTest` runners, but drops the now-obsolete "we need both 8 and 9" framing):

```kotlin
 * DOTNET RUNNER NOTE: we use plain `script { }` build steps that
 * invoke the explicit dotnet binary path, NOT TC's dotnetBuild /
 * dotnetTest runners. Reason: TC's Linux cloud agent ships with an
 * older .NET SDK preinstalled at /usr/share/dotnet, but every C#
 * project in this repo now targets net9.0 (or netstandard2.0 for
 * the MSBuild task). The dotnet* runners locate the dotnet binary
 * eagerly (before the previous step's ##teamcity[setParameter] PATH
 * update takes effect), so they always pick up the preinstalled SDK
 * from /usr/share/dotnet and fail with NETSDK1045 "current .NET SDK
 * does not support targeting .NET 9.0". script-runner steps that
 * call $HOME/.dotnet/dotnet directly sidestep the discovery entirely.
 */
```

The Linux SDK-install step currently reads (lines 107-125):

```kotlin
    steps {
        script {
            name = "Install .NET 8.0 + 9.0 SDKs"
            scriptContent = """
                set -e
                # dotnet-install: idempotent installer that drops the
                # SDK into $HOME/.dotnet. We install both 8 (for the
                # BindingGenerator tool) and 9 (for O3DE.Core and the
                # smoke consumer); the system-preinstalled 8 at
                # /usr/share/dotnet does not include 9, so without
                # this step the build fails with NETSDK1045.
                if [ ! -f /tmp/dotnet-install.sh ]; then
                    curl -sSL https://dot.net/v1/dotnet-install.sh -o /tmp/dotnet-install.sh
                    chmod +x /tmp/dotnet-install.sh
                fi
                /tmp/dotnet-install.sh --channel 8.0 --install-dir "${'$'}HOME/.dotnet"
                /tmp/dotnet-install.sh --channel 9.0 --install-dir "${'$'}HOME/.dotnet"
                "${'$'}HOME/.dotnet/dotnet" --list-sdks
            """.trimIndent()
        }
```

### Task 16: Binding generator — clear warning on malformed `binding_config.json`

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Configuration/BindingConfigLoader.cs:37-60`
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Program.cs:392,410`
- Test: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/BindingConfigLoaderTests.cs` (new)

- [ ] **Step 1: Give `BindingConfigLoader.Load` a way to signal a parse failure**

The current method swallows the exception, prints a console line itself, and returns defaults — the caller (`Program.cs`) has no way to know parsing failed, so it goes on to print a success-looking `Configuration: {path}` line even when the file existed but failed to parse. Add an `out bool usedDefaultDueToError` parameter that is `true` only when the file existed but could not be parsed, and stop printing from inside the loader so `Program.cs` owns all user-facing messaging for this step.

Current code in `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Configuration/BindingConfigLoader.cs` (lines 32-60):

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Load configuration from a JSON file
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="configPath">Path to the configuration file</param>
        /// <returns>Loaded configuration, or default if file doesn't exist</returns>
        public static BindingConfig Load(string configPath)
        {
            if (!File.Exists(configPath))
            {
                Console.WriteLine($"Configuration file not found: {configPath}");
                Console.WriteLine("Using default configuration.");
                return CreateDefault();
            }

            try
            {
                var json = File.ReadAllText(configPath);
                var config = JsonSerializer.Deserialize<BindingConfig>(json, JsonOptions);
                config ??= CreateDefault();
                ExpandEnvironmentVariables(config);
                return config;
            }
            catch (Exception ex)
            {
                Console.WriteLine($"Error loading configuration: {ex.Message}");
                Console.WriteLine("Using default configuration.");
                return CreateDefault();
            }
        }
```

Replace it with:

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Load configuration from a JSON file
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="configPath">Path to the configuration file</param>
        /// <param name="parseErrorMessage">
        /// Set to the exception message if <paramref name="configPath"/> exists but
        /// failed to parse (malformed JSON, I/O error, etc.), and <see langword="null"/>
        /// otherwise (including the "file not found" case, which is not an error -
        /// it's the normal first-run experience). Callers use this to distinguish
        /// "no config file, using defaults" from "config file is broken, using
        /// defaults" and warn the user accordingly.
        /// </param>
        /// <returns>Loaded configuration, or default if the file doesn't exist or failed to parse</returns>
        public static BindingConfig Load(string configPath, out string? parseErrorMessage)
        {
            parseErrorMessage = null;

            if (!File.Exists(configPath))
            {
                return CreateDefault();
            }

            try
            {
                var json = File.ReadAllText(configPath);
                var config = JsonSerializer.Deserialize<BindingConfig>(json, JsonOptions);
                config ??= CreateDefault();
                ExpandEnvironmentVariables(config);
                return config;
            }
            catch (Exception ex)
            {
                parseErrorMessage = ex.Message;
                return CreateDefault();
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Load configuration from a JSON file, discarding parse-error details.
        /// Prefer the <see cref="Load(string, out string?)"/> overload for any
        /// caller that surfaces status to the user.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="configPath">Path to the configuration file</param>
        /// <returns>Loaded configuration, or default if the file doesn't exist or failed to parse</returns>
        public static BindingConfig Load(string configPath)
        {
            return Load(configPath, out _);
        }
```

This keeps the old single-argument `Load(string)` working (defaults-on-failure, exit code unchanged) for any external/undiscovered callers, while `Program.cs` switches to the new overload to get failure detail. Note the "file not found" console lines that used to live in the loader are intentionally removed here — `Program.cs` already prints its own `Configuration: {path or "default"}` line right after `Load` returns, and Step 2 makes that line distinguish all three cases (not found / parse failed / loaded fine) in one place instead of two overlapping messages.

- [ ] **Step 2: Replace the misleading success-looking console line in `Program.cs`**

Current code in `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Program.cs` (lines 390-410):

```csharp
                // Load configuration
                var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(configPath);
                config.Global.Verbose = verbose;
                config.Global.IncrementalBuild = incremental;

                // Override require attribute setting if specified
                if (requireAttribute)
                {
                    config.Global.RequireExportAttribute = requireAttribute;
                }

                // Override C# output path if --output is specified
                if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(csharpOutputDir))
                {
                    // When --output is specified, write each gem's bindings to a subdirectory
                    var absOutput = Path.GetFullPath(csharpOutputDir);
                    config.Global.CSharpOutputPath = Path.Combine(absOutput, "{GemName}");
                }

                Console.WriteLine($"Configuration: {(File.Exists(configPath) ? configPath : "default")}");
```

Replace it with:

```csharp
                // Load configuration
                var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(configPath, out var configParseError);
                config.Global.Verbose = verbose;
                config.Global.IncrementalBuild = incremental;

                // Override require attribute setting if specified
                if (requireAttribute)
                {
                    config.Global.RequireExportAttribute = requireAttribute;
                }

                // Override C# output path if --output is specified
                if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(csharpOutputDir))
                {
                    // When --output is specified, write each gem's bindings to a subdirectory
                    var absOutput = Path.GetFullPath(csharpOutputDir);
                    config.Global.CSharpOutputPath = Path.Combine(absOutput, "{GemName}");
                }

                // NOTE: exit code and fallback-to-defaults behavior are unchanged on
                // purpose - existing automated invocations that point --config at a
                // missing or broken file must keep working. This only fixes the
                // console message so a broken config file doesn't look identical to
                // a successfully loaded one.
                if (configParseError != null)
                {
                    Console.WriteLine($"WARNING: failed to parse {configPath} ({configParseError}) - using default configuration");
                }
                else
                {
                    Console.WriteLine($"Configuration: {(File.Exists(configPath) ? configPath : "default")}");
                }
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Add the config-loader test file**

Create `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/BindingConfigLoaderTests.cs`:

```csharp
//
// Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
// For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
//
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
//

using System;
using System.IO;
using O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Configuration;

namespace O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Tests;

/// <summary>
/// Tests for <see cref="BindingConfigLoader"/>'s failure-handling paths. A
/// missing config file and a malformed config file must both fall back to
/// defaults without throwing or changing the process exit code, but callers
/// need to be able to tell the two cases apart so a broken file can be
/// surfaced as a warning instead of looking like a clean load.
/// </summary>
public class BindingConfigLoaderTests : IDisposable
{
    private readonly string _tempConfigPath;

    public BindingConfigLoaderTests()
    {
        _tempConfigPath = Path.Combine(Path.GetTempPath(), $"binding_config_{Guid.NewGuid():N}.json");
    }

    public void Dispose()
    {
        if (File.Exists(_tempConfigPath))
        {
            File.Delete(_tempConfigPath);
        }
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Load_MalformedJson_ReturnsDefaultsAndReportsParseError()
    {
        // Arrange
        File.WriteAllText(_tempConfigPath, "{ this is not valid json ][");

        // Act
        var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(_tempConfigPath, out var parseErrorMessage);

        // Assert
        var defaults = BindingConfigLoader.CreateDefault();
        config.Global.CSharpNamespace.Should().Be(defaults.Global.CSharpNamespace);
        config.Global.CSharpOutputPath.Should().Be(defaults.Global.CSharpOutputPath);
        config.Global.CppOutputPath.Should().Be(defaults.Global.CppOutputPath);
        config.Global.RequireExportAttribute.Should().Be(defaults.Global.RequireExportAttribute);
        config.Global.IncludePaths.Should().Equal(defaults.Global.IncludePaths);
        config.Gems.Should().BeEmpty();

        parseErrorMessage.Should().NotBeNull("a malformed file must report a parse error so callers can warn about it");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Load_MissingFile_ReturnsDefaultsWithNoParseError()
    {
        // Arrange - _tempConfigPath is a valid path that was never created.

        // Act
        var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(_tempConfigPath, out var parseErrorMessage);

        // Assert
        var defaults = BindingConfigLoader.CreateDefault();
        config.Global.CSharpOutputPath.Should().Be(defaults.Global.CSharpOutputPath);

        parseErrorMessage.Should().BeNull("a missing file is the normal first-run case, not a parse error");
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Load_ValidJson_ReturnsParsedValuesWithNoParseError()
    {
        // Arrange
        File.WriteAllText(_tempConfigPath, """
        {
          "global": {
            "csharpNamespace": "MyGame",
            "requireExportAttribute": true
          }
        }
        """);

        // Act
        var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(_tempConfigPath, out var parseErrorMessage);

        // Assert
        config.Global.CSharpNamespace.Should().Be("MyGame");
        config.Global.RequireExportAttribute.Should().BeTrue();
        parseErrorMessage.Should().BeNull();
    }

    [Fact]
    public void Load_SingleArgumentOverload_StillFallsBackToDefaultsOnMalformedJson()
    {
        // Arrange - the old single-argument overload must keep working for any
        // caller that hasn't been migrated to the out-parameter overload.
        File.WriteAllText(_tempConfigPath, "{ not json");

        // Act
        var config = BindingConfigLoader.Load(_tempConfigPath);

        // Assert
        var defaults = BindingConfigLoader.CreateDefault();
        config.Global.CSharpOutputPath.Should().Be(defaults.Global.CSharpOutputPath);
    }
}
```

```bash
BindingGen: warn clearly when binding_config.json fails to parse

BindingConfigLoader.Load silently fell back to defaults on malformed
JSON, and Program.cs's "Configuration: {path}" console line looked
identical whether the file loaded cleanly or failed to parse - the
only difference was a line printed from inside the loader that scrolled
by earlier in the output. Load now has an out-parameter overload that
reports the parse exception message to the caller, and Program.cs uses
```

### Task 17: Zero-bindings result gives no actionable reason at default verbosity

**Files:**
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/ParsedBindings.cs:1-47`
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEHeaderParser.cs:96-106,374-419,540-549,650-660`
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Generation/MultiGemBindingGenerator.cs:24-31,69-134,195-199`

- [ ] **Step 1: Add skip-reason counters to `ParsedBindings`**

Currently `ParsedBindings` (`Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/ParsedBindings.cs`) has no notion of *why* a class was skipped — the parser computes the reasons inline (see Step 2) but only logs them behind `_verbose`, and nothing aggregates them. Read the current top of the file:

```csharp
namespace O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Parsing
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Container for all parsed binding declarations from C++ headers
    /// </summary>
    public class ParsedBindings
    {
        /// <summary>
        /// Gem this binding belongs to
        /// </summary>
        public string GemName { get; set; } = string.Empty;

        /// <summary>
        /// Parsed class declarations
        /// </summary>
        public List<ParsedClass> Classes { get; set; } = new List<ParsedClass>();

        /// <summary>
        /// Parsed function declarations
        /// </summary>
        public List<ParsedFunction> Functions { get; set; } = new List<ParsedFunction>();

        /// <summary>
        /// Parsed enum declarations
        /// </summary>
        public List<ParsedEnum> Enums { get; set; } = new List<ParsedEnum>();

        /// <summary>
        /// Every header file libclang touched while parsing this gem - the gem's
        /// own headers plus everything they transitively #include. Used by
        /// BuildCache to invalidate when an upstream header (e.g. AzCore math)
        /// changes, even though the gem's own headers did not.
        ///
        /// Populated by O3DEHeaderParser. Excludes system headers.
        /// </summary>
        public HashSet<string> SourceFiles { get; } = new HashSet<string>(System.StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase);
    }
```

Add a `SkipReasonCategory` enum and a `SkippedClassCounts` dictionary field right after `SourceFiles`, and initialize it eagerly (so every category is always present with a `0` entry — this lets the summary line report "0 missing X" instead of omitting categories that never fired):

```csharp
        /// <summary>
        /// Every header file libclang touched while parsing this gem - the gem's
        /// own headers plus everything they transitively #include. Used by
        /// BuildCache to invalidate when an upstream header (e.g. AzCore math)
        /// changes, even though the gem's own headers did not.
        ///
        /// Populated by O3DEHeaderParser. Excludes system headers.
        /// </summary>
        public HashSet<string> SourceFiles { get; } = new HashSet<string>(System.StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase);

        /// <summary>
        /// Count of classes/structs skipped during parsing, bucketed by reason.
        /// Populated by O3DEHeaderParser regardless of verbosity - the counts
        /// themselves are cheap to collect, and MultiGemBindingGenerator uses
        /// them to print an unconditional one-line summary when a generation
        /// run produces zero bindings, so the run doesn't look like it silently
        /// did nothing. Verbose mode still prints a line for each individual
        /// skip; this dictionary is the aggregate.
        /// </summary>
        public Dictionary<SkippedClassReason, int> SkippedClassCounts { get; } =
            new Dictionary<SkippedClassReason, int>
            {
                [SkippedClassReason.MissingExportAttribute] = 0,
                [SkippedClassReason.FilteredName] = 0,
                [SkippedClassReason.NoBindableMembers] = 0,
            };
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Why O3DEHeaderParser skipped a class/struct declaration entirely
    /// (i.e. it never made it into ParsedBindings.Classes).
    /// </summary>
    public enum SkippedClassReason
    {
        /// <summary>
        /// requireExportAttribute is on for this gem and the class declaration
        /// itself has no O3DE_EXPORT_CSHARP annotation. The class is skipped
        /// before ProcessClass ever runs, so its members are never inspected.
        /// </summary>
        MissingExportAttribute,

        /// <summary>
        /// O3DEHeaderParser.ShouldSkipClass matched the name (template
        /// specialization, AZStd/std internal type, iterator, or an
        /// Editor-prefixed class declared inline in a non-editor header).
        /// </summary>
        FilteredName,

        /// <summary>
        /// The class passed the name filters and its export-attribute gate,
        /// but after walking its members it had zero bindable public
        /// methods/properties (everything was private/protected, un-bindable
        /// types, pure-virtual, or filtered method names like operators/RTTI).
        /// </summary>
        NoBindableMembers,
    }
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Increment the counters at the three real skip points in `O3DEHeaderParser`**

Read the current top-level export-attribute gate (the currently-unlogged skip point) in `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEHeaderParser.cs`:

```csharp
                    // Check if we require the export attribute
                    if (_requireExportAttribute && !HasExportAttribute(childCursor))
                    {
                        return CXChildVisitResult.CXChildVisit_Continue;
                    }
```

This gate applies to every top-level declaration kind (class, function, enum), but the skip-reason category we're counting (`MissingExportAttribute`) is specifically about classes going into the zero-bindings summary, so only increment when the skipped cursor is actually a class/struct declaration. Replace it with:

```csharp
                    // Check if we require the export attribute
                    if (_requireExportAttribute && !HasExportAttribute(childCursor))
                    {
                        if (childCursor.Kind == CXCursorKind.CXCursor_ClassDecl ||
                            childCursor.Kind == CXCursorKind.CXCursor_StructDecl)
                        {
                            bindings.SkippedClassCounts[SkippedClassReason.MissingExportAttribute]++;
                        }
                        return CXChildVisitResult.CXChildVisit_Continue;
                    }
```

Next, the name-filter skip inside `ProcessClass` (currently verbose-only). Read the current code:

```csharp

            // Skip classes with invalid/un-bindable names
            if (ShouldSkipClass(className))
            {
                Log($"  Skipping class: {className} (filtered)");
                return;
            }
```

Replace with:

```csharp
        private unsafe void ProcessClass(CXCursor cursor, ParsedBindings bindings, string sourceFile)
        {
            var className = cursor.Spelling.ToString();

            // Skip classes with invalid/un-bindable names
            if (ShouldSkipClass(className))
            {
                Log($"  Skipping class: {className} (filtered)");
                bindings.SkippedClassCounts[SkippedClassReason.FilteredName]++;
                return;
            }
```

Finally, the "no bindable members" skip at the end of `ProcessClass`. Read the current code:

```csharp
            }
            else
            {
                Log($"  Skipping class: {parsedClass.QualifiedName} (no bindable members)");
            }
        }
```

Replace with:

```csharp
            // Only add class if it has usable public methods or properties

                bindings.Classes.Add(parsedClass);
                Log($"  Found class: {parsedClass.QualifiedName} with {parsedClass.Methods.Count} methods, {parsedClass.Properties.Count} properties");
            }
            else
            {
                Log($"  Skipping class: {parsedClass.QualifiedName} (no bindable members)");
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Aggregate per-gem skip counts and print the unconditional zero-bindings summary in `MultiGemBindingGenerator`**

Add an aggregate skip-count dictionary so it survives past the per-gem `ParsedBindings` objects, which go out of scope after each gem is processed:

```csharp
    public class GenerationResult
    {
        public int ClassesGenerated { get; set; }
        public int FilesWritten { get; set; }
        public int GemsProcessed { get; set; }
        public int GemsSkipped { get; set; }
        public List<string> ProcessedGemNames { get; set; } = new List<string>();

        /// <summary>
        /// Aggregate class skip-reason counts across every gem processed in
        /// this run. Populated by MultiGemBindingGenerator.GenerateAll from
        /// each gem's ParsedBindings.SkippedClassCounts. Used to print an
        /// actionable one-line summary when ClassesGenerated is 0 - see
        /// GenerateAll's post-loop block.
        /// </summary>
        public Dictionary<Parsing.SkippedClassReason, int> SkippedClassCounts { get; } =
            new Dictionary<Parsing.SkippedClassReason, int>
            {
                [Parsing.SkippedClassReason.MissingExportAttribute] = 0,
                [Parsing.SkippedClassReason.FilteredName] = 0,
                [Parsing.SkippedClassReason.NoBindableMembers] = 0,
            };
```

Now update `GenerateAll`'s call site and post-loop block. Read the current loop and post-loop code:

```csharp
            foreach (var gem in sortedGems)
            {
                try
                {
                    var (generated, classCount, fileCount) = GenerateGemBindings(gem, gems, projectPath, csharpGenerator, cppGenerator, projectGenerator, metadataGenerator, extensionGenerator);
                    if (generated)
                    {
                        result.GemsProcessed++;
                        result.ClassesGenerated += classCount;
                        result.FilesWritten += fileCount;
                        result.ProcessedGemNames.Add(gem.GemName);
                    }
                    else
                    {
                        result.GemsSkipped++;
                    }
                }
                catch (Exception ex)
                {
                    Console.WriteLine($"Error generating bindings for gem '{gem.GemName}': {ex.Message}");
                    if (_verbose)
                    {
                        Console.WriteLine(ex.StackTrace);
                    }
                }
            }

            // Save the cache
            _buildCache?.Save();

            Log($"Binding generation complete! Generated: {result.GemsProcessed}, Skipped (cached): {result.GemsSkipped}");

            // Output machine-readable summary for orchestrator scripts
            Console.WriteLine($"Generated {result.ClassesGenerated} classes in {result.FilesWritten} files");
            if (result.ProcessedGemNames.Count > 0)
            {
                Console.WriteLine($"Processed gems: {string.Join(", ", result.ProcessedGemNames)}");
            }

            return result;
        }
```

Replace with:

```csharp
            foreach (var gem in sortedGems)
            {
                try
                {
                    var (generated, classCount, fileCount, skippedClassCounts) = GenerateGemBindings(gem, gems, projectPath, csharpGenerator, cppGenerator, projectGenerator, metadataGenerator, extensionGenerator);
                    if (generated)
                    {
                        result.GemsProcessed++;
                        result.ClassesGenerated += classCount;
                        result.FilesWritten += fileCount;
                        result.ProcessedGemNames.Add(gem.GemName);
                    }
                    else
                    {
                        result.GemsSkipped++;
                    }

                    if (skippedClassCounts != null)
                    {
                        foreach (var (reason, count) in skippedClassCounts)
                        {
                            result.SkippedClassCounts[reason] = result.SkippedClassCounts.GetValueOrDefault(reason) + count;
                        }
                    }
                }
                catch (Exception ex)
                {
                    Console.WriteLine($"Error generating bindings for gem '{gem.GemName}': {ex.Message}");
                    if (_verbose)
                    {
                        Console.WriteLine(ex.StackTrace);
                    }
                }
            }

            // Save the cache
            _buildCache?.Save();

            Log($"Binding generation complete! Generated: {result.GemsProcessed}, Skipped (cached): {result.GemsSkipped}");

            // Output machine-readable summary for orchestrator scripts
            Console.WriteLine($"Generated {result.ClassesGenerated} classes in {result.FilesWritten} files");
            if (result.ProcessedGemNames.Count > 0)
            {
                Console.WriteLine($"Processed gems: {string.Join(", ", result.ProcessedGemNames)}");
            }

            // Unconditional (non-verbose-gated) actionable summary for the
            // all-zero case. Without --verbose, a run that discovers gems,
            // finds headers, parses them, and still emits nothing looks
            // identical to a run that is silently broken. The per-reason
            // counts here are the same ones verbose mode already logs per
            // class (see O3DEHeaderParser.ProcessClass / ParseHeaderFile) -
            // this just adds up what was already being computed and prints
            // it once, regardless of verbosity.
            if (result.ClassesGenerated == 0)
            {
                var totalSkipped = result.SkippedClassCounts.Values.Sum();
                if (totalSkipped > 0)
                {
                    var parts = new List<string>();
                    var noBindable = result.SkippedClassCounts.GetValueOrDefault(Parsing.SkippedClassReason.NoBindableMembers);
                    if (noBindable > 0)
                    {
                        parts.Add($"{noBindable} had no bindable public members");
                    }
                    var missingExport = result.SkippedClassCounts.GetValueOrDefault(Parsing.SkippedClassReason.MissingExportAttribute);
                    if (missingExport > 0)
                    {
                        parts.Add($"{missingExport} missing O3DE_EXPORT_CSHARP");
                    }
                    var filtered = result.SkippedClassCounts.GetValueOrDefault(Parsing.SkippedClassReason.FilteredName);
                    if (filtered > 0)
                    {
                        parts.Add($"{filtered} filtered by name (template/AZStd/std/iterator/Editor-prefixed)");
                    }
                    Console.WriteLine($"Skipped {totalSkipped} classes: {string.Join(", ", parts)}");
                }
            }

            return result;
        }
```

This requires `System.Linq` for `.Sum()`, which the file already imports (`using System.Linq;` is present at the top of `MultiGemBindingGenerator.cs`) — no using-directive change needed. `GetValueOrDefault` on `Dictionary<TKey,TValue>` needs no extra using either (it is a `Dictionary<TKey,TValue>` instance method in `System.Collections.Generic`, already imported).


```
    0 Error(s)
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Add the regression test**

Read `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/GeneratorUnitTests.cs`'s existing `using` block and namespace declaration (already shown above) — the new test needs `System;`, `System.IO;`, and the three generator namespaces the file already imports (`O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Caching`, `O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Configuration`, `O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Generation`, `O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.GemDiscovery` — the last one is new and must be added), plus a way to capture `Console.Out`.

Insert this block immediately before that final `}`:

```csharp

    // --------------------------------------------------------------------
    // Zero-bindings summary: an all-skipped generation run must print an
    // unconditional (non-verbose) one-line reason, not silence.
    // --------------------------------------------------------------------

    [Fact]
    public void GenerateAll_ZeroBindableClasses_PrintsActionableSummary()
    {
        // Arrange: a gem whose only header declares two classes that both
        // get skipped, for two different reasons:
        //   - PrivateOnly: public class, but every member is private, so
        //     ProcessClass finds zero bindable methods/properties
        //     (SkippedClassReason.NoBindableMembers).
        //   - AZStd::internal-style name: ShouldSkipClass filters it by
        //     name before it is even inspected for members
        //     (SkippedClassReason.FilteredName). We trigger this using the
        //     "iterator" name-pattern match, which is easiest to produce
        //     from a plain header: a class literally named "MyIterator"
        //     matches the "iterator" substring rule in SkippedClassPatterns.
        var tempDir = Path.Combine(Path.GetTempPath(), Path.GetRandomFileName());
        var projectPath = TestFixtures.CreateMockProject("ZeroBindingsProject");
        var gemName = "EmptyGem";
        var gemPath = TestFixtures.CreateMockGem(projectPath, gemName);

        try
        {
            // CreateMockGem already wrote one bindable sample header
            // (EmptyGemClass.h) under Code/Include/EmptyGem - delete it so
            // this gem truly produces zero bindings, then write our own
            // all-skipped header in its place.
            var includePath = Path.Combine(gemPath, "Code", "Include", gemName);
            foreach (var existing in Directory.GetFiles(includePath, "*.h"))
            {
                File.Delete(existing);
            }

            var headerContent = @"
#pragma once
#include <AzCore/Math/Vector3.h>

namespace O3DE {

    // Public class with zero bindable members - every member is private.
    class PrivateOnly {
    public:
        PrivateOnly();
    private:
        void InternalDoThing();
        AZ::Vector3 m_position;
    };

    // Filtered by name - ""iterator"" substring matches SkippedClassPatterns.
    class MyIterator {
    public:
        void Advance();
    };
}
";
            var headerPath = Path.Combine(includePath, "EmptyGemHeader.h");
            File.WriteAllText(headerPath, headerContent);

            var gems = new Dictionary<string, GemDescriptor>
            {
                [gemName] = new GemDescriptor { GemName = gemName, GemPath = gemPath, IsEnabled = true },
            };
            var sortedGems = new List<GemDescriptor> { gems[gemName] };

            var config = new BindingConfig();
            config.Global.IncrementalBuild = false;
            config.Gems[gemName] = new GemSettings
            {
                Enabled = true,
                HeaderPatterns = new List<string> { "Code/Include/**/*.h" },
                ExcludePatterns = new List<string>(),
            };

            var generator = new MultiGemBindingGenerator(config, verbose: false);

            // Act: capture stdout since the summary is a Console.WriteLine,
            // not a return value - this is the same signal a human running
            // the tool at default verbosity would see.
            var originalOut = Console.Out;
            var capturedOut = new StringWriter();
            Console.SetOut(capturedOut);
            GenerationResult result;
            try
            {
                result = generator.GenerateAll(gems, sortedGems, projectPath);
            }
            finally
            {
                Console.SetOut(originalOut);
            }

            var output = capturedOut.ToString();

            // Assert
            result.ClassesGenerated.Should().Be(0);
            output.Should().Contain(
                "Skipped 2 classes: 1 had no bindable public members, 1 filtered by name",
                "a zero-bindings run must explain itself in one unconditional line, not just at --verbose");
        }
        finally
        {
            TestFixtures.CleanupTempDirectory(projectPath);
            if (Directory.Exists(tempDir))
            {
                TestFixtures.CleanupTempDirectory(tempDir);
            }
        }
    }
```

Note: this test parses real headers through libclang (same as `IntegrationTests`), so it depends on libclang being resolvable in the test environment exactly like the rest of the suite already does — no new test infrastructure is introduced.
