---

### Task 20b: BindingGenerator clang backend — prelude PCH/TU-reuse caching

**Files:**
- Create: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEPreludeCache.cs`
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEHeaderParser.cs:96-261` (the version produced by Task 20a)
- Modify: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Generation/MultiGemBindingGenerator.cs:192-193`
- Test: `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/O3DEPreludeCacheTests.cs` (new file)

This task builds directly on Task 20a — do Task 20a first. It is a larger, higher-risk change than 20a, and it is clang-backend-only (`--source clang`, opt-in; the default `--source reflection` backend is completely unaffected), so real-world user impact is limited to whichever gems/CI jobs explicitly opt into the clang backend.

- [ ] **Step 1: Confirm the current per-file reparse cost this eliminates**

After Task 20a, every `ParseHeaderFile` call still does a full `CXTranslationUnit.TryParse` that walks the entire `clangArgs` list — meaning libclang re-lexes and re-parses all ~25 `AzCorePreludeHeaders` (plus `climits`/`cstddef`/`cstdint`) for every single gem header, even though that prelude's parsed AST is byte-for-byte identical across every file in the gem (same `-I`/`-D`/`-include` args every time, per `ParseHeaders`). Sharing the `CXIndex` (Task 20a) is necessary for this but not sufficient — the actual expensive work (re-lexing/re-parsing the prelude's declarations) still happens per file because each call is a brand-new `CXTranslationUnit.TryParse` starting from nothing.

The real libclang mechanism for avoiding this is a precompiled header (PCH): parse the prelude once into a `.pch` file via `clang_saveTranslationUnit`, then pass `-include-pch <path>` on every subsequent per-file parse instead of the 25 `-include` prelude flags. This task builds that.

- [ ] **Step 2: Read BuildCache's hashing helpers to reuse instead of inventing new ones**

`Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Caching/BuildCache.cs` already exposes:
- `FileHasher.ComputeFileHash(string filePath)` — SHA-based hash of a single file's contents (used at `BuildCache.cs:200` and `:261`).
- `FileHasher.ComputeStringHash(string content)` — hash of an arbitrary string (used at `BuildCache.cs:293` to combine multiple file hashes into one).
- `BuildCache.ToolVersion` (static string, currently `"1.0.0"`) — bump this whenever generator output format changes; the PCH cache should NOT reuse this field (it gates the JSON binding-cache format, a different concern), but should follow the same "hash the inputs, compare, invalidate on mismatch" pattern `BuildCache.NeedsRegeneration` uses.

The PCH cache is a *different* cache from `BuildCache` (that one tracks gem-level "do we need to regenerate bindings at all" state in a JSON file; this one tracks "is the on-disk `.pch` for this gem's prelude still valid"), but it must reuse `FileHasher` rather than adding a second hashing implementation.

- [ ] **Step 3: Create O3DEPreludeCache.cs**

Create `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEPreludeCache.cs`:

```csharp
/*
 * Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
 * For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
 *
 * SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
 *
 */

using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.IO;
using System.Linq;
using ClangSharp;
using ClangSharp.Interop;
using O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Caching;

namespace O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Parsing
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Precompiles the shared AzCore prelude (the ~25 force-included
    /// headers every gem header parse depends on, see
    /// O3DEHeaderParser.AzCorePreludeHeaders) into a libclang PCH file
    /// once per gem/config, and reuses it across every header file in
    /// that gem via "-include-pch". Without this, ParseHeaderFile
    /// re-lexes and re-parses the entire prelude on every single header
    /// file - for a 200-header gem that's 200 redundant prelude parses.
    ///
    /// The PCH is invalidated (and rebuilt) whenever the prelude inputs
    /// change: the clang argument list (include paths, defines, target
    /// flags - anything that could change what the prelude headers
    /// expand to) or the content of the AzCore prelude header files
    /// themselves. Hashing reuses O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Caching.
    /// FileHasher, the same primitive BuildCache uses for its JSON
    /// binding-output cache, so there is exactly one hashing
    /// implementation in the tool.
    ///
    /// Clang-backend only (--source clang). The default --source
    /// reflection backend never touches this class.
    /// </summary>
    public sealed class O3DEPreludeCache : IDisposable
    {
        private readonly string _cacheDir;
        private readonly bool _verbose;
        private CXTranslationUnit? _preludeTU;
        private string? _pchPath;

        public O3DEPreludeCache(string cacheDir, bool verbose = false)
        {
            _cacheDir = cacheDir;
            _verbose = verbose;
            Directory.CreateDirectory(_cacheDir);
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Ensure a valid PCH exists on disk for the given gem + clang
        /// argument list + prelude header set, (re)building it if the
        /// cached one is missing or stale. Returns the absolute path to
        /// the .pch file to pass via "-include-pch".
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="index">Shared CXIndex for this gem (see O3DEHeaderParser.ParseHeaders).</param>
        /// <param name="gemName">Gem name, used to namespace the cache file.</param>
        /// <param name="preludeArgs">
        /// The clang args needed to parse the prelude itself: include
        /// paths, defines, standard/MSVC-compat flags, and the
        /// "-include climits" / "-include cstddef" / "-include cstdint"
        /// pre-includes. Must NOT include the AzCorePreludeHeaders
        /// "-include" flags themselves - those are compiled into the
        /// synthetic prelude.cpp source this method generates.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="preludeHeaderRelativePaths">
        /// The AzCorePreludeHeaders list (relative include paths like
        /// "AzCore/Math/Vector3.h") to bake into the PCH.
        /// </param>
        public string BuildOrReuse(
            CXIndex index,
            string gemName,
            string[] preludeArgs,
            IReadOnlyList<string> preludeHeaderRelativePaths)
        {
            var inputHash = ComputeInputHash(preludeArgs, preludeHeaderRelativePaths);
            var pchPath = Path.Combine(_cacheDir, $"{SanitizeFileName(gemName)}.{inputHash}.pch");

            if (File.Exists(pchPath))
            {
                Log($"[{gemName}] Reusing cached prelude PCH: {pchPath}");
                _pchPath = pchPath;
                return pchPath;
            }

            // Stale/missing - clean up any old PCH files for this gem
            // (different hash = different inputs) before rebuilding.
            foreach (var stale in Directory.GetFiles(_cacheDir, $"{SanitizeFileName(gemName)}.*.pch"))
            {
                try { File.Delete(stale); } catch { /* best-effort cleanup */ }
            }

            Log($"[{gemName}] Building prelude PCH: {pchPath}");
            BuildPch(index, preludeArgs, preludeHeaderRelativePaths, pchPath);
            _pchPath = pchPath;
            return pchPath;
        }

        private unsafe void BuildPch(
            CXIndex index,
            string[] preludeArgs,
            IReadOnlyList<string> preludeHeaderRelativePaths,
            string pchPath)
        {
            // Synthesize a tiny translation unit that #includes every
            // prelude header, then ask libclang to parse + save it as a
            // PCH. This mirrors exactly what O3DEHeaderParser.ParseHeaders
            // does today via repeated "-include" flags, but does the
            // parse work exactly once.
            var preludeSourcePath = Path.Combine(_cacheDir, "__prelude_source.h");
            var preludeSource = string.Join(
                Environment.NewLine,
                preludeHeaderRelativePaths.Select(h => $"#include \"{h.Replace('\\', '/')}\""));
            File.WriteAllText(preludeSourcePath, preludeSource);

            var unsavedFile = new CXUnsavedFile
            {
                Filename = (sbyte*)System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal.StringToHGlobalAnsi(preludeSourcePath),
                Contents = (sbyte*)System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal.StringToHGlobalAnsi(preludeSource),
                Length = (uint)preludeSource.Length
            };

            try
            {
                var translationUnitError = CXTranslationUnit.TryParse(
                    index,
                    preludeSourcePath,
                    preludeArgs,
                    new[] { unsavedFile },
                    CXTranslationUnit_Flags.CXTranslationUnit_ForSerialization |
                    CXTranslationUnit_Flags.CXTranslationUnit_SkipFunctionBodies,
                    out var preludeTU);

                if (translationUnitError != CXErrorCode.CXError_Success)
                {
                    Log($"Warning: Failed to parse prelude for PCH generation: {translationUnitError}. Falling back to per-file -include (no caching).");
                    return;
                }

                using (preludeTU)
                {
                    var saveError = preludeTU.Save(pchPath, CXSaveTranslationUnit_Flags.CXSaveTranslationUnit_None);
                    if (saveError != CXSaveError.CXSaveError_None)
                    {
                        Log($"Warning: Failed to save prelude PCH ({saveError}). Falling back to per-file -include (no caching).");
                        try { File.Delete(pchPath); } catch { /* best-effort */ }
                    }
                }
            }
            finally
            {
                System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal.FreeHGlobal((IntPtr)unsavedFile.Filename);
                System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal.FreeHGlobal((IntPtr)unsavedFile.Contents);
                try { File.Delete(preludeSourcePath); } catch { /* best-effort cleanup */ }
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Hash the clang arg list plus the CONTENT of every prelude
        /// header that actually resolves on disk (using FileHasher, the
        /// same primitive BuildCache.UpdateEntry uses). Invalidates the
        /// PCH when: an include path changes, a #define changes, or any
        /// AzCore prelude header's content changes - matching the
        /// invalidation semantics BuildCache already uses for the JSON
        /// binding-output cache.
        /// </summary>
        private string ComputeInputHash(string[] preludeArgs, IReadOnlyList<string> preludeHeaderRelativePaths)
        {
            var parts = new List<string> { string.Join("|", preludeArgs) };

            // Resolve each prelude header against the -I paths embedded in
            // preludeArgs (they show up as "-I<path>" entries) so we hash
            // actual file content, not just the relative name.
            var includeDirs = preludeArgs
                .Where(a => a.StartsWith("-I", StringComparison.Ordinal))
                .Select(a => a.Substring(2))
                .ToList();

            foreach (var relPath in preludeHeaderRelativePaths)
            {
                var resolved = includeDirs
                    .Select(dir => Path.Combine(dir, relPath))
                    .FirstOrDefault(File.Exists);

                parts.Add(resolved != null
                    ? $"{relPath}={FileHasher.ComputeFileHash(resolved)}"
                    : $"{relPath}=missing");
            }

            return FileHasher.ComputeStringHash(string.Join("\n", parts));
        }

        private static string SanitizeFileName(string name)
        {
            foreach (var c in Path.GetInvalidFileNameChars())
            {
                name = name.Replace(c, '_');
            }
            return name;
        }

        private void Log(string message)
        {
            if (_verbose)
            {
                Console.WriteLine($"[PreludeCache] {message}");
            }
        }

        public void Dispose()
        {
            _preludeTU?.Dispose();
        }
    }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Wire O3DEPreludeCache into ParseHeaders**

Modify `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEHeaderParser.cs`. First add a constructor parameter and field for the cache directory (the cache needs somewhere on disk to persist `.pch` files across separate generator invocations — this is what makes it a *cache* rather than a same-process-only optimization). Replace the constructor (lines 81–86 in the Task-20a version, unchanged from original):

```csharp
        public O3DEHeaderParser(bool requireExportAttribute = false, bool verbose = false)
        {
            _typeMapper = new TypeMapper();
            _verbose = verbose;
            _requireExportAttribute = requireExportAttribute;
        }
```

with:

```csharp
        private readonly string? _preludeCacheDir;

        public O3DEHeaderParser(bool requireExportAttribute = false, bool verbose = false, string? preludeCacheDir = null)
        {
            _typeMapper = new TypeMapper();
            _verbose = verbose;
            _requireExportAttribute = requireExportAttribute;
            // Opt-in: null means "no PCH caching", preserving the
            // Task-20a shared-CXIndex-only behavior for any caller that
            // doesn't pass a cache directory (e.g. ad-hoc/unit-test use).
            _preludeCacheDir = preludeCacheDir;
        }
```

Then, inside `ParseHeaders`, insert the PCH build/reuse step right after the shared `CXIndex` is created and right before the `foreach (var headerFile in headerFiles)` loop. Locate this block (from the Task 20a version of the file):

```csharp
            // Share one CXIndex across every header file in this gem
            // instead of creating/disposing a new one per file. A CXIndex
            // is just a libclang session handle - reusing it is the
            // standard clang_createIndex-once / clang_parseTranslationUnit-
            // many-times pattern, and it's a prerequisite for the PCH/
            // translation-unit reuse caching layered on top of this in
            // O3DEPreludeCache (see BuildOrReuse). Scoped to the gem (not
            // e.g. the whole multi-gem run) because each gem can have a
            // different include-path/define set, and CXIndex doesn't carry
            // per-parse state that would make cross-gem sharing meaningful.
            using var clangIndex = CXIndex.Create();

            foreach (var headerFile in headerFiles)
            {
```

Replace it with:

```csharp
            // Share one CXIndex across every header file in this gem
            // instead of creating/disposing a new one per file. A CXIndex
            // is just a libclang session handle - reusing it is the
            // standard clang_createIndex-once / clang_parseTranslationUnit-
            // many-times pattern, and it's a prerequisite for the PCH
            // reuse below.
            using var clangIndex = CXIndex.Create();

            // Precompile the shared AzCore prelude once per gem/config and
            // reuse it via "-include-pch" instead of re-lexing all ~25
            // AzCorePreludeHeaders on every single file. Opt-in via
            // _preludeCacheDir (set by MultiGemBindingGenerator when
            // --source clang is used); null means "skip caching, use the
            // original per-file -include list" - e.g. for direct
            // O3DEHeaderParser unit tests that don't set up a cache dir.
            var effectiveClangArgs = clangArgs;
            if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(_preludeCacheDir))
            {
                try
                {
                    using var preludeCache = new O3DEPreludeCache(_preludeCacheDir, _verbose);
                    // args WITHOUT the AzCorePreludeHeaders "-include" pairs -
                    // those get baked into the PCH instead. clangArgs at this
                    // point already has every "-include" pair appended in
                    // order: climits, cstddef, cstdint, then all of
                    // AzCorePreludeHeaders. We rebuild the "pre-prelude" arg
                    // list explicitly rather than string-splitting clangArgs,
                    // so the split point can't silently drift if the args
                    // above this method are reordered later.
                    var preludeOnlyArgs = args.ToArray(); // args = climits/cstddef/cstdint + flags, no AzCorePreludeHeaders yet
                    var pchPath = preludeCache.BuildOrReuse(clangIndex, gemName, preludeOnlyArgs, AzCorePreludeHeaders);

                    if (File.Exists(pchPath))
                    {
                        // Rebuild the per-file arg list: same as clangArgs
                        // minus the 2*25 "-include <header>" prelude pairs,
                        // plus "-include-pch <pchPath>".
                        var withoutPreludeIncludes = new List<string>(args) { "-include-pch", pchPath };
                        effectiveClangArgs = withoutPreludeIncludes.ToArray();
                    }
                    // else: BuildOrReuse logged a warning and left no file on
                    // disk (parse/save failure) - effectiveClangArgs stays as
                    // the original clangArgs with the full -include prelude
                    // list, so generation still succeeds, just without the
                    // speedup.
                }
                catch (Exception ex)
                {
                    Console.WriteLine($"  [{gemName}] Warning: Prelude PCH caching failed ({ex.Message}), falling back to per-file -include");
                    effectiveClangArgs = clangArgs;
                }
            }

            foreach (var headerFile in headerFiles)
            {
```

And update the `ParseHeaderFile` call inside that same loop to use `effectiveClangArgs` instead of `clangArgs`:

```csharp
                try
                {
                    ParseHeaderFile(headerFile, effectiveClangArgs, bindings, clangIndex);
                }
```

Important note on the `args` vs `clangArgs` split referenced above: in the Task-20a version of `ParseHeaders`, the local variable `args` (a `List<string>`) accumulates flags in this order: include paths, defines, standard C++ flags, MSVC-compat flags, `climits`/`cstddef`/`cstdint` `-include` pairs, and *then* the `AzCorePreludeHeaders` `-include` pairs are appended in the `foreach (var pre in AzCorePreludeHeaders)` loop — only afterward is `clangArgs = args.ToArray()` assigned. This means `args.ToArray()` captured **before** that `foreach (var pre in AzCorePreludeHeaders)` loop runs is exactly "every flag except the AzCore prelude includes" — which is precisely `preludeOnlyArgs`. To make this ordering explicit and not accidentally fragile, move the `preludeOnlyArgs` capture line so it sits literally between the `climits/cstddef/cstdint` block and the `foreach (var pre in AzCorePreludeHeaders)` loop, rather than re-deriving it later. Concretely, insert this one line immediately after:

```csharp
            args.Add("-include"); args.Add("climits");
            args.Add("-include"); args.Add("cstddef");
            args.Add("-include"); args.Add("cstdint");

            var preludeOnlyArgsSnapshot = args.ToArray(); // <-- ADD THIS LINE: captured before AzCorePreludeHeaders -include pairs are appended below

            foreach (var pre in AzCorePreludeHeaders)
            {
                args.Add("-include");
                args.Add(pre);
            }
```

and then use `preludeOnlyArgsSnapshot` (not a re-derived `args.ToArray()`) in the PCH-wiring block above — i.e. replace `var preludeOnlyArgs = args.ToArray();` with `var preludeOnlyArgs = preludeOnlyArgsSnapshot;`.

- [ ] **Step 5: Pass a cache directory from MultiGemBindingGenerator**

Read `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Generation/MultiGemBindingGenerator.cs:192-193`:

```csharp
            // Parse headers
            var parser = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute, _verbose);
            var bindings = parser.ParseHeaders(headerFiles, includePaths, defines, gem.GemName);
```

Replace with:

```csharp
            // Parse headers. Prelude PCH cache lives under the same
            // project-level cache root as BuildCache's JSON
            // (Global.CacheFilePath's directory), namespaced into its own
            // "PreludeCache" subfolder so .pch files don't collide with
            // the binding-output JSON cache file.
            var preludeCacheDir = Path.Combine(
                Path.GetDirectoryName(Path.Combine(projectPath, _config.Global.CacheFilePath)) ?? projectPath,
                "PreludeCache");
            var parser = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute, _verbose, preludeCacheDir);
            var bindings = parser.ParseHeaders(headerFiles, includePaths, defines, gem.GemName);
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Build verification**

```bash
"$LOCALAPPDATA/Microsoft/dotnet/dotnet.exe" build Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj -c Release --nologo
```

Expected: `Build succeeded.` If `CXTranslationUnit.Save` or `CXSaveTranslationUnit_Flags`/`CXSaveError` are not found by the compiler, check the installed `ClangSharp`/`ClangSharp.Interop` version in `O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj` (currently `ClangSharp 17.0.1` / `libClangSharp 17.0.4`) — these types are part of the standard libclang C API surface (`clang_saveTranslationUnit`) that ClangSharp 17.x exposes as `CXTranslationUnit.Save(string, CXSaveTranslationUnit_Flags)` returning `CXSaveError`; if the exact overload name differs, grep the installed package for the actual signature:

```bash
find ~/.nuget/packages/clangsharp -iname "CXTranslationUnit.cs" 2>/dev/null | xargs grep -n "Save" 2>/dev/null
```

and adjust the call in `O3DEPreludeCache.BuildPch` to match the real signature before proceeding.

- [ ] **Step 7: Byte-identical output regression test using a real fixture**

The test strategy here is: generate bindings for the same header set twice — once with the PCH cache disabled (empty/fresh cache dir forces a rebuild but still exercises the code path) and once by reusing a warm cache — and assert the generated `ParsedBindings` are equivalent, plus separately assert the PCH file is actually reused (not rebuilt) on the second call.

Create `Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/O3DEPreludeCacheTests.cs`:

```csharp
//
// Copyright (c) Contributors to the Open 3D Engine Project.
// For complete copyright and license terms please see the LICENSE at the root of this distribution.
//
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 OR MIT
//

using System.IO;
using System.Linq;
using O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Parsing;

namespace O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.Tests;

/// <summary>
/// Regression tests for the prelude PCH cache (O3DEPreludeCache) added to
/// speed up the clang backend (--source clang). Verifies (1) generated
/// bindings are identical whether or not the PCH cache is warm, and (2)
/// a warm cache is actually reused rather than rebuilt.
/// </summary>
public class O3DEPreludeCacheTests : IDisposable
{
    private readonly string _tempDir;
    private readonly string _cacheDir;

    public O3DEPreludeCacheTests()
    {
        _tempDir = TestFixtures.CreateTempDirectory();
        _cacheDir = Path.Combine(_tempDir, "PreludeCache");
    }

    public void Dispose()
    {
        TestFixtures.CleanupTempDirectory(_tempDir);
    }

    [Fact]
    public void ParseHeaders_WithPreludeCache_ProducesIdenticalBindingsToUncached()
    {
        // Arrange - one fixture header, parsed twice: once with no cache
        // dir (Task 20a behavior only) and once with the PCH cache dir set.
        var header = TestFixtures.CreateSampleHeader(_tempDir, "CachedParseClass");

        var uncachedParser = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute: false, verbose: false, preludeCacheDir: null);
        var uncachedBindings = uncachedParser.ParseHeaders(
            new List<string> { header }, new List<string> { _tempDir }, new List<string>(), "UncachedGem");

        var cachedParser = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute: false, verbose: false, preludeCacheDir: _cacheDir);
        var cachedBindings = cachedParser.ParseHeaders(
            new List<string> { header }, new List<string> { _tempDir }, new List<string>(), "CachedGem");

        // Assert - same class/method/property shape regardless of PCH caching.
        uncachedBindings.Classes.Should().HaveCount(cachedBindings.Classes.Count);

        var uncachedClass = uncachedBindings.Classes.Single(c => c.Name == "CachedParseClass");
        var cachedClass = cachedBindings.Classes.Single(c => c.Name == "CachedParseClass");

        cachedClass.Methods.Select(m => m.Name).OrderBy(n => n)
            .Should().Equal(uncachedClass.Methods.Select(m => m.Name).OrderBy(n => n));
        cachedClass.Properties.Select(p => p.Name).OrderBy(n => n)
            .Should().Equal(uncachedClass.Properties.Select(p => p.Name).OrderBy(n => n));
    }

    [Fact]
    public void ParseHeaders_SecondCallWithSameInputs_ReusesCachedPchInsteadOfRebuilding()
    {
        // Arrange
        var header = TestFixtures.CreateSampleHeader(_tempDir, "ReuseCheckClass");
        var parser1 = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute: false, verbose: false, preludeCacheDir: _cacheDir);

        // Act - first call builds the PCH.
        parser1.ParseHeaders(
            new List<string> { header }, new List<string> { _tempDir }, new List<string>(), "ReuseGem");

        Directory.Exists(_cacheDir).Should().BeTrue();
        var pchFilesAfterFirstRun = Directory.GetFiles(_cacheDir, "*.pch");
        pchFilesAfterFirstRun.Should().HaveCount(1, "the first parse should build exactly one PCH for the shared prelude");

        var firstPchWriteTime = File.GetLastWriteTimeUtc(pchFilesAfterFirstRun[0]);

        // Second call, same gem name + same inputs -> same hash -> BuildOrReuse
        // should find the existing file and skip rebuilding it.
        var parser2 = new O3DEHeaderParser(requireExportAttribute: false, verbose: false, preludeCacheDir: _cacheDir);
        parser2.ParseHeaders(
            new List<string> { header }, new List<string> { _tempDir }, new List<string>(), "ReuseGem");

        // Assert - still exactly one PCH file, and its write time did not change
        // (proves it was reused, not rebuilt).
        var pchFilesAfterSecondRun = Directory.GetFiles(_cacheDir, "*.pch");
        pchFilesAfterSecondRun.Should().HaveCount(1);
        File.GetLastWriteTimeUtc(pchFilesAfterSecondRun[0]).Should().Be(firstPchWriteTime);
    }
}
```

```

Expected: `Passed!` with `Passed: 2, Failed: 0, Skipped: 0`.

- [ ] **Step 10: Before/after timing comparison on a real multi-header fixture**

Use the repo's own O3DESharp gem headers (already present, no external checkout needed) as the "real multi-header gem" fixture, run through the actual CLI with `--source clang`, once against a clean (deleted) `PreludeCache` directory and once warm, and compare wall-clock time. This requires an O3DE engine checkout for full include-path resolution; if one is not available in this environment, run the comparison directly against the gem's own `Code/Include` headers, which is enough to exercise the multi-file-per-gem PCH reuse path even without full engine framework resolution succeeding for every symbol (existing per-file error handling already tolerates unresolved symbols and continues — see `catch (Exception ex)` in `ParseHeaders`'s per-file loop).

```bash
# Clean prelude cache to force a cold PCH build on the first run.
rm -rf F:/O3DESharp/PreludeCache

# Cold run: cache directory does not exist yet, first file pays the PCH build cost.
"$LOCALAPPDATA/Microsoft/dotnet/dotnet.exe" run --project Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj -c Release -- generate --project F:/O3DESharp --gems O3DESharp --source clang --verbose > /tmp_cold_run.log 2>&1
grep -E "Parsed .* classes|real|Generated" /tmp_cold_run.log

# Warm run: PreludeCache/*.pch now exists and should be reused for every file.
"$LOCALAPPDATA/Microsoft/dotnet/dotnet.exe" run --project Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj -c Release -- generate --project F:/O3DESharp --gems O3DESharp --source clang --verbose --force > /tmp_warm_run.log 2>&1
grep -E "Parsed .* classes|real|Generated" /tmp_warm_run.log
```

(`--force` forces regeneration past `BuildCache`'s JSON gate so the parse actually runs a second time against the warm PCH, rather than short-circuiting on "Up to date (cached)" — see `MultiGemBindingGenerator.GenerateGemBindings`'s `_buildCache.NeedsRegeneration` check.)

Expected: both runs report the same class/function/enum counts in their `Parsed N classes, ... in X.Xs` summary line (byte-identical binding *content*, confirming the PCH swap didn't change what gets discovered), and the warm run's total elapsed time is measurably lower than the cold run's for any gem with more than a handful of headers — record both numbers in the PR description for this task as the perf evidence. If the two runs' `Parsed N classes, N functions, N enums` counts differ, that is a correctness regression in this task and must be fixed before merging; do not proceed to Step 11 until they match exactly.

Additionally diff the actual generated output files byte-for-byte between the cold and warm run to confirm the codegen stage sees identical `ParsedBindings`, not just identical counts:

```bash
# Copy cold-run output aside, regenerate warm, diff.
cp -r F:/O3DESharp/Gems/O3DESharp/Assets/Scripts/Generated /tmp_cold_generated
"$LOCALAPPDATA/Microsoft/dotnet/dotnet.exe" run --project Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj -c Release -- generate --project F:/O3DESharp --gems O3DESharp --source clang --force
diff -rq /tmp_cold_generated F:/O3DESharp/Gems/O3DESharp/Assets/Scripts/Generated
```

Expected: `diff -rq` prints nothing (no output means no differences) — confirming byte-identical generated bindings between the cold (PCH-building) and warm (PCH-reusing) runs.

- [ ] **Step 11: Commit**

```bash
git add Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEHeaderParser.cs Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Parsing/O3DEPreludeCache.cs Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/Generation/MultiGemBindingGenerator.cs Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/O3DEPreludeCacheTests.cs
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Perf: cache precompiled AzCore prelude header per gem (clang backend)

Builds on the shared-CXIndex change: precompiles the ~25-header AzCore
prelude into a libclang PCH once per gem/config and reuses it via
-include-pch across every header file in that gem, instead of
re-lexing the whole prelude on every single file. The PCH cache lives
under <project>/PreludeCache and is invalidated by hashing the clang
arg list plus prelude header contents with the same FileHasher
BuildCache already uses for the JSON binding-output cache. Falls back
to the original per-file -include list on any parse/save failure.
Clang-backend only (--source clang, opt-in); reflection remains the
default backend and is unaffected.
EOF
)"
```

- [ ] **Step 1: README.md — add a "Which backend?" callout and fix `--source`-less examples in the binding generation section**

Current text (`README.md:554-583`):

```markdown
## C# Binding Generation Workflow

The canonical binding generator is a **C# tool that uses ClangSharp / libclang
to parse C++ headers directly** — it lives at
`Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/`. For each enabled
gem it emits `.g.cs` C# wrappers, an `InternalCalls.g.cs` interop stub, a
`BindingRegistration.g.cpp` Coral registration file, and a `metadata.json`
hot-reload manifest.

> **Note:** Earlier versions of this gem shipped a separate Python binding
> generator under `Editor/Scripts/` that consumed a BehaviorContext JSON dump.
> That generator is deprecated. The Python files under `Editor/Scripts/` that
> remain are thin orchestrators that shell out to the C# tool.

### Quick start

```powershell
# 1. Build the tool (first time only)
cd Gems/O3DESharp/Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator
dotnet build -c Release

# 2. Generate bindings for every enabled gem in your project
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project>

# 3. Generate bindings for specific gems only
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project> --gems PhysX,Atom

# 4. Force a full regeneration (skip the incremental cache)
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project> --verbose --force
```
```

Replace with:

```markdown
## C# Binding Generation Workflow

The binding generator (`Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/`)
has **two backends**, selected with `--source`:

> **Which backend should I use?**
> - **`--source reflection` (the default)** reads `reflection_data.json`,
>   a dump of O3DE's `BehaviorContext` produced by the editor at runtime —
>   the same public-API surface Lua / ScriptCanvas / Python already use.
>   No header parsing, no MSVC compatibility issues, no cross-gem include
>   walking. **This is the recommended backend for everything a C# script
>   would actually want to call.** Prerequisite: launch the O3DE Editor
>   for your project at least once first, so `AutoExportReflectionData`
>   writes out `reflection_data.json`; then pass its path explicitly with
>   `--reflection-data <path-to-reflection_data.json>` (the CLI's built-in
>   default search path is not guaranteed to match where your project's
>   editor build wrote the file — always pass `--reflection-data`
>   explicitly rather than relying on the default).
> - **`--source clang`** uses ClangSharp / libclang to parse C++ headers
>   directly, emitting `.g.cs` C# wrappers, an `InternalCalls.g.cs` interop
>   stub, a `BindingRegistration.g.cpp` Coral registration file, and a
>   `metadata.json` hot-reload manifest. It's heavier (fights MSVC
>   compatibility and cross-gem include paths) and can generate wrappers
>   that have no matching `BehaviorContext` dispatch path, which crash at
>   runtime if called. Use it only when you need a type a component
>   exposes in its header but hasn't reflected to `BehaviorContext`.

> **Note:** Earlier versions of this gem shipped a separate Python binding
> generator under `Editor/Scripts/` that consumed a BehaviorContext JSON dump.
> That generator is deprecated. The Python files under `Editor/Scripts/` that
> remain are thin orchestrators that shell out to the C# tool.

### Quick start

```powershell
# 1. Build the tool (first time only)
cd Gems/O3DESharp/Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator
dotnet build -c Release

# 2. Generate bindings for every enabled gem in your project (reflection
#    backend — launch the Editor once first to produce reflection_data.json)
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project> --source reflection --reflection-data <path-to-your-O3DE-project>/Generated/reflection_data.json

# 3. Generate bindings for specific gems only, using the ClangSharp header
#    parser instead
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project> --source clang --gems PhysX,Atom

# 4. Force a full regeneration (skip the incremental cache; --source clang only)
dotnet run -- generate --project <path-to-your-O3DE-project> --source clang --verbose --force
```
```

- [ ] **Step 7: Manual verification (review-only, no automated test)**

This task changes only markdown prose; there is no code path to unit test. Instead, a reviewer must manually confirm accuracy:

1. Open `README.md`, `GENERATED_BINDINGS_GUIDE.md`, and `SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md` in a Markdown preview (e.g. GitHub's PR diff view, or VS Code's built-in preview) and confirm all new callout blocks render correctly (blockquote nesting, code fences, table pipes are not broken).

   ```powershell
   cd Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator
   dotnet build -c Release
   dotnet run -c Release -- generate --project . --source reflection --reflection-data ./does-not-exist.json --verbose
   ```
   Expected: the tool prints `Reflection JSON: <full path>\does-not-exist.json` and then fails with a clear "file not found" style message (not a `System.CommandLine` "unrecognized option '--source'" or "unrecognized option '--reflection-data'" parsing error). A parsing error would mean the flag names in the docs are wrong; a "file not found" runtime message confirms the flags are real and the docs' syntax is correct.
   ```powershell
   dotnet run -c Release -- generate --project . --source clang --verbose
   ```
   Expected: the tool prints ClangSharp/header-parsing progress output (not a `--source` parsing error), confirming `--source clang` is accepted.
3. Confirm the `Guid` claim by re-reading `Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/Reflection/EBusHandlerRegistry.cs` lines 294-297 side-by-side with the new doc text — the reviewer should see `if (underlying == typeof(Guid))` handling a JSON string via `Guid.Parse`.
4. Confirm the menu-stub claim by re-reading `Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_bootstrap.py`'s `register_menus()` function (search for `def register_menus`) side-by-side with the new README wording — confirm it still only calls `general.log(...)` and never an ActionManager registration call. If a later change has made menu registration real, this doc edit must be revised again before merging.

- [ ] **Step 8: Commit**

```bash
git add README.md GENERATED_BINDINGS_GUIDE.md SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Docs: clarify reflection-vs-clang backend default, fix C# Project Manager naming, add Guid to EBus marshal coverage

README.md, GENERATED_BINDINGS_GUIDE.md, and SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md all
described the ClangSharp header-parser backend as canonical/primary and
showed example commands without --source, which silently run the
reflection backend (the tool's actual default per Program.cs's
--source option) instead of what the prose implied. Add a "Which
backend should I use?" callout to each doc's binding-generation section
and make every example command explicit about --source.

Also: README.md referred to a nonexistent "Tools > C# Script Manager"
menu — the dialog is actually titled "C# Project Manager"
(CSharpProjectManagerWindow in Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_tools.py),
and Editor/Scripts/csharp_editor_bootstrap.py's register_menus() is
currently a stub that only logs Python-console usage hints rather than
registering a real Tools menu entry, so the doc now describes opening
it via the Python console instead of a menu path that doesn't work
yet. Finally, add Guid (AZ::Uuid) to the EBus handler arg-marshaling
coverage list in README.md and SCRIPTING_GUIDE.md — EBusHandlerRegistry
already supports it but the docs' type lists omitted it.

Review-only: doc-only change, no automated test.
EOF
)"
```

### Task 23: Write RELEASE_NOTES.md v1.2.0 section

**Files:**
- Modify: `RELEASE_NOTES.md`

- [ ] **Step 1: Prepend a new v1.2.0 section above the existing v1.0.0 section**

Follow the exact section structure of the existing `# O3DESharp v1.0.0 — Release Notes` entry (Highlights / Bug fixes / Documentation / Tooling-CI / Known limitations / Upgrade notes). Populate it from the actual commits made across Tasks 0-21 of this plan (the engineer executing this task should look at `git log` between the v1.0.0 tag and HEAD on this release branch to enumerate exactly what landed, rather than copying this list blindly, since some items may have been deferred per Task 10/20's escape hatches). At minimum include:

- **Bug fixes:** the `Quaternion.LookRotation` conjugate-rotation fix (call this out prominently and as an "Upgrade notes" item too, since scripts using `LookRotation`/`LookAt` will now visibly rotate correctly rather than backwards - this is a behavior change, not just a bugfix, for anyone who'd compensated for the old bug), the `Vector3`/`Quaternion`/`Vector2` `Equals`/`GetHashCode` exact-equality change (also an upgrade note), the `Debug.Log*` format-string crash fix, the `Debugger.WaitForAttach(TimeSpan.Zero)` semantics fix (upgrade note: default `WaitForAttach()` call now returns immediately instead of blocking forever), the `NativeReflection` fail-fast fix, the "Clear Selection" script-picker fix, the `ValidateScriptClass` wiring fix.
- **Performance:** the `GenericDispatcher` hot-path allocation removal, the `Entity.GetChildren()` O(n²)→O(n) fix, the `StackAllocator` arena fix, the `ForwardEventToManaged` type-caching fix, and - if it landed (see Task 10's escape hatch) - the `CoralHostManager` ALC separation.
- **Editor UX:** the C# Project Manager build-freeze fix (call this out as the headline editor UX improvement).
- **Onboarding:** the BindingGenerator net8.0→net9.0 retarget.
- **Tooling:** the binding generator's config-diagnostics, determinism, and - if it landed - CXIndex/PCH caching improvements.
- **Documentation:** the backend-default doc correction across three files.
- **Known limitations:** carry forward anything still true from the v1.0.0 section, and add the `GenericDispatcher` BehaviorContext-dispatch perf issue explicitly deferred to the 1.3 BehaviorContext refactor (reference `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-01-1.2.0-ux-perf-audit-design.md` for context).
- **Acknowledgements:** match the existing section's format.

Write the actual prose - do not leave this as a bullet outline in the file; the outline above is instruction for the engineer writing this task, not the final release-notes text itself.

- [ ] **Step 2: Commit**

```bash
git add RELEASE_NOTES.md
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
Release notes: v1.2.0
EOF
)"
```

### Task 24: Tag, merge to main, and push (requires explicit maintainer confirmation)

**Files:** none (git operations only)

- [ ] **Step 1: Run the full verification pass**

Before proceeding, confirm every task above is complete and its tests pass:
- `dotnet test Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core.Tests/O3DE.Core.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo`
- `dotnet test Code/Tools/BindingGenerator.Tests/BindingGenerator.Tests.csproj -c Release --nologo`
- `dotnet build Code/Tools/BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator/O3DESharp.BindingGenerator.csproj -c Release --nologo`
- `dotnet build Assets/Scripts/O3DE.Core/O3DE.Core.csproj -c Release --nologo`
- Native build of the gem (via the O3DE engine's build system - use whatever command the maintainer normally uses; this plan doesn't assume a standalone CMake invocation works outside a full O3DE engine checkout).
- Python: `pytest Editor/Tests/` if any tests were added/modified by Tasks 11-13.
- Manual verification checklist from Task 10 (CoralHostManager), if that item landed.
Expected: everything green. If anything fails, stop and fix before proceeding - do not tag a broken state.

- [ ] **Step 2: STOP - confirm with the maintainer before any of the remaining steps**

This is the point where hard-to-reverse, shared-state actions begin (tagging, merging to `main`, pushing to `origin`). Per the approved spec's release mechanics, get an explicit go-ahead here even though "full release" was pre-approved as the end goal - do not run steps 3-5 without that confirmation in this session.

- [ ] **Step 3: Tag the release**

```bash
git tag -a v1.2.0 -m "O3DESharp v1.2.0"
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Merge development into main**

```bash
git checkout main
git merge --ff-only development
```

If `--ff-only` fails (main has diverged), stop and ask the maintainer how they want to reconcile rather than force-merging or rebasing unilaterally.

- [ ] **Step 5: Push**

```bash
git push origin main
git push origin v1.2.0
```

Confirm with the maintainer once more immediately before this specific step if any time has passed since Step 2's confirmation, since push is the one truly irreversible action in this task.
